#156 The original text reads "desire," emended to "joy" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#157 The original text reads "hexagram," emended to "hang" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#158 The original text reads "sorrow," emended to "black" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#159 The original text reads "obtain," emended to "virtue" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#160 The original text reads "walk," emended to "have" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#161 "Observe" appears in the original text, while the *Baizi Quanshu* edition reads "irrigate."
#162 The original text reads "moreover," emended to "daily" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#163 The original text reads "wood," emended to "not yet" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.

#164 The original text reads "Dao," emended to "retreat" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#165 "Term" appears in the original text, while the *Baizi Quanshu* edition reads "encounter."
#166 "Summon" appears in the original text, while the *Baizi Quanshu* edition reads "term."
#167 The original text reads "its," emended to "together" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#168 The original text reads "already," emended to "self" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#169 The original text reads "nurture," emended to "nurture" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#170 "Call back young Shu; upon arrival, obtain" appears in the original text, while the *Baizi Quanshu* edition reads "upon arrival, obtain; young Shu calls in response."
#171 The original text reads "already," emended to "reed" according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#172 The original text omits "free from illness and harm" after "peace," now supplemented according to the *Baizi Quanshu* edition.
#173 "Weary" appears in the original text, while the *Baizi Quanshu* edition reads "exposed."

*Yilin*, *Upper Canon*, Scroll Two
Hexagram Six: *Contention*

*Yilin*, *Upper Canon*, Scroll Two
Hexagram Six: *Contention*

*Contention*:
Crafty words breed deceit, soon to revert to primal substance.
The dead lie thick as hemp, blood flows to float the catalpa.
All know their mother, none recognize their father—
only when weapons cease do they rest.

*Qian*:
King Wen’s four teats, kindness deep and sincere.
He raised ten sons, none met an early end.

*Kun*:
The sun sets, the carriage awaits—
yet the son’s home remains unseen.
The eldest daughter lacks resolve,
her left hand scratches her head.

*Zhun*:
Bound, I ascend Mount Tai,
and there address Lord Yao:
“Plead my grievance,
lift this sorrow and distress.”

*Meng*:
The celestial writing brush flows swift,
passing Horn and Chamber Mansions.
Proclaim the time, spread harmony—
nothing remains obstructed.

*Xu*:
Tugging the beard, pulling the whiskers,
though fearful, no cause for dread.
The Queen Mother offers prayers—
misfortune fails to take shape.

*Shi*:
Finding water, they plunge in,
delighted, they preen and peck.
Feathers gleam with luster,
fit to carve jade.
The duke departs, never to return—
the Wu clan shelters the guest.

*Bi*:
Water rushes downward,
bound for the Eastern Sea.
Seeking what I possess,
they barter for silk and carp.

*Xiaoxu*:
Deer and river deer follow the herdsman,
secure and sated in their abode.
Returning to the lodging,
lest illness be the cause.

*Zhun* correlating to *Bi*.

**Lǚ**:
The tree beam stands at dawn’s hall,
unable to stir at all.
Royal affairs unceasing,
autumn’s harvest left ungleaned.

**Tài**:
West of the Weak Waters,
dwells the Queen Mother of the West.
Born without knowing age,
she abides with Heaven’s grace.
The traveler meets peril,
but dwelling in goodness brings joy.

**Pǐ**:
Fortunes exhausted, vast and desolate,
besieged within the calendar’s chamber.
Fortunate to ascend the jade hall,
feasting as Yao’s companion.

**Tóngrén**:
The youth grasps the unicorn,
spring and autumn yield to yin.
The supreme sage nears his end—
Confucius’ heart grieves.

**Dàyǒu**:
Yin, father of Boqi,
father and son torn apart.
Guiltless yet condemned,
by the long tongue’s deceit.

**Qiān**:
The planted tree’s branch snaps,
severing mother from child.
The nine marshes’ cries unheeded,
cut off, unknown to each other.

**Yù**:
Shifting peril, no resistance,
battling the magpie.
Wings broken, eyes blinded,
wounded by the turtledove.
Returning to the wild hut,
mother and child support each other.

**Suí**:
Jia, Yi, Bing, Ding,
all return to my court.
Three fools, six sons,
enter the gate to see their mother.

**Gǔ**:
Mulberry and catalpa ravaged by borers,
clothes tattered like nets.
The women’s work undone,
silk and hemp turned to jade.

**Lín**:
Unlock the prison, fling wide the gates,
the royal tour redresses wrongs.
Xia Terrace, Beautiful Within—
King Wen of Shang rejoices.

**Guān**:
Virtue of reverence and clarity,
seated before jade viands.
Surely safeguarding the excellent,
long receiving peace and fortune.

**Shìkè**:
The martial *kuai* oversees the minister,
many mouths contend in litigation.
Metal and fire at the door,
the people find no rest.
The year is lean, nothing remains.

**Bēn**:
Nine-tiered purple palace,
majesty resides within.
Yellow Emperor, Yao, and Shun,
walking in utmost impartiality.
Crowns and robes draped,
the realm rests in tranquility.

**Bō**:
Bearing the ox up the mountain,
striving with waning strength.
Fierce wind, rain, and snow
bar my path ahead.
Turning back midway,
the anxious grow daily glad.

**Fù**:
The lame hare with cleft lip,
walking brings tooth-chill.
Mouth pained, speechless,
a malady born of the body.

**Wúwàng**:
Bodies joined, wings paired,
joyful union in harmony.
With you I share goodwill,
bringing me fortune.

**Dàxù**:
Fretting, unable to escape,
worry wells from the heart.
My treasure lost,
my concubine displaced.

**Yí**:
Two hearts diverge,
one follows west, one east.
Bright discourse all day,
none aligns with me.

**Dàguò**:
Laughter and cheerful speech,
feasting with joy.
Long revelry, cups passed round,
dancing through a thousand autumns,
bowing to receive great fortune.

**Kǎn**:
First sorrow, then delight,
trading with fortune.
Eight rows arrayed in formation,
feasting with all friends.
*As in Kūn’s* **Xiǎoguò**.

**Lí**:
Moving west without a home,
shattering new affairs.
The noble scion loses advantage—
better to stay put.

**Xián**:
The phoenix perches to the left,
the qilin stands to the right.
Sage and worthy meet,
Yi and Lü gather.
No misfortune befalls the time—
fortune is my mother.

**Héng**:
From the frontier of Kangju,
longing for virtue, he enters court.
Fearful as dew at dawn,
three cups exhaust grace—
then returns to his old hut.
*As in* **Tóngrén**’s **Lí**.

**Dùn**:
The sick and poor hope for favor,
sending the elder to trade.
Hawking goods in the marketplace,
opening the pen to choose a sheep—
joy in receiving heavenly auspice.

**Dàzhuàng**:
Dwelling high without harm,
though perilous, not lost.
Holding pearls and jade,
he returns to his homeland.

**Jìn**:
The right hand discards wine,
the left gathers bounty.
On the road, he meets ritual propriety,
fed by virtue from a jade cup.

**Míngyí**:
Raising tigers, herding wolves,
they turn to wound themselves.
Great courage, small gains—
though perilous, not lost.

**Jiārén**:
Crowned with Yao, supporting Yu,
with Master Red Pine and Pengzu.
In the west, encountering the Queen Mother,
the road is smooth and level—
none dare oppose them.
*As in* **Sǔn**’s **Lí**, *and* **Shī**’s **Lí**.

**Kuí**:
Autumn and winter, probing the nest,
the magpie’s chicks are not found.
The chariot points northward,
briefly detaining my young concubine.

**Jiǎn**:
Two paper slips, three sheep,
all come to my homeland.
Lingering amidst many hardships,
their provisions are diminished.

**Xiè**:
Southward migration without shelter,
the crow breaks its own nest.
Felling trees, longing for closeness—
movement brings no advantage.

**Sǔn**:
Disputes unending,
pulling and striking one another.
Zhang Ji’s weak tongue,
hair unbound, flees northward.

**Yì**:
Craning the neck for wine,
it does not enter my mouth.
First joy, then denial—
profit gained, then lost.
*As in* **Lǚ**’s **Cuì**.

**Guài**:
Hair unbound, rushing headlong,
bandits pursue from behind.
Sword and spear lost,
the body remains unharmed.

**Gòu**:
Where unicorn and phoenix roam,
peace and joy without care.
The noble tends the people,
a thousand autumns through the ages.

**Cuì**:
Tattered clothes, fording the river,
the water deep—pray cease.
Fortunate to meet the boatman,
crossing safely without mishap.

**Shēng**:
Debts unpaid, vexation arises.
Grief wells from within.
My golden jar is lost—
unexpectedly, the position slips away.

**Kùn**:
Fleeing not far,
heart and words at odds.
Confucius wanders astray—
the old sprouts yet to bloom.

**Jǐng**:
Great strength, fat and proud,
bestowing favor on all my uncles.
Harmony within and without,
no fear of hunger or thirst.

**Gé**:
The Yellow Emperor establishes the era,
cultivated virtue in his person.
Blessings like spring’s warmth,
enfeoffed as Lord of Lu.

**Dǐng**:
Tigers gather, sharpening fangs,
waiting for the pig’s pen.
To go is certain harm—
better to stay and abide.
*Or*: Sharpening their talents,
awaiting the great hunt.
To go is certain ruin,
fierce defeat leaving no remnant—
profit lies in stillness.

**Zhèn**:
Heaven and Earth paired in offering,
standing in radiant position.
Yin and Yang in proper order,
their work accomplished—
the world at peace.
*As in* **Méng**’s **Xiǎo Xù**.

**Gèn**:
The ape falls from the tall tree,
yet hands and feet remain unscathed.
Preserving my gold and jade,
I return to my chamber.
*As in* **Méng**’s **Lǚ**.

**Jiàn**:
The Purple Palace, firm and unassailable.
The enlightened spirit, virtue perfected—
the lord receives great fortune.

**Guī Mèi**:
The lone old man, the widowed woman,
sleeping alone in sorrow.
Eyes wide, ears ringing,
no one to share laughter or speech.
*As in* **Guī Mèi**’s **Lǚ**.

**Fēng**:
Head bowed, stealing glances,
fearing discovery.
The traveler does not arrive,
the wine sours, the fish spoils—
none relish the feast.

**Lǚ**:
Carrying gold to trade dogs,
profit flees, abandoning me.
Hidden in the depths of the abyss,
regret turns to fault.

**Xùn**:
Violating great taboos,
conspiring with the Lord of Fate.
Seized, bound, and beaten,
shackled by the officials—
the worried find joy.
*Same as* **Bō**.

**Duì**:
Holding jade in delight,
the knot at the waist undone.
From danger to safety,
I am kept from harm.

**Huàn**:
The loom in turmoil,
women’s work undone.
The elder sister betrothed,
yet lacks even a short jacket.
Hearing of misfortune averted,
the ominous fades away.

**Jié**:
A man of metal, a giant of iron,
fire burns on either side.
Though fearful, not terrified—
alone, he remains whole.

**Zhōng Fú**:
Grateful, bowing in thanks,
bound for the land of Hao.
Dancing and leaping in joy,
freely receiving blessings.

**Xiǎo Guò**:
The black ox with white throat,
calls me back to the fields.
Beneath Mount Li,
I may till abundantly.
The year’s joyful seasons,
the people at peace in their labors.

**Jì Jì**:
White pheasants flock and cry,
admiring virtue, they come to court.
The grace of *Zhan Lu*—
I am made to fear.

**Wèi Jì**:
Fleeing calamity east and west,
one reenters the gate of misfortune.
Chaff and husks insufficient—
my heart is weighed with sorrow.

---

**Shī** (The Seventh: *The Army*)

**Shī**:
The crow calls to its young,
feeding them wine and dried meat.
From the high tower’s perch,
the child returns to its mother.
The miser’s success—
a bountiful year, yet the wife bears no son.

**Qián**:
One reed pipe.
Two tongues, flattery’s words—
three deceits make a tiger,
even the mother casts aside her shuttle.

**Kūn**:
Spring peaches blossom,
the youngest daughter marries well.
Receiving abundant blessings,
within the army, good fortune—
the man becomes lord of the state.

**Zhūn**:
Different kinds, divergent paths,
hearts that do not long for one another.
The cow and boar—
none have a home.

**Méng**:
Folding leaves to blind the eyes,
the younger uncle unseen.
The three-legged lone crow,
reaching its end.

**Xū**:
The sparrow seeks grain in the east,
mistakenly enters the snare’s domain.
Fortunate to meet a noble man,
escaping to return and rest.

**Sòng**:
The king’s grandson, Ji Zi,
together they are filial and kind.
Bright, trustworthy, and sincere,
promoted and recommended—
a pillar of the state.

**Bǐ**:
Carving wood, no branches,
parting from you.
Hunger and cold, nothing to eat—
standing alone, mourning.

**Xiǎo Xù**:
Shun ascends, Great Yu,
in the wilds of Shi Yi.
Journeying to the royal court,
appointed to govern the waters and lands.

**Lǚ**:
Righteousness overcome by desire,
self-serving in pursuit.
Seeing profit, seeking favor—
destroying the lord’s good name.

**Tài**:
Three men journey north,
six positions radiant.
Meeting a fair maiden,
she bears me a fine son.

**Pǐ**:
Yi draws the *Wu Hao* bow,
shooting the Celestial Wolf.
The pillar of the state, fierce and brave,
dies in battle at Rongyang.

**Tóng Rén**:
Ji Ji hesitates,
tying her sash, awaiting the hour.
From dawn till dusk,
the hundred carriages do not come.

**Dà Yǒu**:
The wild geese in flight,
weary from toil.
Plague and pestilence afflict the people,
widows and widowers grieve.

**Qiān**:
Piercing the chest, the dog of the state,
stiff and scattered, pounded beside.
Heaven and Earth’s order overturned,
sun and moon begin anew.

**Yù**:
On the northern mountain, jujubes—
Uncle Shu lives long.
On the eastern ridge, many chestnuts—
fit for trade in the market.

**Lù Liáng**:
Male and female beasts rampant,
wherever they go, profit and joy.

**Dùn**:
Dry reeds for banners, flags planted beyond the suburbs.
Though there be precious pearls,
no path to bring them near.

**Gǔ**:
Pure and deep, the abyss blocked,
slandered by false words.
Interrogated and pleaded,
struck at the root’s warmth.
Under the sweet pear tree, judgments heard—
content, they receive grace.

**Lín**:
Black and yellow vipers hiss,
travelers weary and spent.
Conscripted laborers gaunt,
jade-like, yet home they come not.

**Guān**:
Virtue of keen and swift,
roused to action, forgetting food.
Capturing leopards and seizing Yue,
for the king they seek fortune,
to perfect the lord’s virtue.

**Shì Kè**:
Gathering dodder in Mei’s village,
enticing me to Mulberry Center.
Breaking faith, failing the tryst—
grief girds my waist with sorrow.

**Bēn**:
Bo Ning’s blessed son,
brings grace to our state.
Removing harsh cruelty,
he spares the youngest from harm.

**Bō**:
Slanderous fathers, flattering villains,
cast cities and states into chaos.
Parted from filial devotion,
defeat and distress bring no blessing.

**Fù**:
Deep springs and embankments,
waterways open and flowing.
Pouring into lakes and seas,
the state grows rich and full.

**Wú Wàng**:
South of the Jiang, locusts swarm,
stinging my hands and feet.
Entangled in grievance, bent and wronged—
pain pierces heart and belly.

**Dà Xù**:
Three men journey together,
parting to lodge alone.
One body, five hearts—
tossed in confusion, lost,
chaos yields nothing.

**Yí**:
The oriole cries in the courtyard,
warning of disaster and ill.
Double gates bolted, bars struck—
prepared for uninvited guests.

**Dà Guò**:
Tasks completed, affairs settled,
hands clasped in ease.
Establishing virtue with words,
seated, they regulate tribute.

**Kǎn**:
The state in turmoil, unrest,
war and weapons bring calamity.
They plunder my wife and children,
hunger and cold fill the home.

**Lí**:
Bearing Yao, supporting Yu,
following Pengzu and Qiao.
Westward they meet the Queen Mother—
the road smooth and level,
none dare oppose them.

**Xián**:
Long-tailed, sinuous,
drawing rivers on the earth,
too deep to ford.
Utterly beyond compare—
sorrowful, sighing in longing.

**Héng**:
Riding dragons, following the *xiān*,
journeying to the northern gate.
There they see the Hall of Audience,
appointed to guard Shu City.
Pacifying the common folk,
the whole household receives fortune.

**Dùn**:
Above, linked to the mountains,
a lifetime without harm.
Heaven and Earth lofty and bright,
ten thousand years of enduring peace.

**Dà Zhuàng**:
Long drought, waters dried,
withered and parched, no moisture.
Vainly cultivating virtue—
nothing yet gained.

**Jìn**:
Leaning on mountains, relying on earth,
peril and danger kept at bay.
Above, clarity descends;
below, brilliance rises—
receiving great fortune,
the lord reaps its benefit.

**Míng Yí**:
Fire rages, unyielding—
choking, they collapse.
Burning my robes, scorching my flesh—
regret comes too late.

**Jiā Rén**:
Matched in union, welcoming,
profit in the four directions.
Joy and delight spread—
their words find favor.

**Kuí**:
The pure man, noble son,
long detained in the wilds.
Wandering, he returns not—
longing for my kind mother.

**Jiǎn**:
Armories and military storehouses,
where weapons and armor gather.
Not a village or town—
no place to rest.

**Jiě**:
The king’s virtue harmonizes the five elements,
qi aligns with the four seasons.
Yin and yang follow their order—
the state knows no calamity or disaster.

**Sǔn**:
Shedding robes and feathers,
they fly into the great capital.
The gatekeeper stands guard in warning—
Zheng Hū loses his home.

**Yì**:
Severing roots, burning stumps,
flesh does not regrow.
Sickness lies in the heart and belly—
day by day, withering away.

**Guài**:
On Wenshan’s peaks, purple mushrooms;
on Yong and Liang’s slopes, crimson grasses.
Born of harmonious qi,
fortune and blessings arrive.

**Gòu**:
Overloaded, heavily burdened,
cast aside in the wilds.
A small task for a great weight—
only self-exertion and toil.

**Cuì**:
Bright geese cry *ya-ya*,
making their home upon the waters.
Male and female in harmony,
hearts filled with joy and delight—
their desires fulfilled.

**Shēng**:
Ears deaf, eyes blind,
words fail to reach.
Standing in sorrow, weeping—
nothing comes to fruition.

**Kùn**:
The Celestial Palace arrays the stars,
the five spirits dwell within.
Palace gates stand firm—
the lord rests secure in his abode.

**Jǐng**:
Fan Li’s rare talent,
first humiliated, his flesh wounded.
Later, he becomes minister of state—
enfeoffed as Marquis of Ying.

**Gé**:
Searching nests in autumn and winter,
no magpie chicks are found.
Pointing northward, they depart—
briefly, they leave me bereft.

**Dǐng**:
Confucius feared in Kuang,
besieged in Chen and Cai.
Yet his virtue remained unshaken—
he escaped peril in the end.

**Zhèn**:
The swan flies over land,
the duke departs, never to return.
Zhong Shi bears the burden alone,
while Bo Shi lodges as a guest.

**Gèn**:
The crane calls in the marsh,
retreating to seclusion.
Embracing simplicity, guarding truth—
he never follows the crowd.

**Jiàn**:
Shun ascends, Great Yu arises,
in the wilds of Shiyi.
They journey to the royal court—
appointed to govern the waters and soil.

*(Parallels: Qián’s Zhōng Fú, Shī’s Xiǎo Xù.)*

**Guī Mèi**:
Left and right, they assist—
gold and jade fill the coffers.
Ever full, never depleted,
wealth abounds like a granary’s store.

*(Identical to Méng’s Kūn’s final four lines.)*

**Fēng**:
Mount Cui towers in the northern peaks,
a noble guest of the celestial spirits.
Robes and caps never cease—
beneath the mantle of grace.

**Lǚ**:
Empty vats and poured dregs—
the pure and greedy never reach.
Drawing the bow, eyeing the hen—
the male pheasant takes flight.

**Xùn**:
The Hu, Man, Rong, and Di,
gathered in the great yin.
Frozen ice, bitter cold—
the noble man does not endure.

**Duì**:
Sweet dew, sweet springs,
the mechanisms of great peace.
Virtue’s resonance—
years of joy, the people at rest.

*(Parallel: Zhūn’s Qiān.)*

**Huàn**:
E Lai calls out to Bo,
disturbing the guests beyond.

**Zhōngshǒu**:
Guard the quiet dwelling,
prepared for misfortune’s mark.
Though *Lín* brings sorrow’s break,
though destroyed, no harm remains.

**Jié**:
Sun and moon gaze upon each other,
radiant and flourishing in splendor.
Three sages’ flourishing deeds—
virtue’s power greatly exalted.
*(Parallel: Méng’s Qiān, Pǐ’s Bì.)*

**Zhōngfú**:
Creeping vines choke the thorns,
blossoms bear no fruit.
Slander and flattery disrupt governance,
blocking the flow of grace.

**Xiǎoguò**:
Neighbors turn from me,
gazing toward the jade maiden.
My body riddled with sores—
who would wed such a one?

**Jìjì**:
Where sincerity resides,
the spirits lend their aid.
Virtue’s teaching upheld—
through ages it endures.
Three sages join in this,
receiving boundless blessings.

**Wèijì**:
Drilling wood to spark a flame,
digging earth to seek the spring.
The mistress hungers, thirsts—
her child brings fortune to her heart.

---

**Bǐ (Eighth)**:
**Bǐ**:
The deer finds sweet grass,
calling to its companions.
The nine clans live in harmony,
free from hunger’s fear.
*(Parallel: Tóngrén’s Qì, Yì’s Héng.)*

**Qián**:
Restoring the ancestral line,
reviving the ways of Chéng and Kāng.
Light shines upon the myriad lands,
enduring through the ages.

**Kūn**:
Unicorn’s young, phoenix’s chicks,
born in a land of grace.
Where harmonious qi dwells,
peace and joy abound—
the realm teems with wise ones.

**Zhūn**:
A sparkling spring on the peak,
fishing for carp in the heights.
No fish to be caught,
the fire refuses to burn.
*(Parallel: Xiǎochù’s Zhūn.)*

**Méng**:
Péngshēng becomes a boar,
the white tiger brings calamity.
Thieves steal Yáo’s robes,
Jié wields his weapon.
The azure bird lights the night—
three days, the land is wounded.

**Xū**:
Millet and sweet wine,
offered in reverence to the mountain’s spirit.
The gods delight in the feast,
sweet rains descend in blessing.
The people flourish,
singular in their fortune—
no disasters befall them.

**Sòng**:
Plum blossoms bear fruit again,
wild geese nest in clusters.
Wisdom’s first sprouts—
the land is shaded in fortune.
*(Parallel: Xù’s Lí, Yù’s Xiǎoguò.)*

**Shī**:
The ruins of a thousand years,
ravaged by great armies.
Zǐdū unseen,
the city lies empty, no homes remain.

**Xiǎochù**:
The lord’s son, the king’s grandson,
holds the sling and gathers the pellets.
Each shot finds its mark,
the household overflows with plenty.

**Lǚ**:
Lí Jī’s slanderous schemes,
conspiring with the two concubines.
Plotting the prince’s death,
murdering the loyal and filial.
Shēnshēng hangs himself,
Chóng’ěr flees in exile.

**Tài**:
Life without end,
descendants number a thousand million.
The catalpa pillar bears the beam,
firm and unshaken.

**Pǐ**:
Lost in sorrow, burdened with care,
like a caged beast in confinement.
A child lost, a mate gone—
the village offers only borrowed shelter.
*(Parallel: Tóngrén’s benevolence and wisdom lie hidden,
the qilin cannot be found.
Dragons and serpents retreat in concealment,
the hall stands empty.)*

**Dàyǒu**:
Knots tied in intricate measure,
tangled beyond unraveling.
The toad’s mother seeks a match—
her schemes bring ruin upon herself.

**Qiān**:
The bird falls from the tree,
its head and feet unharmed.
Preserving its wings,
it returns to its nest.

**Yù**:
Chén Wǔ and Jìng Zhòng,
their omens rise in Qí’s land.
They journey to Yíngqiū—
eight generations flourish.
*(Parallel: Gòu’s Shī, Zhūn’s Shìkè.)*

**Suí**:
Missing the hour of return,
male and female grieve in sorrow.
Wandering in foreign lands,
separated from their mother.

**Gǔ**:
Qí and Lǔ dispute in words,
battling at Lóngmén.
Grudges breed misfortune,
three generations know no peace.
*(Parallel: Kūn’s Lí, Tóngrén’s Kuí, Qiān’s Xián.)*

**Lín**:
The treasury’s wealth,
the king uses to relieve the needy.
Fishing in rivers and seas,
the greedy reap their fill.
*(Parallel: Sǔn’s Kuí, Tóngrén’s Yì.)*

**Guān**:
The crane cries and flies north,
descending to the rice fields.
Perch, sturgeon, alligator, carp—
abundant in their numbers.
One cast yields two—
profit doubles in gain.

**Shìkè**:
Cāngwú and Yùlín,
the roads are smooth and passable.
Ivory and tortoiseshell,
precious southern gold—
these bring me honor in return.

**Bì**:
Two fires vie in brightness,
though they clash, no harm is done.
Parting yet enduring,
my brothers remain whole.

**Bō**:
Bóyí and Shūqí,
paragons of integrity.
With virtue they ward off peril—
no misfortune lingers.
*(Parallel: Tài’s Qián.)*

**Fù**:
The season departs, I turn east,
my hair tangled like bramble.
Wandering the empty grove,
my heart filled with sorrow.
*(Alternate: Bì’s lines.)*

**Wúwàng**:
A hundred legs move as one,
strength in mutual support.
Three sages assist the throne—
the royal house shines in favor.

**Dàxù**:
Dams and barriers,
water cannot flow.
Fire blazes in yang’s light,
yin’s creatures hide in retreat,
returning to their native ground.

**Yí**:
The snake rides the dragon,
years of hunger and withering.
Famine strikes the land—
the people eat the bitter herbs.

**Dàguò**:
A leaden blade carves jade,
firmness resists its edge.
Exhausting my strength,
the silkworm’s cocoon brings affliction.
*(Parallel: Kūn’s Yù.)*

**Kǎn**:
By Heng Mountain’s shore, the waves swell high—
the lofty city stands intact.
Yin’s qi does not drip,
the floodwaters find no place to rest,
and the captive opens his gate.

**Lí**:
Paired eyes, four wings,
they come to settle my land.
Blessings and goodness ascend the hall,
dwelling with me in the same grove.
*(Parallel: Sǔn’s Suí, Tóngrén’s Duì.)*

**Xián**:
Mouth sealed, tongue knotted,
the heart stifled and pent.
Disaster and woe arise—
nowhere to voice the grievance.
*(Parallel: Pǐ’s Xùn, Pǐ’s Jǐng.)*

**Dàn**:
Dragging its tail, it will not advance,
defying principle, losing its minister.
Hui and Shuo flee in haste.

**Dùn**:
Early frost, late snow,
harming the wheat and grain.
Labor undone, strength squandered,
hunger leaves nothing to eat.
*(Parallel: Xū’s Xián.)*

**Dàzhuàng**:
Bound for the frontier, missing the appointed time,
trouble arises from despair,
fear stirring up sorrow.
Storehouses open and close,
the state sinks into dire distress.

**Jìn**:
Vast Heaven, bright sun,
shining upon my land.
The people thrive in joy,
all relying on blessed fortune.

**Míngyí**:
Supremely auspicious, without blame,
secure and free from peril.

**Jiārén**:
Duke Yi, shallow and foolish,
would not heed counsel.
Without aid, he lost his state,
fallen to the Di’s ravages.

**Kuí**:
A crow perches on the city wall,
crying, “Break the house!”
It calls forth poison and venom,
bringing calamity to the land.

**Jiǎn**:
Long legs delight in running,
striding a thousand li.
Wang Liang rejoices,
Bo Le is on the road.
Shen Sheng sees his mother—
below, there is Youzi.

**Xiè**:
Plowing the stone-crowned peak,
sowing seed in poverty.
Futile toil, empty labor—
no sprouts rise from the earth.

**Sǔn**:
Two men take different paths,
one east, one west.
A journey of a thousand li—
they know not where the other goes.

**Yì**:
Dressed in pure white robes,
bearing the lord, they rise.
Virtue and rightness flourish,
the world turns to benevolence.

**Guài**:
A blade of jade, head of iron,
the granaries stand empty.
The market swells with profit,
yet profit becomes a foe.

**Gòu**:
Ascending Kunlun,
entering Heaven’s gate.
Passing the wine-mound,
lodging by Jade Spring.
Opening the gate of kindness,
beholding the benevolent lord.

**Cuì**:
The round white sun
is devoured by the moon.
The high is diminished, the low destroyed—
Zheng Zhao flees into exile.

**Shēng**:
Granaries overflow with grain,
fit for planting millet and sorghum.
The year is abundant, the harvest ripe,
the nation grows rich.
*(Parallel: Qián’s Shī, Kūn’s Héng.)*

**Kùn**:
Tigers and wolves conspire,
gathering to form a stronghold,
craving to devour
oxen and sheep.
The road is cut off—
my merchants are harmed.

**Jǐng**:
Midlife broken and bent,
ever fearing survival.
Yet in old age, fortune and blessing arrive,
glory and honor lend their aid.

**Gé**:
Riding together in the same carriage,
parting midway.
I lose my stalwart companion,
left alone in sorrow.
*(Parallel: Suí’s Bǐ.)*

**Dǐng**:
Drinking wine, drunk and raging,
leaping and quarreling.
Elder injured, younger felled—
the family prepares for mourning.

**Zhèn**:
Stepping into misfortune,
encountering five red-headed men,
they leap and jeer, offering no aid.
Leaning on a staff, I listen in submission,
daring not stir.

**Gèn**:
Wolves and tigers vie in strength,
rites and right abandoned.
They devour the land whole—
Qi and Lu are left without a king.
*(Parallel: Xiǎochù’s Suí.)*

**Jiàn**:
The youngest son of the southern state,
his bearing fair and fine.
He seeks my eldest daughter,
but she is scorned and denied.
Instead, he receives the ugly—
too late for regret.
*(Parallel: Tài’s Zhèn.)*

**Guīmèi**:
One body, two heads,
no passage through the trunk.
It cannot see my heart—
chaos beyond remedy.

**Fēng**:
Li Er, the magpie’s cry,
meets with dread and sorrow.
It gnaws at my belly,
unable to lift the bar.

**Lǚ**:
Paulownia, cassia, and cedar beams,
strengthened by mutual support.
Entering to spread the five grains,
the royal house enjoys peace.

**Xùn**:
Sparrows forage for food,
returning at dusk to call their young.
Back in their nest,
all is calm as before.

**Duì**:
Four tails, six heads,
a portent of misfortune.
Yin does not serve yang—
the ruler loses his light.

**Huàn**:
A single journey, three passes,
the knot tied awry.
Forked roads diverge—
at dusk, no arrival.

**Jié**:
Teeth sprout from gums,
the hall’s doors swing open.
The secluded one finds advantage in constancy,
beating wings to take flight.

**Zhōngfú**:
Spring swans fly east,
trading horses for gold.
Tenfold profit gained,
heavily laden, they return home.

**Xiǎoguò**:
Joy and delight,
children and grandchildren together.
Holding firm, enduring—
no misfortune or blame.

**Jìjì**:
Spirit wanes, form decays,
gnashing and stumbling,
withered, rotten, and worm-eaten.

**Wèijì**:
Ascending the high mountain,
I speak before the king.
Pleading my grievance,
I receive office and favor.

**Xiǎochù (Chapter Nine)**:
**Xiǎochù**:
A white crow holds the bait,
the swan calls to its young.
Spreading its wings,
it comes to follow its mother.
Elders and juniors,
all raise their hands in celebration.

**Qián**:
Eastward, encountering tigers and snakes,
oxen and horses bolt in terror.
The road is cut off—
the merchant’s work fails.

**Kūn**:
Zi Niu captures the qilin,
the multitude of scholars inaugurate an era.
Heroes vie for fame,
the capital teems with wanderers.

**Zhūn**:
Scorching fire at the spring’s source,
fishing from the mountain’s peak.
No fish to be caught,
the fire refuses to burn.
*(Parallel: Bǐ’s Zhūn.)*

**Méng**:
The mechanism jams,
words cannot be spoken.
Sincerity unheard—
another’s grievance is borne.

**Xū**:
The old house, the former hut,
now crumbling and decayed.
Better the new nest,
where joy and peace may dwell.

**Sòng**:
A small snake follows the stream,
seeking the great fish.
Yu Ju casts the net—
the kitchen master sings of the hinge.

**Shī**:
Carving through mountains to open the road,
southward to the land of Jiā.
The prayers of the Duke of Zhou—
Xiāng’s judgment divides Chǔ.

**Bǐ**:
The magpie’s feet recoil,
head and eyes unseen.
Long worn by exhaustion,
it cannot recover.

**Lǚ**:
Five tongues peck like magpies,
each with its own words.
Foreign lands, strange customs—
the heart grows bewildered,
its desires unmet.

**Tài**:
The gates of heaven swing wide,
the prison’s doors lie open.
Bonds undone, fetters loosed—
captivity released.

**Pǐ**:
Hard ice, yellow crows,
wailing in sorrow.
Flocks of startled gulls—
their cries drift as my woe.

**Tóng Rén**:
Sun runs, moon strides,
each to a different abode.
The resolute wife turns her gaze—
the lord loses his home.

**Dà Yǒu**:
Golden fangs, iron teeth,
the Queen Mother’s child.
No calamity befalls—
at the roadside inn,
parting comes soon.

**Qiān**:
*"How faint, how faint!"*
Woes and misfortunes entwine.
Barred by towering peaks,
households scatter.

**Yù**:
The spirits gather,
conferring in counsel.
The southern land, oppressed and chaotic—
its people toil in suffering.
An army rises to conquer,
a worthy lord is enthroned.

**Suí**:
Tigers and wolves vie for prey,
courtesy and yielding fail.
One devours the land whole—
Qí and Jìn left masterless.
*(Parallel: Bǐ’s Gèn.)*

**Gǔ**:
A rootless parasite,
passing like floating clouds.
The foundation unsteady,
it falls in an instant,
becoming but a withered tree.

**Lín**:
The child wails for food,
the mother goes to seek it.
Returning to an empty nest—
Zǐyì sighs long.

**Guān**:
Four steeds chase the fox,
wheels snag on brambles.
The chariot leaves no track—
the lord’s son gains nothing.

**Shì Kè**:
Square beak, broad mouth—
benevolence, wisdom, sagacity, depth.
Releasing the inverted and suspended,
the land of Táng finds great peace.

**Bì**:
Riding fortune, borne by joy,
bound for the land of Jiā.
Bearing blessings southward,
settling in a peaceful home.

**Bō**:
Kǒng Lǐ, the elder fish,
north to Gāonú.
Wooden horse, golden carriage—
driving to the great capital.
The Queen Mother sees me off,
a mare awaits her foal.

**Fù**:
Three-legged, headless,
it knows not where to go.
The heart wild, the spirit wounded—
let none call it wise.
The sun’s light unseen.

**Wú Wàng**:
The swift mare’s body,
daily crossing three thousand *lǐ*.
South to Cāngwú,
wedded to fortune.
The road smooth and easy—
safe, without peril.

**Dà Xù**:
At the celestial station Jiànglóu,
the king sets forth on his tour.
Broad blessings, bestowed favors—
the land at peace, without care,
awaiting the season’s end in vain.

**Yí**:
The carriage does not come,
the prince flees in pursuit.
The horse’s bit wounds its mouth—
nearness lost, constancy gone.
When will it return?

**Dà Guò**:
Beans fill the central plains,
waiting for the lame to eat.
Feasting with friends,
great desires are fulfilled.

**Kǎn**:
Wine strained through tangled reeds,
the spirit-medium bows in prayer.
The gods refuse their assent—
exhaustion and sorrow remain.

**Lí**:
The plum tree bears fruit again,
the swan’s eggs descend and gather.
Benevolence and wisdom rise—
the state is shaded in fortune.
*(Parallel: Bǐ’s Sòng, Yù’s Xiǎo Guò.)*

**Xián**:
The plain rises from the foothills,
walking along the mountain’s base.
No violent harm befalls—
the people dwell in peace.

**Héng**:
Guests enter the gate,
rushing east and west.
The maiden does not weave,
the scholar abandons the fields.
Bones lie exposed for a thousand *li*—
the year is lean, the people suffer.

**Dùn**:
What Heaven bestows,
fortune and blessings remain constant,
no fear of peril’s onset.

**Dà Zhuàng**:
Locusts devour our rice,
driven away, they will not leave.
The ears bear no grain—
only hollow stalks remain.

**Jìn**:
Ox and steed share the hall,
the Guo clan perishes.
The state lies broken and empty—
the lord flees in flight.

**Míng Yí**:
The dog lacks forefeet,
plotting rebellion in the north.
Self-inflicted ruin—
how can one find rest?

**Jiā Rén**:
Two wheels turn on their own,
ascending the southern slope.
Four horses share the yoke,
no burden too heavy—
laughing with Yu in ease.

**Kuí**:
Shoots and sprouts flourish,
yang thrives abroad.
Left and right grasp the keys—
the lord speaks of bestowing rank.

**Jiǎn**:
Winter blooms, autumn buds,
repeatedly struck by harsh frost.
Armor and weapons fill the court—
all things cease to grow.
A male fire blazes at night—
the people are thrown into great alarm.

**Xiè**:
Frost descends, doors are shut,
creeping things hide away.
Sun and moon unseen—
one dwells among the dead.
*(Parallel: Kūn’s Xū.)*

**Sǔn**:
Bearing the self a hundred *li*,
merit extends to the four seas.
Civil arts lay the foundation,
martial strength erects the pillar of heaven.

**Yì**:
Yu forges the divine tripod,
Bo Yi receives the command.
Axes and hatchets stored high,
a banner stands in solitary vigil.
Goods set out for sale find no buyers—
solemn and distressed, they bring harm.

**Guài**:
Fortune’s blessings gather,
joy arrives, sorrow departs.
Like fish meeting water,
enduring bliss finds shelter.

**Gòu**:
The Azure Dragon hides in concealment,
the qilin and phoenix flee afar.
Bandits and thieves dwell together—
no peace, no rest.

**Cuì**:
A white crane bears a pearl,
feeding by night, awaiting dawn.
Cherishing the Hu’s virtuous renown,
the self receives glory and honor.

**Shēng**:
Born at dawn, dead by dusk—
named the babe-ghost,
unfit for sacrifice.

**Kùn**:
Journeys remain unfinished,
new tasks arise again.
Ji and Jiang toil in weariness—
no peace, no rest.

**Jǐng**:
Worries and troubles dissolve,
joy arrives, blessings come.
Sitting or standing, one listens in awe—
neighbor to delight.
*(Parallel: Méng’s Xián.)*

**Gé**:
The morning wind soars heavenward,
rising in great flight toward warmth.
Passing blindly through my town,
Yi finds nothing to seize.

**Dǐng**:
Planting millet in the low field,
fragrant blossoms brush the teeth.
Great rains pour down—
three sevens, four floods—
lush abundance fills the jars.
*(Pouring down: one version reads "forest-gathered.")*

**Zhèn**:
Birds shelter in lush groves,
the noble one toils without cease.
Heart glad, wishes fulfilled—
all who see reap their harvest.

**Gèn**:
Arm broken, foot stunted,
unable to offer wine.
Sacrifices neglected,
the spirits grow angry, displeased.

**Jiàn**:
Studying the numinous for three years,
benevolent, sagely, and divine.
Wisdom perceives auspicious signs—
joy, fortune, and felicity.
The turtledove flies in,
announcing my freedom from care.
*(One version: The deer calls, the swan soars—
the cry heralds auspicious signs.)*

**Guī Mèi**:
Three wives share a single decision,
hearts estranged, thoughts unaligned.
Resentment lingers in the breast—
ever sorrowful, ever grieving.

**Fēng**:
Millet stands tall in the central field,
offered to the Queen Mother.
Blessings received by the thousand myriad—
all desires grandly fulfilled.

**Lǚ**:
The yang fire knows no sorrow,
the second plowing brings joy.
Fortune descends, blessings arrive—
for me, the zither is strummed,
songs and odes herald delight.

**Xùn**:
The yang brightness does not cease,
yet the lord lacks grace and virtue.
The Elder loses advantage,
the people forfeit their strength.

**Duì**:
Swallows and sparrows bear reeds,
hatching and nurturing their young.
Six brothers,
bound in harmony and filial piety.
Each attains their wish—
joyful, content in one another.
*(Parallel: Suí’s Cuì.)*

**Huàn**:
The quail’s tail flees in haste,
fire rages in the Xū army.
Hao Shu takes flight,
the lower ranks lose their lord.

**Jié**:
Two men stand apart,
unwilling to share a dwelling.
The resolute wife scatters,
the Lord of Wei loses his home.

**Zhōng Fú**:
The drought demon wreaks havoc,
wind scatters the clouds.
Seeking to halt, it cannot—
it returns to its own abode.

**Xiǎo Guò**:
Though the maiden be fair,
she is matched to my lord.
Young Jiang stands at the gate—
the noble one rejoices in delight.

**Jì Jì**:
The loving mother and her red child
feast and receive lands.
The Yi and Di submit in surrender—
the royal house finds peace.

**Wèi Jì**:
The three-legged fox howls,
the spirit wails, the supervisor stumbles.
Reflecting on transgressions, punishing evil—
it destroys its own household.

**Lǚ (Hexagram 10)**:
**Lǚ**:
Ten birds take flight together,
Yi shoots nine hens.
The lone male survives alone—
though startled, unharmed.

**Qián**:
Facing east, the hedge stands firm,
laughing words exchanged.
Zi Ban wields the whip,
musicians perform in joy.

**Kūn**:
Following the river, poling the boat,
sailing beside the Huai’s flow.
The fisherman casts his net—
first to catch the great □.

**Zhūn**:
The shaft snaps, the wheel shatters,
the horse □ lies fallen.
The rear guard loses its lodging,
the right foot stumbles and stumbles.

**Méng**:
Two companions together,
yet at odds, in conflict.
Hearts divided, discordant—
strife and contention rage fiercely.

**Xū**:
The Purple Palace of the Northern Asterism,
robes and caps dwell within.
Embracing harmony, establishing virtue—
ever receiving heaven’s favor.
*(Parallel: Xū’s Guài, Kūn’s Guān.)*

**Sòng**:
Dwelling by Stone Gate,
blessings and fortune remain secure.
Receiving favor from the western neighbor,
returning to drink from Jade Spring.
*(Parallel: Xū’s Jì Jì.)*

**Shī**:
The sheep’s gut winds ninefold,
pushing forward in unison.
Only the king’s grandson may halt—
only he may ascend to heaven.

**Bǐ**:
Contention and strife multiply,
harmony finds no place.
Yin and yang both obstructed—
the Valley Wind, mother and child.

**Xiǎo Xù**:
Guo Shu’s jaw locked shut,
ensnared by thorns.
A child’s face, a double chin—
disaster fails to strike,
returning to his homeland.

**Tài**:
Scorpions in the chamber, wasps at the door,
stinging my hands and feet.
Unable to advance or halt—
they bring me harm and misfortune.
*(Parallel: Zhūn’s Míng Yí.)*

**Pǐ**:
Anger not of one’s own will,
shifting with circumstance.
Coveting the rotten rat,
calling to the shrike and kite.
Self-made loss of bait—
overturned, beset by trouble.

**Tóng Rén**:
The infant seeks the breast,
the mother denies her own child—
the yellow fawn rejoices.

**Dà Yǒu**:
Needles and carvings labor in vain,
brocade and embroidery fail to form.
The hawk pursues pheasant and hare—
its talons break, nothing gained.

**Qiān**:
Rain and floods descend,
rivers and canals blocked.
Qi and Lu sealed off—
markets emptied, fortunes spent.

**Yù**:
The giant boar digs channels,
water and floods fill the empty valley.
Guests halt at the inn—
mud reaches their bellies,
no millet or grain to be found.

**Suí**:
Three traitors stir chaos,
Jie and Zhi as allies.
Above and below in turmoil—
the Way of Heaven severed.

**Gǔ**:
Qi Jing, bewildered and doubtful,
plays the child’s ox.
Lineage unclear,
treacherous sprouts bring calamity.

**Lín**:
Three sheep lost together,
fleeing southward.
Meeting at dusk, their tracks vanish—
none know where they hide.

**Guān**:
Seeking a lord to trade,
in the wilds of Mount Tai.
Traversing perilous paths,
yet no danger befalls—
profit like poured wine.

**Shì Kè**:
The mulberry’s leaves yellow, soon to fall,
stripped of their golden hue.

**Shī Shì**:
Losing power, tilting askew—
nowhere to stand.

**Bēn**:
Climbing mountains to seek fish,
entering water to hunt hares.
The market is not their home,
yet they linger long of their own will.

**Bō**:
Names made, virtues achieved,
yet the nape of the neck remains untested.
Duke Jing grows old,
Confucius departs.

**Pǐ’s Zhūn**.

**Fù**:
The hidden corners of Heaven,
where Yao and Shun dwelled.
Here one may preserve the self,
safeguard our state and land.

**Wú Wàng**:
Crossing rivers to die for fame,
abandoning rites to slay the body.
Failing to follow the Dao,
Chengzi flees to Yan.

**Yī** (variant of *Yí*).

**Dà Xù**:
Two men contend,
neither can settle.
Hearts at odds, minds apart—
litigation arises, bringing misfortune.

**Yí**:
The osprey and the fair maiden,
sage and worthy paired as mates.
A harmonious home receives blessings,
good fortune enduring and long.

**Dà Guò** (variant of *Wú Wàng*):
Leaping into the river to seek oranges,
instead finding a great chestnut.
Boiling lamb, roasting meat,
drinking wine, singing, laughing.

**Kǎn**:
Mountains steep and hard to traverse,
ravines filled with stones.
The cart races, wheels striking—
heavy loads snap the axle.
Burdened, one stumbles,
right foot twisted and sprained.

**Qián’s Qiān**.

**Lí**:
Utterly blessed, profoundly fortunate,
cherished by the spirits.
Joy without sorrow,
attaining every desire.

**Xián**:
Crows and magpies eat grain,
gaping beaks receive their feed.
Nurtured by kindness, growing to maturity,
gentle, yielding, and upright—
ruler and minister in harmony.

**Héng**:
Mists gather in layers,
droplets converge.
Essence flows downward,
torrents surge and pour.

**Chí**:
The road bristles with thorns,
thistles pierce my feet.
Ill-suited for travelers,
poisoning the heart.

**Sǔn** hexagram identical.

**Dà Zhuàng**:
Vipers gather in search of shelter,
hard to dwell among.
Their venomous stings bring agony,
incurable.

**Jìn**:
Unicorn and phoenix follow,
observing safety and peril.
The sage of the eastern state,
Hou Ji and the Duke of Zhou.
Favorable for settling,
long free from disaster and misfortune.

**Míng Yí**:
Jie’s chaos, untimely,
stirs the people’s resentment and sorrow.
The six blessings bark—
the lord in peril, the minister shamed.

**Jiā Rén**:
Born of the Yellow Emperor,
within Fuxi’s domain.
No blades reach here,
favorable for dwelling.

**Kuí**:
Sparrows forage for grain,
returning at dusk to call their young.
Back to their nests they go,
safe and sound as before.

**Bǐ** (variant of *Xùn*).

**Jiǎn**:
The Grand Granary stores grain,
the land abounds in food.
Yin and yang in harmony,
years and seasons yield their bounty.

**Xiè**:
Banners and flags flutter,
standards raised in the wilds.
Though pearls lie within reach,
no path leads to them.

**Shī’s Suí**, **Yù’s Zhōng Fú**.

**Sǔn**:
Treading peril, stepping on air,
plunging into the spring abyss.
Lame, unable to advance,
feet crippled, unsteady.

**Yì**:
Taking orders, mounting the chariot,
reconciling two houses.
Fair brows and gleaming teeth—
the two states remain unharmed.

**Guài**:
Auspicious day, chariots advance,
hunting and fowling yield game.
King Xuan drinks wine,
descending to proclaim great merit.

**Nì**:
Gold and silk, precious treasures,
fit for our market exchange.
Marriage brings favor,
gains more than double.

**Cuì**:
Craning necks for wine,
yet none enters our mouths.
Reveling in solitude,
wounds heal, profits vanish.

**Sōng’s Yì**.

**Shēng**:
Appointed governor of Dai,
feasting and bestowing sweet gifts.
Gaining the favor of warriors,
scholars in accord—
a great victory over the Hu,
the state and capital secure.

**Kùn**:
The sun rises from Warm Valley,
shining upon ten thousand lands.
The noble and bright,
paired with Yu and Xia.

**Jǐng**:
Chasing hares, seeking crows,
breaking my bow and cart.
Dusk falls, too late—
losing advantage, missing the hour.

**Zhūn** (variant of *Cuì*).

**Gé**:
False words, reckless speech,
attendants mislead.
Losing the way to the left,
returning home yet not knowing the door.

**Dǐng**:
Treading on a tiger’s tail,
diminishing my authority.
The noble loses his chariot,
departing his state.

**Zhèn**:
Roots unsteady,
new blossoms fall away.
Now a lone widow,
unable to see one another.

**Gèn**:
Five yokes, four linchpins,
abundance and plenty.
Offering strength in rank,
Zou and Yu rejoice.

**Jiàn**:
The Yellow Emperor’s purple clouds,
sage and divine.
Radiant omens appear,
proclaiming no misfortune.

**Guī Mèi**:
Five blessings, four fortunes,
all tilling the high fields.
Millet and rice flourish,
harvesting herbs and grain.

**Fēng**:
Tigers enter the town,
seeking meat.
The great one guards,
the lord does not lose his state.

**Lǚ**:
Crow chicks and magpie fledglings,
ever with their mother.
Yearning for the flock,
yet not rearing their own young.

**Xùn**:
A lame donkey, unfit,
a fine steed missing its hour.
Sinews strained, strength spent,
weary upon the dunes.

**Duì**:
Black-maned, dark-faced,
bound for the lofty village.
The vermilion bird guides,
the sacred tortoise bears the offering.
Reaching Heaven’s Gate,
meeting my true lord—
man and horse unharmed.

**Huàn**:
Probing the nest, finding fledglings,
turtledoves and magpies arrive together,
bringing me joy.

**Jié**:
Securing the high, fitting for office,
nine promotions in a day.
Rising swiftly above ranks,
shepherding Changshan.

**Zhōng Fú**:
Large head, bright eyes,
bearing great fortune.
Three sparrows fly in,
meeting their due reward.

**Xiǎo Guò**:
Gazing a thousand *li*,
yet not seeing Master Mo.
Louluo’s sharp sight,
turned toward the petty man.

**Jì Jì**:
Three women conspire,
turning their backs to part at night.
Laughing with the Earl,
unable to bear the Queen Mother.
The sweet wine lost—
who bears the blame?

**Lí’s Sòng**.

**Wèi Jì**:
The stars align poorly,
strong and weak clash.
One hen, two cocks—
guests overcome the host.

**Tai’s Eleventh**

**Tai**:
Seeking in the state of Chen,
lingering in bound domains.
Awaiting our lord’s grandson,
he returns in the fourth month.
The lord possesses virtue,
receiving grace and fortune.

**Qian**:
Boyi and Shuqi,
teachers of integrity and purity.
With virtue they ward off calamity,
no sorrow or misfortune remains.
*See Bi’s Bo.*

**Kun**:
The ford is deep and hard to cross,
soaking my robes and sash.
Five sons excel in promotion,
free from other mishaps.
*Variant: "robes" for "sash."*

**Zhun**:
Leaning to gaze afar,
the path to me opens wide.
Driving forth in haste,
paired fish share the bed.

**Meng**:
Vines and brambles choke the thorns,
flowers bear no fruit.
Slanderers hold power,
blocking kindness and grace.
*See Shi’s Zhongfu.*

**Xu**:
Four stallions without horns,
the nobleman’s mount.
Marching south to report,
sharing virtue with fortune.

**Song**:
Ankles and heels wounded,
the big toe stricken with palsy.
Losing one’s company, delayed in time,
profit flees and does not return.
*See Lü’s lower line, Meng’s loss.*

**Shi**:
Spring’s city, summer’s land,
a realm of long life.
Here one may consume and preserve,
safeguarding home and state.

**Bi**:
Gazing for the swift steed, it does not come,
bound and lame, I grieve.
Rain startles my heart,
wind stirs my hunger.

**Xiaoxu**:
Long a guest without merit,
I long to return to my homeland.
Thunder and rain overflow,
the road remains impassable.

**Lü**:
A square boat prepared for water,
fires lit along the riverbank.
Accumulating good brings signs—
a life without disaster.
Heaven’s blessing, good fortune,
eternal peace and well-being.
*See Dayou’s Qian.*

**Pi**:
The land-crab gazes at its mother,
endless toil without cease.
Royal governance decays,
no one can be preserved.
*See Tongren.*

**Tongren**:
Heavily laden, bearing weight,
discarded in the wild.
The Queen Mother parts from her child,
grieving and toiling in sorrow.
*See Shi’s Gou.*

**Dayou**:
Born where the earth nurses,
the Supreme Emperor rejoices greatly.
Bestowing upon me blessings,
lifespan unbounded,
honored in the decree’s making.

**Qian**:
Gathering in haste, stumbling,
falling from the mountain’s peak.
My good name extinguished,
lost forever, never to return.
*See Pi’s Li.*

**Yu**:
The eastern neighbor marries off her daughter,
becoming the king’s consort.
Duke Zhuang builds a hall
to honor the Queen Mother.
Returning to the capital,
Ji Jiang rejoices.

**Sui**:
Bo Hu and Zhong Xiong,
their virtue and righteousness deep and vast.
They spread the Five Teachings,
yin and yang in proper order.
*See Kun’s Gou, Yi’s Zhun.*

**Gu**:
Swift and nimble,
like an ape ascending the tree.
Though the bow is well-tuned,
in the end, nothing is gained.

**Lin**:
Raising sleeves to cover the eyes,
unable to see sun or moon.
Fur robes and rush mats,
dwelling in the chamber of eternal night.
*See Kun’s Sui.*

**Guan**:
Enduring shame, lacking modesty,
no face, yet a head remains.
Wasting and diminishing,
daily dwindling away.

**Shike**:
Solid yin, frozen and blocked,
perpetual ice, never warm.

Causing men to fall into indolence,
great hail brings disaster.
You feel you have prospered smoothly from youth to age.

Lightning and fire spread wildly.

**Bi**:
Summer wheat withers, its awns struck by frost.
The cruel lord ruins the state,
causing me to die young in sorrow.

**Bo**:
The abyss dries, the dragon grieves,
Jizi becomes a slave.
Ganshu meets his end,
the Yin house collapses.

**Fu**:
The lame and the halt follow one another,
at dusk the ox tires.
The rear guard lags behind,
losing advantage and the female.

**Wu Wang**:
The mulberry is about to shed,
its yellow leaves fall.
Losing power, toppling over,
as if without a place to stand.

**Da Xu**:
Longevity comes in its season,
roots flourish and grow.
Yin and yang harmonize,
the year is joyful, free from care.

**Yi**:
The maiden has no chamber,
no match has been made.
Yin and yang are not in harmony,
sitting alone, sleeping solitary.

**Da Guo**:
Spring decrees pardon,
benevolent virtue is not universal.
The Three Sages act as one,
the Zhou state flourishes and rises.

**Kan**:
Metal’s essence leaps in fury,
a sword is worn past noon.
Two tigers face each other,
though startled, no fault comes.

**Li**:
Sitting in peril until dusk,
plans yield no success.
Sweet rain does not fall,
governance turns harsh, the people grow fierce.

**Xian**:
The old poplar wanes with the days,
its branches withered and dry.
Rank and title do not advance,
each day declines, crumbling away.
*(Leads to Meng’s Song.)*

**Heng**:
The Marquis of Cai journeys to Chu,
lingering by rivers and lakes.
Days stretch into months,
longing for his lord behind him.

**Dun**:
Right hand rests on the sword at the waist,
left hand grips the hooked belt.
Fierce disputes never cease,
clashing in strife,
losing profit in the marketplace.

**Da Zhuang**:
Water flows downward,
rushing far to the Eastern Sea.
Seeking what I possess,
one buys sturgeon but obtains carp.
*(Leads to Song’s Bi.)*

**Jin**:
Ascending the stool, mounting the carriage,
driving a team of four southward.
Alliances unite, rivalries scatter,
Yan and Qin grow strong.

**Ming Yi**:
Seeking a hare but gaining a river deer,
beyond all expectation.
Joyfully welcomed,
high rank brings injury.
*(Variant: "with one...")*

**Jia Ren**:
Missing the time to return,
the road is distant and bewildering.
The traveler’s heart grieves,
leaving me to wander in hesitation.

**Kui**:
A soul alone, without a chamber,
lodging in a borrowed dwelling, eating borrowed food.
Bandits rise, the people scatter,
facing the enemy, the inner strength is lost.

**Jian**:
Dwelling like a rolling pellet,
peril offers no peace.
East and west unsettled,
every movement breeds distress.

**Xie**:
The earth’s profound thickness bears all,
the myriad things flourish and multiply.
Level, peaceful, upright, and just,
it brings a hundred blessings to rest.

**Sun**:
A worn-out thorny bramble,
bearing worthy shoots to halt insult.
All foes despise it—
who would welcome it?
Above and below, there is green.

**Yi**:
The phoenix bears a missive in its beak,
a dark jade tablet bestowed upon me—
enfeoffed as Marquis of Jin.

**Jia**:
To act inauspiciously is unwise,
dragging one another into the well.
Drowning in guilt and transgression,
misfortune breeds, sorrow multiplies.

**Gou**:
Wailing in northward flight,
bereft of an elder brother.
First and second—both ill-fated,
their bones lie ruined and lost.

**Cui**:
Lamb’s wool and leopard’s fur,
exalting my halls anew—
the noble one is renewed.

**Sheng**:
At midday, the marketplace,
each clutches what they possess.
Exchanging goods and wealth,
treasuring flavors, cherishing treasures,
hearts rejoice in gladness.

**Kun**:
Relief is cut off, principles severed,
only yang prevails, no rain falls.
All things ail, withered and dry,
blossoms and fruit are no more.

**Jing**:
The fox’s snare strips bare,
climbing the warm, verdant thicket.
Thorns of cold bring affliction—
what is not lacking?

**Ge**:
Treading through peril and hardship,
shedding bonds to escape calamity.
Entering the gate of fortune and joy,
beholding the great lord’s instruction.

**Ding**:
Fourfold chaos brings no peace,
east and west breed trouble.
Restraining my steps, I do not leave the city—
thus preserved whole,
relying on the blessing of life.

**Zhen**:
The southern state’s youngest son,
talent and strategy refined, most fair.
He sought my eldest daughter,
yet deemed her base and would not wed.
Instead he took the foul and vile—
afterward, deep regret arose.
*Compare to* **Jian**.

**Gen**:
Rash anger forfeits reason,
yang stands alone, no aid in sight.
All things ail, withered and dry,
the year’s millet harvest fails.

**Jian**:
Dreading distant blame,
shunning harm, one flees early.
Emerging, three foxes are caught—
their great beauty made a treasure.

**Guimei**:
Chasing deer on mountain peaks,
profit flees to my west.
Though searching north and south,
nothing is not obtained.

**Feng**:
Where dragons and serpents gather,
great waters find their joy.
Swelling, surging, overwhelming—
they leave me helpless.

**Lü**:
Wind fans the flames,
dragging the qilin’s tail.
Easy the task achieved,
fortune follows collapse.

**Xun**:
Marshlands breed dogs, waters breed turtles,
chicks of fowl and beasts are few.
The household does not prosper—
the heart longs for swift passage.

**Dui**:
Waters ruin my village,
flowing east to form the sea.
Turtles, turtles, clamoring—
no sight of a loving mother.
*See* **Huan** *and* **Cui**.

**Huan**:
Donning robes to wade the stream,
deeply soaked, one begs to cease.
Fortunate to meet a boatman,
crossing safely, no mishap.

**Jie**:
Turtles retreat to rivers and seas,
yet journey on land without end.
Self-inflicted withering,
losing the city’s market,
worry brings no harm.

**Zhongfu**:
Same root, different leaves,
delighting in benevolence and right virtue.
Eastern neighbors admire righteousness,
coming to flourish our state.

**Xiaoguo**:
Peach and plum blossom and bear fruit,
daily swelling in their clusters.
Grown large and ripe,
sweet and fine to eat—
bringing me profit and fortune.

**Jiji**:
Four pupils, four breasts,
keen of hearing, clear in reason.
Nothing hidden does not appear,
subtle sights span a thousand li.
Disasters do not arise,
the noble gather in throngs.

**Weiji**:
Shen and Shen dwell in the wastes,
by justice they chastise transgression.
Halting to forge alliances,
they achieve hegemonic might.

**Pi** (The Twelfth):
**Pi**:
Qin, wolf and tiger,
contends with Jin for supremacy.
Devouring its state,
it is named the First Emperor.

**Qian**:
The Yangzi, Yellow, Huai, and Ji—
heaven’s hidden treasuries.
Where all profits gather,
one may grow abundant,
delighting our lord.
*See* **Qian** *in* **Xian**.

**Kun**:
Where heaven brings disaster,
misfortune cannot be dwelt in.
Moving away brings fortune,
staying invites peril.

**Zhun**:
Reputation made, virtue achieved,
Xiang Yu’s neck untested.
Duke Jing grows old,
Confucius departs.

**Meng**:
Holding to good, shunning evil,
fortune and rank endure.
Though ravenous tigers lurk,
they cannot bring harm.

**Xu**:
Avoiding peril east and west,
one enters the gate of fortune.
Chaff and dregs are not enough—
worry stirs my heart.
*See* **Song** *in* **Weiji**.

**Song**:
Jades of ritual purity,
bearing gifts to see the king.
Raising Qi and Ji in a hundred li,
answering the summons of Qi and Qin.

**Shi**:
Dredging waters, deepening channels,
making stones gleam white.
Clad in plain robes with crimson lining,
playing by the marsh’s edge.
Obtaining the lord’s desire,
the heart’s will finds joy.

**Bi**:
Offices and ranks secure,
dwelling therein brings no harm.
Seeking release yet denied,
the elder brother harbors regret.

**Xiaoxu**:
A cart loaded without trousers,
naked, one sets forth on the road.
Children laugh in mockery,
the nobleman meets with woe.

**Lü**:
Pearl in hand, placed in the mouth—
for me, a precious profit.
Gaining what I possess,
delight and joy abound.

**Tai**:
Going is not like stopping,
straight cannot be bent.
Advancing is not like retreating—
thus may one be secure and fortunate.

**Tongren**:
A host of ghosts gathers like tiles,
within lies a great monstrosity—
nine bodies, no head.
Souls startled, spirits flee,
it cannot be dwelt in.

**Dayou**:
Households provided, people content,
hymns of praise arise as one.
The four barbarians submit,
spears and shields laid to rest.

**Qian**:
Faces of men, mouths of ghosts,
long tongues sharp as axes.
Smashing coral and jade tubes,
the Yin and Shang’s sacrifices cease.

**Yu**:
The steepness of southern mountains,
where the true person resides.
Virtue matched to Yao and Shun,
heaven’s mandate is their child.
Protected and blessed, they feast,
their persons receive great fortune.

**Sui**:
Spring peaches bloom,
the youngest daughter finds a home.
Receiving fortune for many years,
her son becomes lord of the state.

**Gu**:
Owls shatter the axe,
striking one to peril.
Relying on their loyal virtue,
they turn misfortune to fortune,
restoring what was toppled.

**Lin**:
Apes fall from lofty trees,
yet hands and feet remain unharmed.
Preserving my gold and jade,
they return to their chamber.
*See* **Song** *in* **Gen**, **Yi**, *and* **Yu**; *also* **Meng** *in* **Sui**.

**Guan**:
Heaven’s hidden corners,
where Yao and Shun dwelt.
Here one may preserve the self,
safeguarding our state and home.

**Shike**:
Bo Yi and Shu Qi blind,
feet pained, they cannot walk.
From dawn to dusk,
they do not leave their village.

**Bi**:
Sun and moon gaze upon each other,
radiance flourishing and bright.
The Three Sages succeed,
benevolent virtue greatly exalted.

**Bo**:
Peach and plum blossom and bear fruit,
daily swelling in their clusters.
Grown large and ripe,
sweet and fine to eat—
bringing me profit and fortune.
*See* **Tai** *in* **Xiaoguo**.

**Fu**:
Entering harmony, emerging in clarity,
movement and action bring light.
Turning and resting in due measure,
all one does is prosperous and healthy.

**Wuwang**:
Yin wanes, old and exhausted,
yang reveals its power.
Bearing *li*, carrying light,
the world grows bright.
Yet the enterprise does not last—
the toad usurps the throne.
*See* **Dayou** *in* **Lin**; *also* **Kun** *in* **Weiji**.

**Daxu**:
The journey not yet done,
new affairs arise again.
The lady Ji labors in toil,
no rest is granted.

**Yi**:
The fox howls in the northern chamber,
hungry, with nothing to eat.
Stranded on an empty mound,
none lend their strength.

**Daguo**:
The heroic sage hides his name,
people conceal the qilin afar.

The phoenix flees northward, chaos yet unceasing.

**Kan**:
Sickness and poverty yearn for fortune—
the Earl dispatches traders.
Opening the pen to choose the ram,
many gain great profit.
*See* **Song** *in* **Dun**.

**Li**:
Rustling and trembling,
collapsing in ruin.
Their good name extinguished,
long lost, never to return.
*See* **Tai** *in* **Qian**; *also* **Shihe** *in* **Kan**.

**Xian**:
The flower’s petals thin, its fruit hollow—
clothing worn to threads.
The woman’s craft fails,
silk and cloth become jade.

**Heng**:
Warm mountain pines stand together,
ever lush, never falling.
Sheltered by luan and phoenix,
they find joy and delight.
*See* **Xu** *in* **Kun**.

**Zhu**:
Losing grasp of a mother’s teaching,
a fine mate flees.
Like a lost elder,
like a stray dog without a home.

**Dazhuang**:
Taiyi rides a piebald steed,
descending from the heavens.
Favoring my younger uncle,
he is enfeoffed as Lord of Lu.
*See* **Tun** *in* **Sui**; *also* **Xu** *in* **Bi**.

**Jin**:
Dual wild ducks take flight,
seeking to return to the rice pond.
Cutting through the marsh of beans,
they are struck by arrows—
my breast and chest are wounded.
*See* **Tun** *in* **Lü**.

**Mingyi**:
The deep pit is filled level,
the world at peace.
Joyful in heart, delighting in mind,
relying on blessings for long life.

**Jiaren**:
All become heaven’s people—
clouds pass west of me.
The Wind Earl and swift rain
owe me no kindness.

**Kui**:
Wild crows and mountain magpies
gather at the game of liubo.
Three owls scatter, four flee—
the host triumphs over the guest.

**Jian**:
Northern Yin rules the cold,
unyielding ice stays chill.
Human feelings grow slack,
great hail brings disaster.

**Xie**:
The Earl of Yi retires,
leaving Jie to till the fields.
Holding to compliance, awaiting his return—
harmony restored, no blame.

**Sun**:
Autumn winds clasp hands,
laughing and chatting together.
Elder sings, younger dances—
feasting and joy abound.

**Yi**:
Leaving the nest, departing home,
passing south beyond White Horse.
East and west, receiving fortune—
reunited with mother.

**Guai**:
The crow flies, stumbling—
two by two, they harmonize.
No ailment in the limbs,
depart without doubt.

**Gou**:
A three-year-old dog,
born of the year *xu*.
The Xianyun invade from above,
the Lord of Ji flees.
*See* **Kun** *in* **Zhen**; *also* **Xu** *in* **Song**; *and* **Bi** *in* **Fu**.

**Cui**:
A broken basket, a tattered mat—
cast aside upon the road.
Collapsed and threadbare, full of holes,
no longer treasured.

**Sheng**:
Knots untied, bonds released,
worry brings no disaster.
Feasting on the spoils of captive homes,
receiving fortune in ease.

**Kun**:
The white sun shines bright,
thunder chariots hide away.
Clouds and rain do not move—
each returns to their own village.

**Jing**:
Mouth sealed, tongue tied,
heart stifled and oppressed.
Disaster departs, calamity arises,
nowhere to voice grievance.
*See* **Xun** *in* **Pi**; *also* **Xian** *in* **Bi**.

**Ge**:
Demanding cowries to ransom a fox,
refusing to heed my words.
Grasping a tiger’s whiskers,
dragging it back—impossible.
*See* **Kui** *in* **Xu**; *also* **Pi** *in* **Tong Ren**.

**Ding**:
Holding a crane, cradling its young—
what harm in seeing a snake?
The household remains whole,
none lose their place.
*See* **Heng** *in* **Tong Ren**.

**Zhen**:
Chasing a hare west of the mountain,
profit lies in entering the gate.
By my virtue and power,
I gain what becomes my fortune.

**Gen**:
Endless labor, no rest,
contending with the people for time.
An ox born with five toes—
walking in peril brings sorrow.

**Jian**:
Spring chestnuts, summer pears,
few and rare are the fresh.
Measuring by the thousand, by the ten thousand—
precious, beyond seeking.

**Gui Mei**:
Wailing in grief, heading north,
losing their eldest brother.
First and second—both misfortune,
bones scattered, ruined.

**Feng**:
Taxes levied again and again,
governance preys upon the people.
Shuttles and spindles empty,
families abandon their homes.

**Lü**:
Clothing and conduct invite enmity,
misfortune and blame align—
sorrow leaves no room for laughter.

**Dui**:
A rabbit-hat to advance the worthy,
stepping beyond the palace gate.
Bearing improper form,
treacherous scions bring harm.

**Xun**:
Mouth sealed, tongue tied,
words become the mother of disaster.
The Earl of Dai bears the calamity—
no prayer or plea can avert it.
*See* **Jing** *in* **Pi**; *also* **Xian** *in* **Bi**.

**Huan**:
Marrying the Jiang maiden,
a carriage welcomes the new bride.
Young Qi stands at the gate—
this child brings joy and delight.

**Jie**:
Tending sheep in the rice fields,
he hears the tiger’s roar.
Trembling in fear, he holds his breath—
yet in the end, no harm befalls.
*See* **Fu** *in* **Chun**.

**Zhong**:
The old concubine sits at the loom,
the weft snaps, unnoticed.
Her woman’s work remains undone—
winter’s cold comes, and she has no clothes.

**Xiao Guo**:
The black dragon spits forth light,
turning yin back to yang.
The honored one hunts and bears the sage—
the six armies prosper.

**Ji Ji**:
The eastern neighbor’s daughter weds,
becoming the king’s consort and queen.
Duke Zhuang builds a lodge
to oversee the royal mother.
Returning to the capital,
the Ji and Jiang clans rejoice.
*See* **Guan** *in* **Chun**, *also* **Yu** *in* **Tai**.

**Wei Ji**:
Guan Jie and his band,
their path rough, their steps unsteady.
The day and hour bode ill—
sickness becomes the body’s calamity.

*End of the Upper Canon, Scroll Two*
#1 *"Trust"* — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"Custom."*

**#2** *"Nan"* — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"Chu."*
**#3** Originally written as *"heaven"* (天), emended to *"premature death"* (夭) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#4** *"No premature death"* (无有夭折) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"Premature death is absent"* (夭折无有).
**#5** *"Countenance"* (容) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"guest"* (客).
**#6** *"Pursue"* (趁) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"hasten"* (趋).
**#7** *"Beam hall"* (杠堂) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"planted buds"* (植蕾).
**#8** *"Vast"* (昊) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"cloud"* (芸).
**#9** *"Autumn"* (秋) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"autumn"* (秋).
**#10** Originally written as *"fault"* (尤), emended to *"obstruction"* (尼) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#11** Originally written as *"harmony"* (谐), emended to *"separation"* (离) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#12** Originally written as *"unicorn"* (麒), emended to *"wings"* (翅) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#13** *"Fragrance"* (棻) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"leaf"* (叶).
**#14** *"Shang"* (商) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"Tang"* (汤).
**#15** Originally written as *"king"* (王), emended to *"jade"* (玉) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#16** *"Minor conduct"* (行少) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"base conduct"* (劣行).
**#17** Originally written as *"stockade"* (寨), emended to *"obstruction"* (蹇) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#18** Originally written as *"north"* (北), emended to *"comparison"* (比) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#19** *"Heart"* (心) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"center"* (中).
**#20** Originally written as *"utensils"* (具), emended to *"cowrie"* (贝) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#21** Originally written as *"Pi’s Kan"* (否之坎), emended to *"Fellowship’s Li"* (同人之离) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#22** *"Heavenly omen"* (天祥) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"great omen"* (大祥).
**#23** Originally written as *"mix"* (拌), unchanged in *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#24** Originally written as *"gouging"* (抉), emended to *"supporting"* (扶) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#25** Originally written as *"replace"* (代), emended to *"conquer"* (伐) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#26** Originally written as *"si"* (巳), emended to *"already"* (已) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#27** Originally written as *"life"* (生), emended to *"mutual"* (相) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#28** The phrase *"The noble one soothes the people, generations endure for a thousand autumns"* (君子抚民，世代千秋) is absent after *"anxiety"* (忧) in the original; now supplemented following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#29** *"Untie"* (解) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"entangle"* (绊).
**#30** *"Reckless action"* (妄行) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"gazing homeward"* (望家).
**#31** *"Dwell"* (居) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"tiger"* (虎).
**#32** *"Talent"* (才) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"fang"* (牙).
**#33** *"Great"* (大) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"hound"* (犬).
