**#244** *"See"* (见) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"establish"* (建).
**#245** Originally written as *"sixth earthly branch"* (巳), emended to *"already"* (已) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#246** *"Woman"* (女) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"Jiang"* (姜).
**#247** Originally written as *"orphan"* (孤), emended to *"fox"* (狐) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#248** *"Collapse peak"* (崩颠) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"summit collapse"* (巅崩).
**#249** *"Worn"* (弊) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"decay"* (敝).
**#250** Originally written as *"king"* (王), emended to *"jade"* (玉) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#251** Originally written as *"earth"* (地), emended to *"Kun"* (坤) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#252** *"Foolish"* (傻) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"seize"* (擭); collator’s note: should be *"slack"* (慢).
**#253** *"I"* (我) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"I"* (吾).
**#254** Originally written as *"defend"* (戍), emended to *"eleventh earthly branch"* (戌) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#255** Originally lacked the appended judgment *"Song zhi Fu"* (讼之复) after *"lawsuit"* (讼), supplied following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#256** Originally written as *"fruit"* (实), emended to *"treasure"* (宝) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#257** *"Transmit"* (传) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"transmit"* (传).
**#258** Originally written as *"palm"* (椰), emended to *"village"* (乡) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#259** Originally written as *"pillar"* (柱), emended to *"block"* (杜) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#260** Originally written as *"Buddha"* (佛), emended to *"Buddha"* (佛) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#261** Originally written as *"utensil"* (具), emended to *"cowrie"* (贝) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#262** *"Point"* (指) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"at"* (於).
**#263** Originally lacked *"Kui zhi Pi"* (同人之否) after *"Kui"* (睽), supplied following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#264** Originally lacked the appended judgment *"Suo zhi Heng"* (同人之恒) after *"place"* (所), supplied following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#265** *"Few"* (少) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"mountain"* (山).
**#266** *"Self-enemy"* (自敌) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"white silk"* (白缟).
**#267** *"Arrange"* (列) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"arrive"* (到).

**#268** Originally written as *"provide"* (给), emended to *"bind"* (结) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#269** *"Alike"* (齐) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"wife"* (妻).
**#270** *"Flourish"* (荣) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"bear"* (熊).
**#271** Originally written as *"filth"* (垢), emended to *"consort"* (妃) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#272** *"Oversee"* (监) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *"vessel"* (尊).
**#273** Originally lacked *"Tai zhi Yu"* (泰之豫) after *"Observe"* (观), supplied following *Baizi Quanshu*.

**The Forest of Changes, Upper Canon, Scroll Three**
**Hexagram Thirteen: Fellowship (同人)**

**Fellowship (同人)**
Atop the true mountain’s peak,
melting blades to cast plowshares.
No longer used for war,
the world rejoices greatly.

**Qian (乾)**
One arm, six hands,
yet none will stop the gaping mouth.
None willing to serve,
profit flees me.

**Kun (坤)**
Deer chase the trees,
sated, they return to their abode.
Resting in peace, no regrets.

**Zhun (屯)**
Wild geese and fish swim against the current,
reaching where men lurk in hiding.
Reeds replace pillars,
the sky’s roof inverted.

*(From here to Pi, one version diverges; see later textual variants.)*

**Meng (蒙)**
Three segments, five omens,
moving together in procession.
Lost in the empty marsh,
traversing six steeds—
wounded by bandits.

*(Bandits as "ravagers.")*

**Xu (需)**
The Yellow Emperor sets forth,
riding dragons and steeds.
Ascending Mount Tai in the east,
passing south through Qi and Lu,
all states rejoice.

**Song (讼)**
Treading peril, unsettled,
the heart drifts east and west.
Chasing deer in haste,
empty-handed in the end.

**Shi (师)**
Gazing toward Shang’s pillar,
the Grand Steward, the Duke of Zhou.
Shielding Tang and Wu,
enfeoffed as lords.

**Bi (比)**
White dragon, black tiger,
rising and raging together.
Battling at Ban’s mound,
Chiyou flees in defeat,
dying at Lu’s head.

*(Identical to Meng’s Kan and Yi’s Bi.)*

**Xiao Xu (小畜)**
Hauling stones up the mountain,
each step falters.
Brows knit in worry,
no joy found,
only long sighs of sorrow.

**Lü (履)**
Zhou’s virtue perfected,
its axle unwavering.
At the hour of Shen and You,
age and decline depart,
acupuncture offers no relief.

**Tai (泰)**
Riding clouds, bearing rain,
soaring with the flying birds.
A thousand *li* in motion,
I meet my loving mother.

*(Motion alternatively rendered as "movement and stillness.")*

**Pi (否)**
Offering cowries to ransom the raccoon,
yet it heeds not my words.
Grasping the tiger’s whiskers,
it cannot be dragged forth.

**Da You (大有)**
Three wings fly hither,
meeting my timely fortune.
Arriving first together,
great profit is gained.

**Qian (谦)**
Two feet, four wings,
flying into my land.
My elder sister finds peace,
reunited with our mother.

**Yu (豫)**
Dredging the lake’s pools,
jade cups bestowed by heaven.
Fish like white clouds,
a nation reaps carp.

**Sui (随)**
Ji Ji paces in hesitation,
gazing toward the city’s corner.
From dawn till dusk,
she sees not the Marquis of Qi,
yet her home knows no sorrow.

**Gu (蛊)**
The dragon seeks springs in hidden corners,
clouds and shadows follow.
The River Lord proffers a goblet,
kneeling to offer wine,
as torrents surge.

**Lin (临)**
Stepping out, misfortune strikes,
turning anger to enmity.
Blades cross in assault,
wounding my hand.

**Guan (观)**
Donning robes, delighting in heaven,
ordained by Qian and Kun,
at peace, no fault.

*(Delight alternatively rendered as "dance"; Qian and Kun as "chaos spirits.")*

**Shi He (噬嗑)**
Two metals clash,
bold and fierce in battle.
All day they war,
unbroken, unchipped.

**Ben (贲)**
The great cart hard to harness,
two earthworms like ropes.
Horses bolt behind the mountain,
wheels detach—no progress.
Midway, disaster strikes.

**Bo (剥)**
On Wen’s mountain, purple mushrooms,
red grasses of Yong and Liang.
Longevity and harmonious *qi*,
the king treasures them.
The ancestral spirit joins the feast,
blessings and fortune arrive.

**Fu (复)**
Pearl in hand, placed in the mouth,
a treasure I nurture.
Gaining what is mine,
joyful and glad.

**Wu Wang (无妄)**
Bearing a cart up the mountain,
strength spent, the path arduous.
Fierce wind, rain, and snow
block my way.
Turning back mid-journey,
the troubled find joy.

**Da Xu (大畜)**
Tao Zhu and Bai Gui,
masters of trade, amassing wealth.
Threefold they gain a thousand gold,
their virtue bestowing upon the highest benevolence.

**Yi (颐)**
Zi Niu grasps the unicorn,
the *Spring and Autumn* records its omen.
The primal sage nears his end,
Confucius grieves.

**Da Guo (大过)**
Spring’s warmth spreads,
blessings and steps grow in unison.
The four seasons unmarred,
harmony brings prosperity.

**Kan (坎)**
Kong Huai, jade-like,
emerges from the dark valley.
Soaring to the tallest tree,
beating its wings,
its radiance dazzles the eyes.

*(Identical to Kun’s Bi.)*

**Li (离)**
Qu Tu and Kang Ju,
admiring virtue, enter court.
The joy of deep dew,
three cups complete the grace.
Returning to the yurt,
their home at peace.

*(Identical to Song’s Heng.)*

**Xian (咸)**
Traveling by autumn and winter nights,
gazing at the stars.
The Dao’s path smooth and profitable,
a lifetime without harm.

**Heng (恒)**
Like the crane nurturing its young,
seeing the snake—what fault?
The household intact,
none lose their place.

**Dun (遯)**
Steadfast as Mount Tai,
fortune and longevity ever nearing.
Though jackals and tigers prowl,
they cannot endanger me.

**Da Zhuang (大壮)**
The aged and ignorant slumber,
unaware of east or west.
The year’s lord loses reason,
straight commands bent to crooked,
the king calls it treasure.

**Jin (晋)**
Bearing jade tablets, riding scepters,
pleading at the river.
The Duke of Zhou’s swift success,
the young lord’s ailments healed.

**Ming Yi (明夷)**
The great king governs,
the year bountiful, the people prosperous.
The state abundant,
the king rejoices.

**Jiaren (家人)**
Households contend, turning their backs,
harmonious qi nowhere to dwell.
Yin and yang both obstructed,
valley winds part mother and child.

**Kui (睽)**
Qi and Lu dispute in words,
battling at Dragon Gate.
Resentment sows calamity,
three generations unsettled.
As in *Bi*’s *Gu* or *Kun*’s *Li*.

**Jian (蹇)**
Deer find sweet grass,
calling to their kin.
The nine clans in harmony,
never leaving their homeland.

**Xie (解)**
A hundred li hard to traverse,
yet dimness gives way to light.
Leaving Yu for Qin,
he became the minister of Mu.

**Sun (损)**
Plums and plums bear winter fruit,
the land teems with bandits.
Chaos erupts on all sides,
the king cannot restrain it.
As in *Tun*’s *Shi*.

**Yi (益)**
The treasury overflows,
the king dispenses relief.
Fishing in rivers and seas,
the bamboo nets haul much.
Great serpents and giant eels
clash at the city’s outskirts,
the lord flees in terror.
As in *Bi*’s *Lin* or *Sun*’s *Kui*.

**Guai (夬)**
The male pheasant takes flight, the gate opens,
great troubles dissolve.
Leaving the old, mounting the horse,
no harm befalls the self.
As in *Xu*’s *Dui*.

**Gou (姤)**
Marrying a wife in Yichang,
the household sings and dances,
ever joyful and glad.
At the height of the yang’s zenith,
the Jia clan perishes.
Disaster strikes Liu Xu,
kinship destroyed, reduced to ruins.

**Sheng (升)**
Brightness passes the thatched hut,
delighting in eel and bream.
Though driven, they will not flee,
Tian Jun bears sorrow.

**Kun (困)**
The lame and the halt travel together,
at dusk the cart breaks,
the traveler loses their way, lacking grain.

**Jing (井)**
Dragon Gate’s minor straits,
flowing without harm.
The people dwell securely in their land,
lord and minister preserve one another.

**Ge (革)**
Mountains and hills block all four sides,
barricading my path.
Wishing to advance but unable,
all return to their former place.

**Ding (鼎)**
Two tigers fight,
blood flows like floating pestles.
The city walls stand empty,
mugwort and blossoms choke the roads.

**Gen (艮)**
Dragons are born without constancy,
some lodge in hollow mulberries.
Riding wind and cloud,
they render service for Yao.

**Zhen (震)**
Leaning against the eastern wall,
aspirations low, the heart toils.
Morning meal at the Chu pavilion,
Han Zi bows his head.

**Jian (漸)**
The great whale swishes its tail,
pursuing clouds to blow fire.
Mud becomes dry land,
low fields yield millet.

**Guimei (归妹)**
The lame and crooked follow one another,
at dusk the ox tires.
The journey lags behind,
profit lost, the female gone.

**Feng (丰)**
Three travel together,
seeking great auspices in the north.
The eldest’s feet ail,
the youngest is asked to bear the load.
The debt of Liu Xia—
not missing the black or yellow.

**Lü (旅)**
The phoenix on the left,
the qilin on the right.
The sagely and wise meet,
Yi and Lü gather.
Harm does not reach,
the time free of misfortune,
fortune becomes my mother.
As in *Song*’s *Xian*.

**Xun (巽)**
Riding a raft to cross the river,
though deep, no peril.
Great-grandson and august ancestor,
generations together,
receiving great fortune.

**Yun (兑)**
Paired eyes, four wings,
come to pacify our land.
Blessings ascend the hall,
sharing my bed.
As in *Bi*’s *Li* or *Sun*’s *Sui*.

**Huan (渙)**
Wed among the Jiangs and Lǚs,
a carriage welcomes the new bride.
The young wife at the gate,
the eldest son rejoices.
*Pi*’s *Huan*.

**Jie (節)**
Moth-worms turn traitor,
harming my grains and millet.
All the rice, wheat, and barley—
autumn yields nothing.
*Pi*’s *Huan*.

**Zhong Fu (中孚)**
Clothes worn inside out,
summoned by the king’s call.
Achieving and binding Zhou,
the realm rests in great peace.

**Xiao Guo (小過)**
Prince Sun and Master Ji,
befriend one another.
Sincere and bright,
promoted and recommended.

**Ji Ji (既濟)**
A gushing spring flows smooth,
its current unbroken.
Fouling into rivers and seas,
ruining towns and hamlets.
No home to dwell,
hearing tigers yet unafraid,
turning to me with laughter.

**Wei Ji (未濟)**
The shrike steals fat,
pecking grain amiss.
Chaotic governance, no constancy,
plunging my clarity into disorder.

**Da You (大有) The Fourteenth**

**Da (大)**
A white tiger bares its fangs,
marching to subdue the eastern Hua.
The crimson magpie leads the way,
offering pleasing words of praise.
The enemy sues for peace,
bearing jade in haste.

**Qian (乾)**
Southern mountains, great ranges,
trapped in barren mulberry.
Old sands turn to stone,
oxen and horses starve.

**Kun (坤)**
Coiling branches lose their fork,
parting from their mother,
severed, never knowing one another.

**Zhun (屯)**
What I say, steadfast and sure,
none match my walls.
Joy in strength, firm and enduring,
here one may long abide.
*Qian*’s *Kun*.

**Meng (蒙)**
Plum and peach blossoms scatter,
the heart stirs with sorrow.
Fear and shame, slight remorse,
disordering my spirit and qi.

**Xu (需)**
Fire though fierce,
lies behind me.
Bandits though many,
stand to my right.
My person safe and blessed,
no peril or danger.

**Song (訟)**
A tiger crouches in the mountain’s corner,
a deer passes its flank.
Bow and arrow drawn again,
mistaken for the clerk of works—
it cowers, does not rise.
Reaching the wild marshes,
it finds sweet grass.

**Shi (師)**
Three fires blaze bright,
rain quenches their light.
High rank swiftly toppled,
arrogance invites ruin.

**Bi (比)**
A lone bird in Chu,
slandered yet blameless,
long scattered in sorrow.
*Alternative reading: Lü (旅)*.

**Xiao Xu (小畜)**
One house, ten sons,
same heart, different mothers.
With righteousness to guard against calamity,
misfortune does not arise.

**Lǚ (履)**
A merchant travels,
possessing nothing.
Greedy for profit’s pearl,
he lingers in the royal market.
Returning home, looking inward—
what fault lies with the lord’s son?

**Tai (泰)**
Yu prepares to rule,
entering Kunlun from the north.
Gradually advancing into sunlight,
ascending the warm springs,
his merit and virtue shine bright.

**Pi (否)**
Qian walks in great virtue,
treading the field without bound.
Abundant harvests ripen,
each attains what is due.

**Tong Ren (同人)**
The southern land flourishes,
millet and sorghum brew wine.
One may feast the elders,
delighting in worthy friends.

**Qian (謙)**
Square boats ready for water,
fires lit along the riverbank.
A lifetime without misfortune,
with *Guai*’s good fortune,
ever secure and at peace.
*Tai*’s *Lǚ*.

**Yu (豫)**
Thunder pursues relentlessly,
no rest, no respite.
Battling on the plain,
overturned by the Yi.

**Sui (隨)**
Hesitating, pacing,
hand to heart, scratching the head.
Five days and four nights,
gambling with the Marquis of Qi.

**Gu (蠱)**
A wide mouth, full lips,
the spirit’s messenger speaks.
Yellow dragon, radiant star,
emerging at Virtue’s Gate.
Ascending the hall with blessings,
the world rests in peace.
*Xu*’s *Cui*.

**Lin (臨)**
Yin wanes, old and spent,
Yang builds its power.
*Li* bears the sun’s light,
the world grows bright.
*Pi*’s *Wu Wang*, *Kun*’s *Wei Ji*.

**Guan (觀)**
Three paths, five peaks,
Yangcheng and Mount Tai.
Where spirits and sages dwell,
no weapons or war—
below, the land is preserved. *Xu*’s *Meng*.

**Shi He (噬嗑)**
Years of abundance, harvests ripe,
benevolent rule brings joy to the people.
Favorable for settling,
travelers find good fortune.

**Bi (賁)**
A Chu crow meets an arrow—
it cannot be left to roam long.
Exiled without guilt,
he composes this poem,
to tell of Confucius’ sorrow.

**Bo (剝)**
Stepping out boldly,
at odds with a wicked brother.
Yugong’s mother of Jin,
brings me grief for my toes.

**Fu (復)**
Fire in the well’s valley,
willow shoots grow horns.
Passing through the Celestial Market,
gazing upon the Supreme Ultimate.
Ascending the jade terrace,
the household gains six lords.

**Wu Wang (無妄)**
A shepherd meets a wolf,
though fearful, he is unharmed.
Trembling in dread,
yet in the end, no disaster befalls.

**Da Xu (大畜)**
Silkworm cocoons and sacrificial beasts,
reverently serving ghosts and spirits.
The spirits feast and drink,
receiving blessings and many descendants.
Wang Ji does not come—
Confucius is trapped in Chen.
*Qian*’s *Lǚ*.

**Yi (頤)**
The great marsh adorned,
the south is defeated, the herdsman blessed.
Lord Chang works for me,
gaining many horses and cattle,
favorable for relocation.

**Da Guo (大過)**
A withered tree, no branches,
parting from my child.
Hunger and cold, no one to provide—
alone, I grieve.

**Kan (坎)**
Heaven and earth, ninefold layers,
Yao and Shun govern the center.
Straightening cap and robes,
the cosmos is at peace.

**Li (離)**
The egret wades the Jing,
the noble one finds tranquility.
Restoring virtue without fault,
fortune and prosperity come to fruition.

**Xian (咸)**
A barefoot chase after a fox,
mocked by others.
The hen crows at dawn—
the root of disorder in the household.

**Heng (恒)**
Canonical texts and legal words,
stored in the Orchid Terrace.
Though calamity strikes,
alone, I avoid disaster.
*Da Guo*, *Kun*’s *Da Xu*.

**Dun (遯)**
Three fools, half-mad,
yearning for a peaceful village.
Bewildered, they lose the Way,
unable to tell dusk from dawn.

**Da Xu (大畜)**
Lumps, sores, and rashes,
festering wounds on the body.
Illness and chronic ailments,
yet never in mortal danger.

**Jin (晉)**
Three pigs run together,
battling at the valley’s mouth.
The white pig does not prevail,
dying beneath the ruins.

**Ming Yi**
By the lord’s radiance sustained,
by virtue’s blessing protected.
Though plunged in dire straits,
alone, I escape misfortune.

**Jia Ren**
Uphold righteousness, exalt virtue,
to establish great fortune.
Auspicious to proclaim at dawn,
as the martial deeds of Zhou arose.

**Kui**
Fourfold chaos unsettles,
east and west breed resentment.
The body halts, no merit gained,
confined within the city walls.
Yet preserved in wholeness,
by the blessing of life’s fortune.

**Jian**
Golden fangs, iron teeth,
son of the Queen Mother of the West.
No peril or danger,
crossing the Way brings great profit.
*Xiao Xu*’s *Da You*.

**Xie**
Celebration follows fortune,
daily gains multiply in joy,
delight and attainment abound.

**Sun**
Vast Heaven, bright sun,
shining upon our land.
All the people at peace,
each receiving their blessing.

**Yi**
Left eye blind, right eye dim,
vision obscured, unclear.
The people below suffer many afflictions,
the lord loses his constancy.

**Guai**
I possess millet and fine grain,
heaped by the roadside.
With carts and covered wagons,
they arrive in my homeland,
stored in the noble granary.

**Gou**
Different kinds, divergent paths,
hearts that do not yearn.
The sow has no boar,
the castrated pig dwells in the house.

**Cui**
The sparrow forages in flight,
exiting the gate, it sees the hawk.
Tumbling up and down,
scarcely finding a place to rest.

**Sheng**
The wilds hold stacked grain,
the reaper harnesses and takes it.
No wolf or tiger encountered,
returning home at dusk.

**Kun**
Virtue of keen sensitivity,
roused to action, forgetting food.
The captured leopard, the seized crane,
seeking fortune for the king.
*Shi*’s *Guan*.

**Jing**
Bright rites, spring’s completion,
the crowing of chickens at dawn.
Yang’s brilliance loses the Way,
unable to preserve itself,
diminishing into misfortune.

**Ge**
Left arm cradles gold and jade,
right hand gains a bear’s paw.
Ever full, never lost,
attaining the heart’s desire.

**Ding**
Treading in mud, soiling the feet,
name besmirched, body shamed.
Two foes meet,
the self reduced to nothingness.

**Zhen**
Dwelling in peace, reluctant to move,
not leaving its dust.
The scent of grain and rice lingers,
joy in enduring property.

**Gen**
Where Heaven’s disasters roam,
misfortune cannot be abided.
Moving away brings fortune,
lingering invites peril.

**Jian**
Dim and silent,
unaware of daylight.
Chaotic clouds obscure,
light concealed,
King You loses his kingdom.

**Gui Mei**
The bright goose honks,
making its home upon the water.
Male and female in harmony,
ever sharing delight,
obtaining their desire.
*Da Xu*’s *Ding*.

**Deng**
Longevity without end,
descendants in the thousands and millions.
Pillars bear the beams,
firm and unshaken.

**Lü**
Qilin and phoenix,
auspicious omens of good governance.
Yin and yang in harmony,
the state free from calamity.

**Xun**
The hidden corner of Heaven,
where Yao and Shun dwelled.
Here one may preserve the self,
safeguarding one’s household.

**Dui**
Matched in union, mutually welcomed,
profit spreads to the four directions.
The wedding set as the appointed time,
joined with fortune and joyful laughter.

**Huan**
Honing virtue, tempering talent,
at last completing the Zhou.
Receiving the great mandate,
enfeoffed as the Marquis of Qi.

**Jie**
Seated with fortune,
storing water to guard against fire,
ever free from disaster.

**Zhong Fu**
Concealed in dawn and dusk,
awaiting the time with gentle warmth.
At last encountering the bright sun,
becoming the honored master of the age.

**Xiao Guo**
Gazing at the sun, its light renewed,
in harmony with Heaven.
Everlasting joy and delight,
fortune as an elder brother.

**Ji Ji**
Great head, bright eyes,
receiving blessings anew.
Two sparrows fly in,
striking the green one.

**Wei Ji**
Thorns grow on Mount Ke,
fate bound to the losing side.
Robes stripped away,
scorching in summer, freezing in winter.
Standing withered and dry,
none among the multitude descend.
*Qian*’s *Ji Ji*.
*Qian*’s fifteenth.

**Humility**

**King Jian**
Wang Qiao free from illness,
a dog’s head free from pain.
Losing a sandal, limping away,
lacking my followers, turning back.

**Qian**
Croaking frogs in the dark,
groping blindly in gloom.
Much talk, little substance,
words accomplish nothing.

**Kun**
The Purple Palace of the North Star,
robed and capped, stands at the center.
Embracing harmony, embodying virtue,
ever receiving great fortune.
A bronze knife carves jade—
unyielding, nothing is gained.

**Tun**
A bound jade’s lingering glow,
dim and obscured in number.
The Queen Mother’s envy spreads,
disrupting my undertakings.

**Meng**
The lower turns its back on the upper,
relying on its brightness to yield.
Ziying with two heads,
Chen laid waste to its ruins.

**Xu**
A phoenix born in Kuaiji,
gradually growing strong enough to fly.
Soaring over the osmanthus groves,
it becomes the leader of the flock.

**Song**
Digging a well to seek jade,
not the treasure of He the Jade Carver.
Reputation ruined, body humiliated,
labor yields no reward.
*Variant: Shi hexagram.*

**Shi**
Envoys dispatched with gifts,
escorted to Lai.
All officials rise in unison,
the lord’s heart rejoices.
*Variant: Song hexagram.*

**Bi**
Anxi and Kangju,
foreign lands of domed tents.
Not within our realm’s borders,
the envoy grieves in sorrow.

**Xiao Xu**
The Yangtze, the Yellow River, the Huai, the seas—
Heaven’s great markets.
Merchants receive fortune,
the state grows rich.

**Lü**
Same root, different leaves,
delighting in benevolence and lofty virtue.
The eastern forests admire righteousness,
coming to invigorate our land.

**Tai**
A white crane holds a pearl,
the night chamber shines again.
Cherishing my virtuous words,
my person receives glory and honor.

**Pi**
Treading through peril and hardship,
escaping calamity and misfortune.
Entering the joyful gate,
I see my mother, my lord.

**Tong Ren**
Gong and Shang in harmony,
notes following one another.
A black colt at the gate,
the lord rejoices.

**Da You**
Heaven and Earth unite in offering,
the six positions radiant.
Yin and Yang in proper order,
thus accomplishing their work.

**Yu**
The Yangtze, the Yellow River, the Huai, the seas—
Heaven’s hidden treasuries,
where all benefits gather.
One may grow abundant,
delighting our lord.
*Pi’s Kun.*

**Sui**
Two crows fly together,
seeking to return to the rice pond.
Cutting through the reed marshes,
they are struck by arrows,
wounding my chest.
*Tun’s Lü, Pi’s Jin.*

**Gu**
Eldest, second, third, youngest—
at dusk, they sleep.
Naked and blind,
losing my cowrie pouch,
gnawing at the roadside.

**Lin**
Receiving the mandate from the cultured ancestor,
bearing decline and reviving.
Restrained by righteousness,
though suffering, no blame.

**Guan**
The Dipper turns on its pivot,
following Heaven without care,
joining in joy.
*Yi’s Jie.*

**Shi Ke**
The Zhou army strikes Zhou,
battling at Muye.
At dawn on the jiazi day,
the Son of Heaven rejoices.

**Bi**
Ten hens, a hundred chicks,
ever with their mother.
Holding a chicken to fight a tiger—
who dares harm them?

**Bo**
Jie and Zhou dwell together,
the people grieve in sorrow.
Bearing arms and shouldering staves,
they battle in Qi and Lu.

**Fu**
Southern Mountain, vast Heaven,
Ci and Zheng mourn their lords.
Grieving the innocent,
they turn their backs, making enemies.

**Wu Wang**
A hundred rivers flow to the sea,
flowing without cease.
Though the path is distant,
none fail to reach it.

**Da Xu**
Eyes cannot close,
feet tremble with worry.
Startled and fearful,
I leave my state’s borders.

**Yi**
A crow ascends,
an osprey soars,
illuminating the Eastern Sea.
A dragon descends to the courtyard,
becoming the successor of Tao Shu.
Enfeoffed at Liaoqiu,
fortune and blessing abound.
*Xu’s Da Xu.*

**Da Guo**
The north abounds in jujubes,
where tangerines and pomelos gather.
Bearing sacks of millet,
my baskets overflow.

**Kan**
A hanging fox, eating without labor,
consuming what it has not earned.
Losing the trust of distant people,
truly it wearies my heart.

**Li**
Lambskin and leather,
the gentleman’s court robes.
Assisting governance, upholding virtue,
uniting the myriad states.

**Xian**
Qi and Lu contend in speech,
battling at Dragon Gate.

**Gou**
Breeding resentment, inviting disaster,
three years without peace.
*Kun’s Li, Tongren’s Kui, Bi’s Gu.*

**Heng**
Endless dark, ceaseless rain,
paths turned to mire and flood.
Merchants halt their trade,
markets stand empty and bare.

**Dun**
A turtledove steals fat,
perching on a slender branch.
Trembling, unsteady,
blown by the wind.
A heart chilled with dread,
ever fearing peril and danger.

**Dazhuang**
Guard against calamity, prepare for disaster,
misfortune will not come.
Though distressed, no harm befalls.

**Jin**
Stretching the neck, breaking the stocks,
separated from mother by different gates.
No one to fear,
with whom can one speak?

**Mingyi**
Fish and shrimp leave the sea,
hiding in dried-up pools.
Streets and alleys narrow and cramped,
no freedom to move.
North and south boundless,
thirst and hunger breed illness.

**Jiaren**
Reverent, generous, trustworthy, diligent,
merit spreads across the four seas.
Banishing misfortune,
joy returns with the mother.

**Kui**
Years of famine, no harvest,
tyrannical rule harms the people.
Ganxi and Lishan,
Qin and Chu nurse grudges.

**Jian**
The right eye lacks a pupil,
squinting, dim of sight.
Ten paces away,
unable to tell who it is.

**Xie**
Cicadas and toads rejoice,
plants and trees flourish.
Leaves multiply, thriving,
daily increasing in abundance.

**Sun**
Virtue constant, self-assured,
sitting at ease without blame.
Fortunate to enter a noble land,
secure and honored to old age.

**Yi**
A cunning hare darts,
a fine hound gives chase.
The pheasant is harmed,
seized by the hawk.

**Guai**
Spring peaches bloom;
a young maiden marries well.

**Gou**
Receiving blessings for many years,
the son is enfeoffed as a lord.

**Gou**
Mountain stones rot and decay,
crumbling and collapsing.
Above and below, hearts diverge;
the lord suffers their curse.

**Cui**
Waters ruin my village,
converging streams form a sea.
Turtles and dragons clamor,
my home unseen.

**Sheng**
Ten orifices, a dragon’s body,
evolved from the Eight Primes.
Following heaven, emulating earth,
acting in accord with the seasons,
wealth and nobility endure forever.

**Kun**
The four barbarians admire virtue,
coming to prosper our land.
The cultured lord descends to the plains,
together they receive its power.

**Jing**
At the summit of Mount Ge’s head,
immortals roam the Daoist path.
Auspicious for dwelling,
ever free from blame and sorrow.

**Ge**
The turtledove migrates,
westward to Pingzhou.
Struck by thunder and hail,
my reed hut is damaged.
Household cold and hungry,
I long for my former home.

**Ding**
The dog lacks forelegs,
the yin male rebels in the north,
becoming a harm and thief to itself.

**Zhen**
Yang stands alone, extreme and proud,
filled with resentment and confusion.
The carriage overturns, its canopy lost,
the self faces terror.
Yet its wish is granted,
male and female endure together.
*(Hexagram Qian’s first line: Tun)*

**Gen**
An empty trough blocks the way,
the pig’s vapor does not arrive.
Drawing the bow to curse the chicken,
the rooster flies away.

**Jian**
Long nights, short days,
yin becomes a thief to yang.
All things wither and empty,
hidden in the northern wilds.

**Guimei**
Warriors of claws and fangs,
resentful and venomous, curse their father.
Turning their woe upon themselves,
the harm does not reach their mother.

**Feng**
Kneeling to beg for a hare,
no virtue, only rot and stench.
Biting their fingers in distress,
they cannot go north.

**Lü**
The youngest daughter of Youshen,
becomes the queen and empress.
Her noble son lives long,
mother to the four seas.

**Xun**
Young Jiang hesitates,
waiting at Meng’s city corner.
From dawn till dusk,
she does not see the Lord of Qi.

**Dui**
That battle, those words reversed,
father and brother bring trouble.
Crossing this sorrow and resentment,
they die in the end, never returning.

**Huan**
Chasing deer on the mountain’s peak,
the advantage flees west.
Wandering south and north,
what is sought is not found.

**Jie**
Piercing the nose, threading a pearl,
seized by the tiger.
The Queen Mother offers blessings,
disaster does not form a calamity,
yet suddenly comes of itself.

**Zhongfu**
Tigers, leopards, bears, and brown bears
play in the mountain valleys.
The noble and virtuous lord,
too, attains his desire.

**Xiaoguo**
Plums ripen in winter,
the land teems with thieves.

**Disorder and chaos arise together,
the king cannot control them.**

**Jiji**
Hoping for favor, it does not arrive;
literary works remain unfinished.

**Yang** child chases the hare,
the hound’s hook catches nothing.

**Weiji**
A thousand pillars, a hundred beams,
yet they never collapse or fall.
With benevolence and wisdom aiding the sage,
the Zhou house remains peaceful and secure.

**Yuzhi Sixteenth**

**Yu**
Ice drifts and scatters,
wild geese call in harmony.
Strong men and grown women
may gather as one,
giving birth to the worthy.

**Qian**
The dragon-horse ascends the mountain,
no springs of water remain.
Throat scorched, lips parched,
the mouth cannot speak.

**Kun**
The Marquis of Cai pays court to Chu,
lingering by the river’s edge.
Months pass in delay,
longing for his lord.

**Zhun**
Wen’s distress in Meili,
Tang’s imprisonment in Xatai.
Yet benevolence and sageliness bring no harm—
what worry in repeated hardship?
Bound in fetters like a rabbit,
he becomes a luminary for the age.

**Meng**
Canonical texts and legal writings,
stored in the Orchid Terrace’s vaults.
Though chaos and ruin strike,
they alone escape disaster.

**Xu**
In the land of felt and furs,
rites and decorum are neglected.
Mounted archers assail
our capital city.

**Song**
Stars fall like rain,
strength weakens, no aid comes.
The strong yin restrains yang—
no peace on this land.

**Shi**
Locusts devour our rice,
driven away, they will not leave.
The ears bear no grain,
only hollow husks remain.

**Bi**
The hungry tiger seeks to feed,
but is subdued by the dragonfly.
Yu dredges Dragon Gate,
avoiding fault, dispelling peril—
the great and base find peace.

**Xiaoxu**
Bats hide by night,
daring not venture by day.
Wine turns to sour broth,
spindles rot in spoiled stew.

**Lü**
Essence and bloom wither,
the form grows ugly.
Jarring and stumbling,
withered, rotted, poisoned.

**Tai**
Both feet fail to move,
journeying far is difficult.
Hastening steps cannot keep pace—
the rear guard misses its moment.

**Pi**
Commanding the wife, honoring the mother,
the household thrives without fault.
The noble one’s joy
endures long.

**Tongren**
Hunger and fleas build a house,
marriage brings tangled chaos—
no thread can be found.

**Dayou**
Zilu grasps the qilin,
the *Spring and Autumn* records its omens.
The primal sage meets his end—
Confucius grieves in his heart.

**Qian**
Moth larvae become pests,
ruining our crops.
All grain and wheat are devoured—
autumn yields nothing.

**Sui**
Worry festers within,
mountains collapse into illness.
Disaster rises from the inner wall—
in the end, it overthrows the state.

**Gu**
Eating lingzhi, swallowing yellow,
drinking from jade cups.
Spirits flow in communion—
no grief or misfortune remains.

**Lin**
One decision, two hearts,
the thrust does not run deep.
Deeds yield no success—
endeavors do not bear fruit.

**Guan**
Gazing ten li at the smoke,
scattered and dispersed in all directions.
Form and face vanish—
the lord is never seen.

**Shike**
Drawing the bow, readying the crossbow,
traversing mountain paths.
Though tigers lie in ambush,
who dares harm them?

**Bi**
Springs dry, marshes parch,
the lord suffers hunger and thirst.
The noble one, though distressed,
slowly finds relief.

**Bo**
Wild apes and mountain magpies
play at weiqi and liubo.
Three ravens, four scattered—
the host triumphs over the guest.

**Fu**
Sheep startle, horses bolt,
upheaval above and below.
Drums sound without cease—
Xiangong flees in defeat.

**Wuwang**
The Yellow Emperor, divine and wise,
his eight sons sagely and keen.
All receive great fortune—
the world is peaceful and prosperous.

**Daxu**
Tethering horses, brewing wine,
a violent gale suddenly rises.
The sacrificial vessels overturn,
rank and position are cast aside.
Yet the luminous spirits descend in blessing—
the Dao remains free of harm or bandits.

**Yi**
The victorious snake rides the dragon,
Song and Zheng suffer famine and misfortune—
the people eat grass and thistles.

**Daguo**
Dredging water, chiseling in secret,
making stone gleam white.
Clad in plain robes with crimson borders,
they wander the marshlands in play.

Obtaining what the lord desires,
heart and will rejoice in delight.

**Kan**
Westward past the tiger’s den,
startling my vanguard.
Though troubled, no danger arises.

**Li**
Garments made without sleeves—
one does not know where to thread them.
Guests point east and west,
unable to settle in peace.

**Cheng**
The morning wind’s patterned wings,
following the season to warmth.
Male and female harmonize—
no fear of peril or danger.

**Heng**
The heart brims with regret,
words spoken turn strange.
An owl hoots in the northern chamber—
its voice foul and loathsome.
Petitions go unanswered.

**Dun**
The parted woman departs in separation,
grieving in bitter sorrow.
The Qi woman’s lack of goodness
brings me heartache.

**Dazhuang**
Missing the time of return,
male and female suffer bitter grief.
Wandering in foreign lands,
separated from one’s uncle.

**Jin**
Magpies nest in the willow,
the turtledove seizes its place.
Relying on strength, virtue thin,
heaven’s mandate offers no aid.

**Mingyi**
A crane steals my pearl,
fleeing to the eastern capital.
The swan, enraged, pursues—
to the ruins of the Guo clan.
No trace is found,
causing the elder’s heart to grieve.

**Jiaren**
Husband and wife turn their backs,
harmony cannot dwell.
Yin and yang both obstructed,
the strong wife bears no child.

**Kui**
The moon races, the sun strides—
they do not share the same lodging.
Wife and husband glare,
the lord loses his home.

**Jian**
A Luoyang girl is wed,
a fine suitor chases her.
Three widows lose their mates,
the bride bears no child.

**Xie**
The Zhou virtue complete,
the loom’s shuttle does not tilt.
The grand minister travels east and west,
the Xia realm enjoys peace.

**Sun**
At midday the market thrives,
exchanging treasures for profit.
All that is sought in name and gain
brings joy to the heart.

**Yi**
A young maid sleeps alone,
the eldest daughter unwed—
no benefit is gained.

**Guai**
Loyal words aid completion,
the king’s governance does not falter.
The foundation of Gong Liu,
cultivated by Wen and Wu.

**Gou**
Ox and steed share the hall,
the Guo clan perishes.
The state lies in ruins,
the lord flees in haste.

**Cui**
Beans grow in the central plains,
awaiting the pheasant’s feast.
Feasting with friends,
all that is sought is greatly obtained.

**Sheng**
Much emptiness, little substance,
words cannot be understood.
The goblet stands empty, no wine—
reckless speech falls like rain.

**Kun**
Green flies gather on the fence,
the lord trusts slander.
Harming the worthy, wounding the loyal—
trouble arises from women.

**Jing**
Treading on a stump, the carriage overturns,
the horse bolts, the cart is damaged—
walking brings me worry.

**Ge**
The merchant’s wind summons bandits,
calling northern raiders.
Spies respond from within,
contending with me in battle.
The concubine’s treasure hoard—
the master does not prevail.

**Ding**
Indulging in pleasure, fond of wandering,
not at ease in his home.
Perhaps a young concubine—
long lost, she does not return.

**Zhen**
I have fine steeds,
raising them in due season.
The eastern family’s elders and youths
come to my chariot.
The price is fair, the deal sound—
no later regret or harm.

**Gen**
Distress and hardship open upward,
encountering Yao.
Ascending the great forest,
the land knows no wicked men.

**Jian**
All hares flee together,
a male bear follows behind.
The rider cannot advance,
losing trust, dwelling alone.

**Guimei**
Not venturing far,
thrice pondering before turning back.
The heart fears calamity—
at midday, one rests.

**Feng**
Hastily dispatched on a mission,
Zhongshan’s filial son.
The Marquis of Wen rejoices,
summoning his heir to court.

**Lü**
Entering the gate of heaven, guarding the city,
the lord dwells in peace.
No toil or hardship—
the pheasant perches on Mount Wen.
Rich in fat and marrow,
the prince’s wish is granted,
bearing towering fortune.

**Xun**
Ascending the steps to the hall,
meeting my father and brothers.
Wine to the left, ale to the right—
fortune comes to greet me.

**Dui**
Autumn serpents seek their dens,
not losing their rhythm.
The parted woman, Lady Jiang,
returns from Qi.

**Huan**
Bearing shame, lacking modesty,
a face without a head.
Wasting and loss, emptiness and void—
diminishing day by day.

**Jie**
Auspicious stars illuminate the hall,
unicorns roam, phoenixes soar.
Benevolence spreads widely,
hymns of praise arise together.

**Zhongfu**
Banners and pennants,
standards raised in the outskirts.
Though there are precious pearls,
no path to deliver them.

**Shi** to **Sui**, **Lü** to **Xie**.
**Xiaoguo**
Plum blossoms bear fruit again,
the swan’s eggs descend in clusters.
With the rise of virtuous power,
the state is shaded in fortune.
**Xiaoxu** to **Li**, **Bi** to **Song**.

**Jiji**
White crows and red crows
battle in the eastern capital—
defeat and ruin bring sorrow.

**Weiji**
Gathering firewood, one finds a qilin—
the great mandate topples.
Heroes contend for fame,
the realm divides fourfold.
**Tun** to **Kun**.
**Sui**, the seventeenth.

**Sui**

Crows cry east and west,
welcoming their flock’s chorus.
Though seeming to belong,
they cannot act alone—
returning empty, solitary.

**Qian**
Nose and eyes transposed,
unable to discern fragrance from stench.
The lord, deluded by affairs,
forfeits his favored rank.

**Kun**
Tang and Yu aid one another,
birds and beasts dance in joy.
Peace and well-being reign,
the state grows rich.

**Tun**
Left and right ministers,
gold and jade fill the coffers.
Ever full, never depleted,
wealth like granaries overflowing.
*As in* **Shi** *to* **Guimei**, **Meng** *to* **Kun**.

**Meng**
An eastern dragon appears alone,
clashing with stone,
both horns broken.

**Xu**
Hooked eyes, swollen cheeks,
skilled at chasing men away.
A bride arrives without choice,
restless in her new home.

**Song**
Chasing hares, driving wolves,
shunning misfortune.
Evil flees north,
meeting good on the path.

**Shi**
Offering cowries to ransom a fox,
yet it heeds not my words.
Caught in the tiger’s whiskers,
it cannot be pulled free.
*As in* **Xu** *to* **Kui**, **Tongren** *to* **Pi**, **Pi** *to* **Ge**.

**Bi**
Riding together in the same carriage,
parting midway.
Losing my great mate,
I dwell alone.
*As in* **Bi** *to* **Ge*.

**Xiaochu**
Flapping wings, beating pinions,
bound for a blessed land.
Missing the appointed time,
yet attaining my desire.

**Lü**
Eyes askew, heart bewitched,
Lady Xia at his side.
Shen Gong in disarray,
Wu Chen sows chaos in the state.

**Tai**
Shooting turtledoves, slinging magpies,
hunting hares north of the mountain.
Pellets spent, day wanes—
nothing caught, nothing gained.

**Pi**
A deer seeks its fawn
in the tiger’s den.
Tang Bo and Li Er,
greedy, refuse me.

**Tongren**
Rotten fish in a decaying chamber,
the stench unbearable.
Treading mud on the mountain,
returning with wounded feet.

**Dayou**
A hundred branches of flowered lamps,
dispelling darkness and decline.
Essence and light exhausted,
reduced to ashes and dust.

**Qian**
Yan Shu and Zixia,
roaming the halls of benevolence.
Gentle and kind, they receive fortune,
never losing their place.

**Yu**
Beams and pillars stand firm,
descendants flourish.
Blessings and joy abound,
ending without misfortune or regret.

**Gu**
Frontiers unsettled,
people roam the wilds.
The miser succeeds,
the harvest plentiful.

**Lin**
Snails in the pool croak,
calling for my floodwaters.
Clouds and rain gather,
flowing into rivers and seas.

**Guan**
Will aligned, intent shared,
Ji and Jiang unite.
A fine match at the gate,
the lord rejoices.

**Shike**
A white horse, black-maned,
ever renewing.
A wealthy merchant,
profits piled high as hills.

**Bi**
Great Si and Yu of Xia,
opening the nine roads.
Each has its place,
the people dwell in peace.

**Bo**
Jia, Yi, Ji, and Geng,
moving with the seasons.
Unwavering in purpose,
Tang’s last scion rouses,
capturing and slaying Ziying.

**Fu**
Mu strays a hundred li,
dispatching the bright and martial.
Generals launch an assault,
defeated at Ban’s right flank.

**Wuwang**
Dwelling in reeds like wood,
harmonizing with its kind.
Yearning for the flock,
never leaving the nest.

**Daxu**
Elders and juniors,
drowsing at dusk.
Sitting, lying—sight lost,
their cowrie pouches gone.

**Yi**
Losing the sheep, mending the pen,
Zhang loses his ox.
Drunken steeds bolt,
magpies steal my fish.
*As in* **Gou** *to* **Dazhuang**.

**Daguo**
Sparrow eyes, swallow’s jaw,
fearing darkness, no light.
Longing for my cunning youth,
yet I see not Zichong.

**Kan**
Entering darkness, emerging into light,
movement and action radiant.
Turning, resting in due time,
ever joyful and secure.

**Li**
Unable to overcome private desire,
ensnared by profit.
Her chamber bears an orphan,
ruining a good family.

**Cheng**
Invoking the spirits above,
pleasing the gods.
Receiving blessings manifold,
descendants multiply in merit.

**Heng**
Qi Jiang and Shuzi,
heaven’s mandate upon them.
Shichen and Shenlu,
enfeoffed as Lord Kang.

**Dun**
Roaming without peril,
entering and exiting safely.
Ever receiving its grace,
the noble one lives ten thousand years.

**Dazhuang**
Clad in cultured virtue,
ascending the great forest.
Four gates harmonious,
receiving great fortune.

Turtledoves and crows cry,
holding fast to unity, no fault.
Within the inner chambers, order reigns,
the lord delights.

**Jin**
Bearing gold, holding jade,
returning south to a blessed land.
Wasps and fireflies do not sting,
profit enters my house.

**Mingyi**
The sun atop the mound,
facing darkness, turning to dusk.
Petty men gather,
the noble one grieves for the order.

**Jiaren**
Water and fire as parents,
first wailing in lament.
Atop the marsh’s edge,
dwelling on high.

**Kui**
The eastern neighbor’s maiden,
becomes the king’s chief wife.
Gentle, yielding, upright, and steadfast,
fitting to bear a long-lived son.

**Jian**
Wearing a pot to gaze at heaven,
unable to see the stars.
Seeking small, losing great,
fortune flees afar.
*Yuan* should read *gu*.

**Xie**
Wang Qiao free of illness,
the dog’s head unharmed.
Losing a sandal, missing a shoe,
my followers falter.

**Sun**
Sending Yan to build a house,
no shelter for himself.
The home cannot hold a carriage,
my clothes follow after.

**Yi**
Authority and power sundered,
crows wander at night.
Contending to obscure the moon’s light,
the great one punishes and wounds.
*As in* **Jiaren** *to* **Wuwang**.

**Guai**
Distinguishing white from black,
clever words disrupt the state.
The great one loses fortune,
the noble one is bewildered.

**Gou**
Armor of leather and metal,
a broken basket for tools.
The great one pays no heed,
the young maiden does not take it,
discarding it by the road.

**Cui**
Swallows and doves bear mud in their beaks,
hatching and nurturing their young.
Six brothers in harmony,
bound by fraternal love and filial piety.
Their hearts rejoice,
delighting in one another’s joy.
*As in* **Xiaoxu** *to* **Xun**.

**Sheng**
Ascending the steps, mounting the carriage,
driving a team of four southward.
Alliances formed, rivalries dissolved,
Yan and Qin grow strong.

**Kun**
Dark and clamorous,
enmity and misfortune converge.
Ice enters a chamber of coals,
melting ceaselessly away.

**Jing**
Crows and magpies shatter the axe,
the state’s people face peril.
Yet by their loyal virtue,
misfortune turns to fortune,
and danger is restored to stability.

**Ge**
Carrying gold to trade for dogs,
profit flees and abandons me.
Hiding in deep pools and channels,
the sea and lakes bring calamity.

**Ding**
The deep pit levels again,
the cave’s dwelling finds peace.
Anxieties dissolve,
relying on fortune for long life.

**Zhen**
Li Ji slanders with deceit,
conspiring with two wicked sons.
She praises my humble child,
murdering the loyal and filial.
Driven forth from the gate of joy,
the Lord of Shang meets harm.

**Gen**
The butchered sheep is misplaced,
blood scant, no broth remains.
A woman holds an empty basket,
unable to gather mulberry leaves.

**Jian**
Tending sheep in the rice fields,
he hears the tiger’s roar.
Trembling with fear,
yet in the end, no disaster befalls.

**Guimei**
Luminous virtue hides,
the qilin and phoenix retreat afar.
The House of Zhou totters,
nowhere to find rest.

**Feng**
My neighbor turns away,
seeking treasures and jade.
My body bears scabs and sores—
who would seek my favor?

**Lü**
At first, no carriage,
but later, one is obtained.
By good fortune,
escaping war and strife.

**Xun**
Water breaches my village,
converging into a sea.
The tortoise and turtle fear the clamor,
unable to glimpse the Queen Mother.

**Dui**
Two hearts at odds,
one east, one west.
Though the beginning and end are clear,
none know which path to follow.

**Huan**
The Heavenly Emperor’s chariot hangs idle,
rites abandoned, no court held.
Robes are plundered, no order remains,
his house loses favor.

**Jie**
Rivers and seas converge,
distant marshes are hard to dwell in.
Water and earth differ,
longing for my august ancestor.

**Zhongfu**
Goujian’s peril,
exiled to Kuaiji.
The Grand Steward’s reproachful words
restore the state of Yue.

**Xiaoguo**
The kind crow and turtledove,
holding fast to one, no fault.
Within the inner chambers, all is well—
the noble one rejoices.

**Jiji**
A wealthy widow in her youth,
lives alone, bereft.
Cocks crow, dogs bark—
none dare inquire.
My life meets no fortune,
I alone endure cold and suffering.

**Weiji**
Rivers and seas change their garb,
drowning in excess, unfathomable.
High ranks collapse,
favor and emolument reverse.

**Gu Eighteenth**
**Gu Fang**
Born by Jiang and Huai,
one spin becomes a hundred.
Flowing through the four directions,
no evil or harm befalls.

**Qian**
Head and eyes anointed with dew,
bearing blessings and fortune.
I possess fine wine,
welcoming the good with it.

**Kun**
Tattered banners and pennants,
year’s end worn and frayed.
Favor and fame cast aside,
the lord declines in power.

**Zhun**
Chopsticks block the sun,
shielding the king’s gaze.
The marshal is unworthy,
Pingzi meets harm.

**Meng**
Home lies at the sea’s edge,
circling the whirling currents.
The prince travels alone,
no reckless pursuit follows.
Frost seals the cold,
perpetual ice unwarmed.
Later, miscarriage befalls,
great hail brings ruin.

**Xu**
Upholding justice, grasping virtue,
no peril, no danger.
Stretching the neck, lingering—
secure within his walls.
Though depletion lingers,
in the end, no great sorrow.

**Song**
A long tongue disrupts the state,
axes lost, chariots broken.
Yin and yang out of order,
Ji and Jiang decline in sorrow.

**Shi**
Two share the road,
bound westward together.
A thousand *li* apart,
they know not each other’s place.

**Bi**
Sight dimmed, unclear,
clouds veil the sun’s light.
Zidu unseen,
the people of Zheng grieve.

**Xiaoxu**
First sorrow, then joy,
trading for fortune.
Eight rows of dancers arrayed,
feasting with noble friends.

**Lü**
A young maid sleeps alone,
the eldest daughter unwed—
no profit to be gained.

**Tai**
Darkness seals the four bounds,
the yin female plots in hiding.
They call to my walls and roof,
recognized by the shamans.

**Pi Zhong**
The year withers in decay,
ever fearing decline.
Yet age regains blessing,
the fifth brother becomes minister.

**Tongren**
Bo Shi slaughters the ox,
acting against heaven’s time.
The altar of Bo is razed,
Chaoge reduced to ruins.

**Dayou**
Days grow short, nights long,
fortune and fate dim.
Early parted from father and brother,
the hare meets sorrow.

**Qian**
Gathering *tang* in the deep village,
casting for trysts in the mulberry groves.
Lost in heart, failing to meet—
anxious thoughts weigh heavy.

**Yu**
Blind sight, no light,
night reveals no brightness.
Groping an empty bed,
the youngest flees in exile.

**Sui**
Lifting the foot, shaking the wings,
south to the blessed land.
I meet my elder aunt,
harmony and kindness unite.

**Lin**
Following heaven, obeying time,
wandering its ruins.
Dwelling with joy,
no fault or sorrow.

**Guan**
A tower’s door, a wasp’s nest,
stinging my hands and feet.
No advance to be made—
it brings me harm and blame.

**Shike**
Gongsun rides a black steed,
traveling to Qi in haste.
Yanling delights in his estate,
bequeathing fine robes to Ji.

**Ben**
Turning to Mount Li,
greatly losing the original heart.
Liu Ji rages,
commanding the death of Ziying.

**Bo**
The sheep’s intestines wind ninefold,
pushing forward step by step.
Only when the prince halts
does he ascend to heaven.

**Fu**
Wax and tallow fill the side,
flatterers deceive and confuse.
Women’s petitions run rampant,
the right path blocked.

**Wuwang**
Fortune and emolument do not follow,
the household plagued by strange omens.
The elk and deer wail in the third, ninth, and fourth months,
longing for their great stag.

**Daxu**
Clouds and thunder accumulate,
heavy rains layer upon layer.
Long without the sun,
it saddens my heart.

**Yi**
The Three Rivers converge,
waters surge in fury.
They ruin my royal house,
the people starve, without food.

**Daguo**
Traveling at dawn in the rain,
arriving early at the capital.
Rebirth overturns collapse—
in the end, nothing is achieved.
Three heads, two eyes,
yet the truth remains unseen.

**Kan**
Bao Si gives birth to a snake,
Jing grows old and weak.
Duke Ai stumbles,
drunk on wine, ensnared by Huang Li.

**Li**
Wild geese fly south,
following the sun’s warmth.
Conveying heaven’s harmony,
a thousand *li* without pause.

**Xian**
Missing the time, losing advantage,
desires unfulfilled.

**Heng**
The heart holds much regret,
words spoken turn strange.
An owl cries in the northern chamber—
its voice foul, detestable.
Petitions denied.

**You**
Four horses pass like a crack,
time lost cannot be regained.
Confucius, the sage,
struck yet unfed.

**Dazhuang**
Yin transforms into yang,
a woman becomes a man.
The governance Dao flows freely,
lord and minister succeed one another.

**Jin**
Kunlun’s source-mouth,
flowing without cease.
Gun and Yi buttress the pillar,
the people find no peace.
The mother returns to aid her child,
the yellow muntjac rejoices.

**Mingyi**
Ge and Jing entangled in thorns,
blossoms bear no fruit.
Slander and flattery disrupt governance,
blocking the path of grace.

**Jiaren**
The duke must not drive too far,
the Celestial King’s horse balks.
Where it ought not tread,
injury and fracture bring misfortune.

**Kui**
The great granary overflows,
the myriad things flourish,
the harvest year ripens in glory.
Holding the reed-pipe to light the sacrifice,
it is blown by the wind.
The fire dies, no light remains—
black and yellow fade from sight.

**Xie**
The crow returns to its old nest,
home to its chamber.
Heart level, intent upright,
it calls in harmony with its kin.
Ascending high, it falls—
losing favor and rank.

**Sun**
The crossbow unstrung, the bow put away,
the good hound is not boiled.
Within, no resentful maiden;
the decisive strike waits in the hall.

**Yi**
The sacrificial ox vast and broad,
its virtue daily renewed.
The cultured lord goes hunting,
Jiang receives the blessing.

**Guai**
Autumn’s first month, winter’s onset,
cold dew descends as frost.
Great yin fills the courtyard,
the common things do not grow.
Cocks crow, dogs bark—
the household’s worries multiply in alarm.

**Gou**
Heart full of regret and resentment,
stepping out to see omens.
A three-legged snake slithers back,
its voice foul and detestable.
A blind mother acts as matchmaker—
the request is denied.

**Cui**
Tigers and leopards vie in strength,
the Dao is blocked, impassable.
Petty men fear litigation,
usurping heaven’s merit.

**Sheng**
The chicken pecks at grain,
pursued by the fox.
It flees, unable to eat—
trembling in terror, panting in fear.

**Kun**
Chen Mao and Jing Zhong,
an omen heralds the rise of Qi and Jiang.
They journey to Yingqiu—
eight generations flourish greatly.

**Jing**
The bright sun of heaven
shines upon our land.
The ten thousand people at peace,
all rely on joyous fortune.

**Ge**
Cloud Dream’s great marsh,
where the hunt finds its quarry.
The gamekeepers share their duty,
the black colt delights in joy.

**Ding**
River deer, pheasants, hares,
gathered in the eastern state.
Reed-yellow, white-backed,
all pursue the chase.
Nine in ten captured—
the lord rejoices.

**Zhen**
Virtue and kindness vast and bright,
the lord restores his rule,
securing his hall and chamber.

**Gen**
What heaven has broken,
none can forcibly sustain.
The clamor of many mouths—
though noble, one is surely imperiled.

**Jian**
Heaven’s hidden corner,
where Yao and Shun dwelled.
One may preserve the body whole,
safeguarding our state and home.

**Guimei**
The lower spring, thick with reeds,
nine rulers in ten years.
Xun Bo meets his time,
anxious for the Zhou capital.

**Feng**
The Jiang, Huai, and sea’s edge,
where the people’s profits gather.
One may roam at ease—
the year’s end brings no care.

**Lü**
South Mountain’s yellow bamboo,
three bodies, six eyes.
Issuing commands, governing,
the august sovereign proclaims decrees.
The lord is honored, the ruler secure—
Zheng knows no trouble.

**Xun**
Tribute of rare herbs through many translators,
coming to dispel our woes.
Joy and happiness dwell together,
sharing in their blessed fortune.

**Dui**
South Mountain’s high ridge,
the qilin and phoenix in the hall.
Embracing harmony, treading the center—
the state suffers no calamity.

**Huan**
Purple mushrooms and vermilion grasses,
growing with harmonious qi.
The ancestral spirit partakes in the feast—
fortune and emolument descend.

**Jie**
The office complete, the chamber finished,
advancing with music and dance.
The talented and wise in the hall—
fortune and emolument shine brightly.

**Zhongfu**
The Shang’s descendants,
without means to sustain themselves.
Chasing foxes for their pelts,
lingering in the marketplace.
Returning the axle to the inner village—
what harm in joy?

**Xiaoguo**
Holding the scepter, entering court,
presenting the fox-fur robe.
The great general brings peace,
the deserts tremble in fear.

**Jiji**
Gushing springs, surging ceaselessly,
flowing south without end.
Breaching to form the Huai and sea,
ruining towns and villages—
no place for the household to dwell.

**Weiji**
Solid yin, bitter cold,
perpetual ice never warms.
The indolent and lazy suffer,
great hail brings disaster.

**Lin (Nineteenth Hexagram)**
**Lin**
West of the Weak Waters,
there is the Queen Mother of the West.
Born without knowing age,
she endures with heaven.
The traveler rests in peril,
the settled dweller rejoices in goodness.

**Qian**
The yellow furnace bears a child,
which itself becomes the mother.
The Jin army camps outside the capital—
Duke Yu flees.

**Kun**
In haste, bearing the mission,
Zhongshan’s filial piety.

**Wenhou Rejoices**
Wenhou rejoices in delight,
striking the drum to summon Zizheng.

**Zhun**
Mechanisms awry, words fail to emerge.
Sincerity blocked, wronged by others.

**Meng**
White cogon grass, sweet wine,
the spirit-medium bows in prayer.
The gods relish the feast,
granting the lord longevity.

**Xu**
Four pupils, four breasts,
eyes keen and ears sharp.
Universally benevolent, a paragon of sageliness,
appointed as chief minister.

**Song**
Floods rise, no boat in sight,
breaching the city, collapsing the dikes.
The great army marches forth,
perishing in a single dawn—
his young wife never seen again.

**Shi**
Six men journey together,
each losing their sack.
The swan goose drops its pearl,
left with no light.

**Bi**
Moving with the times, turning in accord,
never losing constancy.
Each delights in their kind,
the self free from misfortune.

**Xiaoxu**
The Cai woman rocks the boat,
bringing the state worry and grief.
The Bao consort at his side,
shielding the king’s eyes—
the six livestock wither early.

**Lü**
Riding dragons, mounting tigers,
traversing all under heaven.
As envoy of the divine,
he meets the Queen Mother of the West,
no peril or danger to fear.

**Tai**
The grievances of Xuhao,
all schemes sealed in silence.
Whipping to pacify Jing,
eradicating great calamity.
Terror shakes the enemy state—
at dawn, he returns to receive the highest rank.

**Pi**
The thatched hut of Tangyi,
where the people of Jin reside.
Yu Shu receives fortune,
Huang Shen rules the land—
generations abide in joy.

**Tongren**
Guan and Bao know each other,
their perfect virtue never parted.
Three words to Huan,
and the state of Qi finds peace.

**Dayou**
Thirty years without a home,
the eldest daughter sleeps alone.
Her heart toils in vain,
grief lodged in her breast.

**Qian**
Scattered and dispersed, the waters swell,
winds blow toward my homeland.
Fire extinguished, no light—
Duke Huan’s heart undone.

**Yu**
Maggots fly, worms writhe,
each finds its mate.
Great and small protect one another,
all secure in their place.

**Sui**
Peace and ease at the feast,
yet the Jade Gate remains uncrossed.

**Gu**
Great calamity arises,
the lower lands choked with misfortune,
plunging my state into chaos.

**Guan**
Living without end,
descendants number a thousand, a hundred million.
The catalpa pillar bears the beam,
firm and unshaken.

**Shihe**
Revering august Heaven,
charting the stars’ paths.
Fitting to bestow the seasons upon the people,
harmonizing yin and yang.

**Bi**
The Three Rivers converge,
waters surge in fury.
They ruin our royal house,
the people starve.

**Bo**
Longevity like Peng and Wang,
peer to sun and moon.
Ever at peace and joyful,
no parting from fortune or woe.

**Fu**
What Heaven bestows,
blessings and prosperity ever present,
no fear of peril.

**Wuwang**
Receiving the six talismans,
the chamber of illusions lies empty.
Though lost, no sorrow—
my wealth remains whole.

**Daxu**
Seeking gold to buy a carriage,
losing the Way, missing the time.
Exhausted and weary, beset by care—
my heart finds rest.

**Yi**
At the peak of Mount Huashou,
where immortals wander.
Favorable for dwelling,
long free from misfortune.

**Daguo**
Gathering mallow in Moixiang,
trysting in the mulberry grove.
Faith broken, no meeting—
grief tightens like a sash.

**Kan**
A face with nine mouths,
a long tongue like an axe.
Severing the coral branches,
the Yin Shang line cut short.

**Li**
By the stream, the bridge ails,
though fearful, no danger—
merriment in laughter and song.

**Xian**
Surging, seething waters,
springs turned to harm,
leaving me with no recourse.

**Heng**
Locusts and caterpillars as thieves,
ravaging my crops.
Autumn’s harvest meager,
farmers’ tables bare.

**Guo**
Eight hundred lords,
unsummoned, arrive as one.
Admiring the virtue of the western Wen,
reviving my clan—
the household harmonious.

**Dazhuang**
Eldest son and youngest daughter,
facing each other in laughter.
Bringing joy and fortune,
harmony and delight.

**Jin**
A state without a lord,
the Xia clan stirs rebellion.
The raven’s cry steals forth,
Duke Ling meets his end.

**Mingyi**
Spring’s rich rains,
summer’s abundant moisture.
Crops ripen in the fields,
a hundred bushels per acre.

**Jiaren**
A guest lodges in the cold,
the mat thin, no ease.
The journey fraught with peril,
no joy in lingering.

**Kui**
Riding a raft across the sea,
though fearful, no danger.
The mother carries her child—
what misfortune in the end?

**Jian**
Hands clumsy, unfit,
unable to fell the sandalwood.
The cart lacks axle and shaft,
travelers suffer hardship.

**Xie**
Tang and Yu aid each other,
birds and beasts dance in step.
The people at peace, no strife,
the state prosperous.

**Sun**
The autumn snake seeks its den,
never losing its rhythm.
The resolute Lady Jiang,
from Qi returns to her heart.

**Yi**
Illness grave, beyond cure,
harmony cannot heal.
Life ends, forever stilled—
below, the thatched hut.

**Guai**
Green flies swarm like clouds,
city gates sealed tight.
The lord defends and guards,
the people plagued by woe.

**Gou**
Teeth sprout from gums,
the hall’s doors open wide.
The secluded one finds good fortune,
beating wings in dance.

**Cui**
Sailing the rivers and seas,
a journey of a thousand li.
Thought lost to death,
yet seen again in Kongsang—
a land of joy and long life.

**Sheng**
The Yellow Emperor sets forth,
riding dragons, mounting phoenixes.
East to Mount Tai,
south to Qi and Lu—
all states rejoice.

**Kun**
Treading peril without cease,
facing ghosts eye to eye.
Terrified, qi scattered,
like treading a tiger’s tail.

**Jing**
Autumn south, spring north,
never missing the signs.
Wading through harmony, treading the center,
no time for concealment.

**Ge**
Dragon Gate, Mount Dizhu,
dredging the waterways.

All rivers flow in harmony,
the people dwell in peace.

**Ding**
A thousand-year-old temple hall,
its beams bent, pillars collapsed.
Heaven rejects the Zhou’s virtue,
its favor and glory lost.

**Zhen**
Chopsticks block the eyes,
young Shu unseen.
A five-foot orphaned crow,
far from home and kin.

**Gen**
Gazing north toward Shu Mountain,
ridges bar my sight.
What I seek remains unseen,
leaving my heart perplexed.

**Jian**
The gourd’s offspring,
one *mu* yields ten households.
In the capital of ten thousand states,
the northern gate brings fortune.

**Guimei**
Anxious and restless,
misfortune ever near.
Mountains divide us,
households scattered apart.

**Feng**
The qilin flicks its ears,
grazing on duckweed,
roaming Stone Gate,
up and down the mountain’s slope.

**Lü**
Heaven blesses prosperity,
culture makes it flourish.
The martial king is born in abundance,
the Ji clan receives its fortune.

**Xun**
The sheep’s gut path winds ninefold,
pushing forward step by step.
Only the king’s grandson may halt,
for he alone ascends to heaven.
*(Gu’s Bo)*

**Dui**
A destitute ghost guards the gate,
daily shattering my pots.
The lone mare bears no foal,
the hen hatches no chick.

**Huan**
Well-fed and at ease,
entering the gate, ascending the hall.
Unfailing in routine,
the household suffers no misfortune.

**Jie**
Yin’s excess knows no end,
the white horse becomes the sea.
The marshland’s child,
seeks high ground to dwell.

**Zhongfu**
Standing with spears at the ready,
prepared for sudden violence.
A thousand men lift the dragon,
from peril to the sea—
what fear remains in the end?

**Xiaoguo**
Breaching the river to wed,
waters rise, no boat in sight.
Hope fades in pursuit,
the joyful lord unseen.

**Jiji**
Yin and yang transform,
each finds its proper place.
Above and below in harmony,
accomplishment is complete.

**Weiji**
Wild and weak, virtue meager,
servants and concubines lost.
Fields yield no game,
hounds catch nothing.

**#38** *"Wei"* (維), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Jie"* (結).
**#39** The original text reads *"Ying"* (盈); amended to *"Gu"* (蛊) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#40** Originally *"Ge"* (各); corrected to *"Dong"* (冬) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#41** Originally *"Huo"* (货); amended to *"Dai"* (贷) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#42** Originally *"Gou’ou"* (苟耦); corrected to *"Sunwang"* (笋网) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#43** Originally *"Zhun"* (屯); amended to *"Bi"* (比) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#44** Originally *"Zhen"* (震); corrected to *"Kui"* (睽) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#45** Originally *"She"* (社); amended to *"Mu"* (牡) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#46** The original omits *"Qu lao cheng ma"* (去老乘马) after *"Jie"* (解); restored per *Baizi Quanshu*. In the *"Cui"* (萃) hexagram’s forest of verses, *"Jia"* (甲) was originally *"Shen"* (申); corrected per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#47** Originally *"Xihan"* (西寒); amended to *"Sisai"* (四塞) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#48** Originally *"Zuo"* (柞); corrected to *"Chu"* (杵) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#49** Originally *"Yu"* (于); amended to *"Zi"* (子) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#50** *"Huo"* (火), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Shui"* (水).
**#51** Originally *"Han"* (汗); corrected to *"Wu"* (污) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#52** Originally *"Mei"* (昧); amended to *"Mei"* (妹) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#53** Originally *"Guan"* (观); corrected to *"Feng"* (丰) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#54** *"Xiang"* (祥), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Pan"* (胖).
**#55** The original omits *"Pi zhi Huan"* (否之涣) after *"Xi"* (喜); restored per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#56** Originally *"Dong"* (冬); amended to *"Jin"* (尽) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#57** Originally *"Hun"* (珲); corrected to *"Chan"* (婵) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#58** *"Yunming"* (允明), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Mingyun"* (明允).
**#59** *"Shi"* (识), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Cheng"* (诚).
**#60** Originally *"Lou"* (漏); amended to *"Yong"* (涌) per *Baizi Quanshu*. Below, *"Ji"* (悸) was originally *"Bei"* (悖); corrected per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#61** Originally *"Que"* (鹊); amended to *"Hu"* (扈) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#62** Originally *"Shu"* (束); corrected to *"Su"* (粟) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#63** *"Luan"* (乱), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Kong"* (孔).
**#64** *"Shi"* (食), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Liang"* (粮).
**#65** The character originally read *"Dundun"* (蹲蹲); corrected to *"Dundun"* (蹲蹲) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#66** *"Jingfen"* (精愤), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Jifen"* (积愤); should be *"Fenfen"* (愤愤).
**#67** *"Ju"* (惧), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Huai"* (怀).
**#68** Originally *"Bao"* (胞); amended to *"Xiong"* (胸) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#69** Originally *"Hua"* (猾); corrected to *"Wei"* (谓) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#70** *"Yang"* (洋), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Ping"* (平).
**#71** Originally *"Ju"* (具); amended to *"Qi"* (其) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#72** Originally *"Ren"* (人); corrected to *"Ru"* (入) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#73** *"Lü"* (履), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Fu"* (覆).
**#74** *"Heng"* (亨), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Peng"* (烹).
**#75** Originally *"Heng"* (亨); amended to *"Xiang"* (享) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#76** According to the *"Tai zhi Lü"* (泰之履) forest of verses, *"Ji shan you zheng"* (积善有征) should follow *"Huo"* (火); this is likely an omission here.
**#77** Originally *"Wei"* (为); corrected to *"Wu"* (无) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#78** *"Yu Guai"* (与夬), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Tian yu"* (天与).
**#79** The original omits *"Tai zhi Lü"* (泰之履) after *"Kang"* (康); restored per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#80** The original omits *"Pi zhi Wuwang, Kun zhi Weiji"* (否之无妄、坤之未济) after *"Ming"* (明); restored per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#81** Originally *"Guai"* (夬); amended to *"Tai"* (太) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#82** The original omits *"Xu zhi Meng"* (需之蒙) after *"Guo"* (国); restored per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#83** *"Yang"* (杨), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Yang"* (阳).
**#84** The original omits *"Sheng"* (圣) after *"Kong"* (孔); restored per *Baizi Quanshu*. In the *"Yi"* (颐) hexagram’s forest of verses, *"Xi"* (徙) was originally *"Tu"* (徒); corrected per *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#85** *"Yi"* (衣), in *Baizi Quanshu* as *"Chui"* (垂).
**#86** Originally *"Ban"* (板); amended to *"Ji"* (圾) per *Baizi Quanshu*.
