Her noble husband, her long-lived son,
her mother honored across the four seas.

**Gu (蠱):**
Virtue spreads to the eight wilds,
the southern barbarians submit in droves.
No scorpions stir,
the Way knows no harsh malice.

**Lin (臨):**
Bearing the sun’s radiance,
its six dragons harnessed in harness.
Fate and fortune reach the heavens,
enfeoffed as King of Yan.

**Guan (觀):**
Collar tight, neck drawn in,
unable to move forward.
Five stones reveal their portent—
Xiang Bo’s plans come to naught.

**Shi He (噬嗑):**
The serpent returns to its den,
hemp worn in mourning.
Once grief and weeping arise,
death is sent off from home.

**Bi (賁):**
On all four sides, unrest,
weapons and war bring disaster.
They plunder our wives and children,
guests left hungry and cold.

**Bo (剝):**
Riding the wind, Yu’s bridge,
soaring with the flying birds.
A single flight of a thousand li,
to see my beloved mother.

**Fu (復):**
Struck by thunder and lightning,
the five traitors are executed.
Utterly annihilated, no bounds,
fear only subsides now.

**Jian (蹇):**
Zhang offers wine,
seeking audience with the court.
The king withers in decay,
alone, he gains no favor.

**Da Xu (大畜):**
Seated, they quarrel and litigate,
clamoring in chaos.
At last, calamity erupts,
disaster strikes the lord’s house.

**Yi (頤):**
Frost falls on doors and windows,
creeping insects hide away.
Never seeing sun or moon,
they join the ranks of the dead.

**Da Guo (大過):**
Rats gather, breeding strangeness,
bringing me regret and woe.
The Way is cut off, impassable,
merchants and travelers lose their way.

**Kan (坎):**
Cold and heat misaligned,
the celestial measures awry.
One ahead, one behind—
years of scarcity abound.

**Li (離):**
Building a house upon the water,
perched on a single tooth’s edge.
If Chou and Yin do not move,
Chen and Mao will meet misfortune.

**Xian (咸):**
Raising chickens, keeping dogs,
their growth abundant, stores full.
Plowing fields to yield millet,
the mistress dances with joy.

**Heng (恒):**
A glimmer from the bound jade,
yet its count dims, unclear.
The mistress, jealous and grasping,
disrupts my undertakings.

**Dun (遯):**
Hard and soft clash,
fire melts metal away.
The osprey seizes the hare,
attacking Chu brings merit.

**Jin (晉):**
The state of Zheng, rife with slander,
repeatedly plagued by Chu’s woes.
Conscripted men grieve in bitterness,
the people languish in despair.
A hundred and three pigs run,
battling at the tiger’s maw.
The white boar fails to prevail,
dying beneath the pit.

**Ming Yi (明夷):**
Bow and arrow drawn taut,
the sling’s string snaps.
The pellet never flies—
on the road, harm befalls.

**Jia Ren (家人):**
Raising the goblet to drink,
the wine never reaches his lips.
Cast aside in drunken rage,
he draws his sword in fury—
Marquis Wu rues his actions.

**Kui (睽):**
Azure hawks flock together,
traveling in ranks ahead.
Prince Sun, Duke Shen,
startled, seize my male.
The northern gate of heaven opens,
divine fire brings flying disaster.
If reverence and trust are lacking,
affairs crumble to dust.

**Jian (蹇):**
Breaching the house brings profit,
doubling my gain to the north.
Following crooked, deceptive paths,
the welcome cannot be found.
Gazing north and south toward the city,
at last, I return within.

**Xie (解):**
Longevity like Peng and Wang,
living as long as sun and moon.
Ever at peace, ever joyful,
never parted from woe.

**Sun (損):**
Stepping out to look eastward,
elder and younger brothers do not come.
Illness and suffering afflict,
causing the mother to sigh in sorrow.

**Yi (益):**
The granddaughter of Tai Ji,
the nine sons of King Wen.
All receive their due,
honored, noble, and rich.

**Guài (夬):**
Peach and plum blossom like treasures,
their radiance swells with the sun.
Growing tall and ripening,
sweet and fine to taste—
bringing me profit and fortune.

**Gòu (姤):**
Marriage rites unclear,
men and women lose their norms.
Wayfarers speak ill,
stirring disputes against me.

**Cuì (萃):**
Holes pierced, leaks unstopped,
broken beams and shattered tiles.
Yin cannot mend them—
shards lie incomplete,
a house built on doubt.

**Shēng (升):**
Numbers exhausted, vast and empty,
trapped in a cramped chamber.
Yet climbing the jade hall,
I dine with the aged.

**Kùn (困):**
The Way is damp, forming pits,
wheels sink and stall.
The southern lands harbor taboos,
filling me with dread.

**Jǐng (井):**
Widowed, orphaned, solitary,
blessed with meager fortune.
Entering the house without a wife,
my child’s grief knows no end.

**Gé (革):**
Sleeves raised to cover my eyes,
I see neither sun nor moon.
Robes draped, staff in hand,
I retire to my night chamber.

**Dǐng (鼎):**
Long-tailed and stunted,
drawing rivers on the ground.
Too deep to cross,
cut off from the world’s likeness—
I sigh in sorrow.

**Zhèn (震):**
Morning winds and patterned wings,
soaring toward warmth.
Passing dimly through my town,
Yì finds nothing to seize.

**Gèn (艮):**
Coming and going in season,
south and north hold no care.
Hastening after my pursuit,
I return from afar.

**Jiàn (漸):**
Yang’s madness spreads,
Jisun’s order collapses.
Ministers seize power,
Pingzi is broken—
Jixin’s heart knows no joy.

**Guī Mèi (归妹):**
Five crows and six ravens
perch facing one another.
Courtesy and yielding forgotten,
Yu and Ran vie in dispute.

**Fēng (丰):**
Longing for my kin,
separated in the east.
Suffering floods and overflow,
rivers and streams burst their banks.
Fortune spares me—
I return alive to my home.

**Lǚ (旅):**
Chasing game to the east,
a hare darts behind me.
My blade dulls,
empty-handed I remain.

**Xùn (巽):**
Dogs bark at their masters,
chaos reigns above and below.
Enemies launch their assault—
King Min flees in flight.

**Duì (兑):**
Song Gao and Dai Zong,
towering, upright, and divine.
Striking stone, moisture gathers—
a thousand li receive its grace.

**Huàn (涣):**
Watching fish at Chen’s shrine,
wolves and tigers prowl.
Opening paths for the people,
they lose their ancestors’ legacy.

**Jié (节):**
Four walls without doors,
three steps and I halt.
East, west, south, north—
profit cannot be found.

**Zhōng Fú (中孚):**
Seeking the lord’s robes,
desire burns uncontrollable.
Offending taboos in the west,
the elder meets misfortune.
Yet the lord’s peace above
brings safekeeping.

**Xiǎo Guò (小过):**
Spring swans fly east,
trading horses for gold—
profit lies within reach.

**Jì Jì (既济):**
Worms bore into the grain,
turning back to devour it—
I gain nothing.

**Wèi Jì (未济):**
Jie’s chaos knows no Dao,
the people scatter, ungathered.
Those who abandon their homes
flee in threes and fives.

---

**Jìn (晋) Thirty-Five:**
**Jìn (晋):**
Forging plowshares from blades,
resting oxen, releasing horses.
Armor and weapons laid aside,
husband and wife keep one another.

**Qián (乾):**
One robe, three crowns—
the crowns find no place.
Clothing incomplete,
bringing disaster upon myself.

**Kūn (坤):**
A hundred legs move as one,
strength in mutual support.
Three sages aid the cause—
the royal house shines in favor.

**Zhūn (屯):**
Fish and serpent omens
fill the great with dread.
The lord of Liang loves walls—
he loses his peace.

**Méng (蒙):**
Young, without strong aid,
grown, without a mother.
A heart laboring in distant thought,
grieving in sorrow.

**Xū (需):**
No shelter from the heat ahead,
no profit to be taken.
Two li from the market gate,
my trade is ruined.
Old ox, sick horse—
what regret in letting them go?

**Sòng (讼):**
The lord is bright in virtue,
ascending to great fortune.
Enacting policies, bestowing kindness,
he completes his grace.
The middle son journeys south,
soaring yet unreturned.

**Shī (师):**
Responding with reverent assent,
honoring the honored guest.
Holding fast to respect, dispelling harm,
warding off regret to bring fortune.

**Bǐ (比):**
Millet, grain, and rice
hang heavy, nearly ripe.
Mid-drought, no rain—
wind harms the healing herbs.

**Xiǎo Xù (小畜):**
Three lean, six spent,
unable to rise.
The eastern merchant loses his horse,
toiling back and forth.

**Lǚ (履):**
Leaning, gazing toward one another,
adjusting robes in preparation.

Dark clouds veil the sun,
a violent rain descends in torrents.
The roads are blocked,
our joyous meeting thwarted.

**Tài (泰):**
Long legs stride swiftly,
shoulders gladly bear the load.
A thousand *li* a day—
the merchant’s market reaps reward.

**Pǐ (否):**
The north wind brings bitter cold,
rain and snow congeal to ice.
Worry and sorrow weigh heavy,
a single sigh stirs grief in the heart.

**Tóng Rén (同人):**
Though the turtledove is but a dove,
holding fast to the One, it bears no fault.
Order reigns within the inner chambers—
the noble one delights in joy.

**Dà Yǒu (大有):**
The wind sighs through dew-drenched jades,
the noble one basks in radiant favor.
Phoenix bells chime in harmony—
fortune and blessing arrive as one.

**Qiān (谦):**
Journeying south in search of blessing,
one meets with joy and good fortune.
Receiving enfeoffment and highest reward,
one stands as a tripod leg to aid the state.
*(Same as Héng in the hexagram Xián.)*

**Yù (豫):**
Mulberry blossoms rot and bore,
clothes fray like tangled hemp.
Women’s work remains undone—
silk and cloth turn to jade.

**Suí (随):**
Left and right exchange places,
Wang Liang’s heart rejoices.
Joy and profit follow him.

**Gǔ (蛊):**
Long life unmarred by forgetfulness,
four steeds harnessed in perfect order.
Three journeys to Chen and Song,
southward trade with Chu and Jing.
Profit grows ever greater.

**Lǚ (旅):**
The traveler’s body wearies,
fearing day yet welcoming night.

**Lín (临):**
Lambskin cap and courtly robes—
the noble one dons his regalia.
Assisting in governance, upholding virtue,
he unites the myriad states.

**Guān (观):**
The turtledove moves its nest,
westward to Pingzhou.
Struck by thunder and lightning,
it shatters reeds and rushes.
The household suffers hunger and cold,
longing for the days of old.
*(“全” should read “我.”)*
*(Same as Suí in the hexagram Xián.)*

**Shì Kè (噬嗑):**
A tail large and head small,
so heavy it cannot be shaken.
Above weak and below strong,
yin restrains its female.
*(Same as Kǎn in the hexagram Xián.)*
The female acts as male.

**Bì (贲):**
Feet unshackled, shoulders at rest,
yet wary of peril and hardship.
Bronze walls and iron gates,
with bastions for self-defense.
At ease in heart, free from harm.

**Bō (剥):**
Heaven’s decree: the dark bird
descends to give birth to Great Shang.
Establishing bounds on all four sides,
its rule endures for long ages.

**Fù (复):**
Taxes levied thick and frequent,
governance preys upon the people.
The loom’s beam lies empty—
I depart from that house.

**Jiǎn (蹇):**
Yin and yang sundered and blocked,
betrothal promised yet delayed.
The mound of Wanqiu, the new terrace—
regret and sighs for what has passed.

**Dà Xù (大畜):**
Longing to ascend the heights,
the mind ever seeks escape.
Jia’s bitterness, Chou’s ugliness—
the wife finds no peace with her husband.

**Yí (颐):**
Tiptoeing, peering in secret,
fearing discovery and flight.
Hiding in concealment,
finding profit only by night.

**Dà Guò (大过):**
Trustworthy, keen, reverent, humble,
honoring ghosts and revering spirits.
The Five Peaks and Four Rivers
satisfy the Emperor’s heart,
bringing blessed longevity.

**Kǎn (坎):**
Far south at sea, suspended in longing,
ten thousand *li* from home.
The flying hare, the owl with a broken waist—
one day reunited with its mother,
my gloom and sorrow dispelled.

**Lí (离):**
Though soiled, not disgraced—
why grind down the feet?
A child’s hem hiked up,
five steps and all is well.

**Xián (咸):**
The palace walls stand in sight,
robes stitched with jagged seams.
Reverent and cautious in self-defense,
no misfortune or blame befalls.

**Héng (恒):**
Bamboo traps set in the beams,
yet no fish are caught.
Gazing a thousand *li* for food,
arriving only to emptiness.

**Dùn (遁):**
A colt from a thousand *li* away,
harnessed to the king’s chariot.
Admired for its black mane’s splendor,
the noble one achieves success.

**Dà Zhuàng (大壮):**
Tripod legs uphold virtue,
auspicious plans engender fortune.
Opening court for the king,
all desires are fulfilled.

**Míng Yí (明夷):**
The right hand finds no match,
the left finger breaks alone.
Yu and Tang lose their thrones,
their deeds and merit unfulfilled.

**Jiā Rén (家人):**
Woes and misfortune compound,
perils near yet unresolved.
Heart bound west, intent east—
no success in any endeavor.

**Kuí (睽):**
Journeying east to eat elm seeds,
ensnared by withered stumps.
Husband and wife without a home,
their aspirations crushed by sorrow.

**Qiān (骞):**
The Five Classics and Six Records,
where the Way of benevolence resides.
In the first month, thick frost—
narrowly escaping blame.
*(Lí should read lí.)*

**Xiè (解):**
Slack and slow, failing to advance,
idle and losing opportunity.
The solstices’ warning—
the household knows no misfortune.
Carving wood into shapes,
hearing words yet disbelieving.
*(Shuǐ should read mù.)*

**Sǔn (损):**
Benevolence deep and sincere,
not swayed by resentment.
Harming one’s own child,
I return to my old capital,
daily growing richer.

**Yì (益):**
Broken and incomplete, the embryo unformed—
no sign or shape appears.

**Guài (夬):**
Horns snapped yet unharmed, though broken they regrow.
Virtue upheld without fault, the aged rely on its glory.

**Gòu (姤):**
Riding a raft across the sea, escaping dire straits—
though beset, no misfortune.

**Cuì (萃):**
Phoenixes and mandarin chicks, crows and swans and doves.
Soaring over the purple abyss, in the land of fine grain—
gazing at the child with joy.

**Shēng (升):**
Sweet dew, warm and moist—
all come to fulfill their wishes.
The joyful, easygoing noble one
meets no calamity or chaos.

**Kùn (困):**
The eastern rider falls, a thousand li from shelter.
Lofty shores become valleys, the yang loses its chamber.

**Jǐng (井):**
The eight talents ascend, accomplishing fine deeds.
The dragon descends to the courtyard, the land knows no disaster.

**Gé (革):**
Reversed words from Na and E—
father and elder brother bring trouble.
Plunged into sorrow and regret,
they die abroad and never return.

**Dǐng (鼎):**
Five blades blunt the jaw, granaries lie empty.
The market yields no profit, turning gain into enmity.

**Zhèn (震):**
A white bird takes the bait, calling to its young.
Wheeling, spreading its wings, it returns to its mother.

**Gèn (艮):**
Studying the numinous for three years,
sagely and spiritually enlightened.
First to perceive auspicious omens—
prosperity and abundant blessings.
A divine horse appears, announcing no cause for worry.

**Jiàn (漸):**
Clouds and vapors rise, losing their proper course.
Harming the year’s harvest, the spirit-lord’s essence.

**Guī Mèi (归妹):**
Spring plowing yields rest, autumn brings profitable fortune.
Offering fine timber and great beams, rejoicing in success.
*(Dà yí should read sī.)*

**Fēng (丰):**
A gaunt boar staggers, a tiger enters the town.
Blocking left and right, the city gates grow tense.

**Lǚ (旅):**
Journeying east to the western edge, south and north lose their way.
The traveler strays from the group, my fine robes lost.

**Xùn (巽):**
Within the household, the butcher and wife live in harmony.
The petty man rides the carriage, the carriage at the husband’s home.
The great fruit loses its keeper—
who knows what is right?

**Duì (兑):**
Early spring in the east, crossing ice with a basin.
Fearful and unsettled, yet joy endures a lifetime.

**Huàn (换):**
Wind stirs the dust, ten li without shelter.
The southern land’s harvest fails, no place to rest secure.

**Jié (节):**
Overloaded, the cart breaks; the woman lacks a husband.
Twenty (or thirty) unmarried, sitting alone in an empty hut.

**Zhōng Fú (中孚):**
A failing ox, a gaunt horse—
trading for profit brings me no joy.

**Xiǎo Guò (小过):**
The moon rises in the east, the mountain obscures its light.
Zhang Fu worries in the tower, Jizi feigns madness.

**Jì Jì (既济):**
Entering and exiting the gate, the Way opens smoothly.
Qi Liang’s trust—
the sun does not pass its zenith.
Shao Ji crosses the river, returning to his homeland—
yet illness and danger loom.

**Wèi Jì (未济):**
Dwelling in a garrisoned town, like tumbleweed in the wind—
to reside here is perilous.

---

**Míng Yí (明夷), the Thirty-Sixth:**

**Míng Yí (明夷):**
The other mountain’s stone, taken as an enemy.
Coming to attack our city, wounding our flesh—
the state and home in turmoil.

**Qián (乾):**
Treading on freezing ice, ten steps, nine stumbles.
Only bitter pain—
no cause for deeper worry.

**Kūn (坤):**
The Grand Duke fled Zhou, hiding for seventy years.
At last meeting the sagely Wen, he became the kingdom’s pillar.

**Zhūn (屯):**
The path of sun and moon—
wherever they travel, they arrive without harm or obscurity.

**Méng (蒙):**
Chanting virtue, reciting merit, fine customs flourish.
Aiding the rise of Zhou, its glory aids the humble.

**Xū (需):**
A youth without a chamber, no partner to join—
sitting alone, sleeping in solitude.

**Sòng (讼):**
Pierced nose, bound to a stump, seized by a tiger.
The Queen Mother’s incantation—
disaster does not take form, suddenly they escape.

**Shī (师):**
The Yellow Emperor, spiritually enlightened, his eight sons sagely wise.
Receiving great fortune, the world is at peace.

**Bǐ (比):**
Deep valleys become hills, the weak revive.
A land in chaos, the people rest in virtue.

**Zhōng Fù (中孚):**
The middle wife falls ill, entering the dark chamber.

**Xiǎo Xù (小畜):**
The Way is distant and remote, the road fraught with regret.
Fools gather, breeding my fear and dread.

**Lǚ (履):**
Planting beans at dawn, by dusk they become thick soup.
What the heart delights in, the will rejoices.

**Tài (泰):**
Pressing troubles—
misfortune does not come to pass.
The tiger dare not bite, fortune favors me.

**Pǐ (否):**
The king and elder rest afar, the eldest wife remains within.
A different kitchen awaits the meal—
what is sought is not obtained.

**Tóng Rén (同人):**
Cold and heat out of season, drought brings disaster—
though losses occur, no cause for worry.

**Dà Yǒu (大有):**
Though poor, restored to prosperity; treading peril without misfortune—
attaining brilliant success.

**Qiān (谦):**
Where wolves and tigers dwell, one cannot reside—
it brings me woe.

**Yù (豫):**
Whispering in the shadows, light and dark intertwine.
Much talk, little substance—
words accomplish nothing.

**Suí (随):**
Treading on ice and frost, though beset, not impoverished.
Beating drums, climbing the crag—
in the end, no misfortune.

**Gǔ (蛊):**
Ink and soot intermingled, fortune and misfortune entwined.
North and south lose their way, east and west fail to reach.
*(One version reads: Ink and blackness, sorrow and fortune entwined.)*

**Lín (临):**
Endless disputes, exchanging accusations.
Zhang Ji’s weak tongue—
hair unbound, he flees north.

**Guān (观):**
Virtue accumulated, meeting the hour—
fitting for fine talent.
Aiding the wise and enlightened, receiving blessings and joy.
The eldest daughter unwed—
later, great regret.

**Shì Kè (噬嗑):**
The Yangtze’s waters overflow, longing to follow the noble one.
Zhong Bo returns—
he will not look upon me, the niece and sister filled with resentment.

**Bì (贲):**
Radiant rites, spring’s completion, the courtyard rooster crows.

**Shī (师):**
The enlightened master loses the Dao,
unable to guard himself—
dissolving into misfortune.

**Bō (剥):**
A startled tiger brings no harm;
Yu speaks for me,
and I rely on this for peace.

**Fù (复):**
False words and reckless speech,
twisting into error—
no knowing where the wolf lurks.

**Jiǎn (蹇):**
Treading on frost, self-made foe—
misfortune arrives,
grief so deep one wishes for death.

**Dà Xù (大畜):**
Dragging its tail, it will not advance,
defying principle, losing its minister—
Hui and Shuo flee in haste.

**Yí (颐):**
Three wildcats hunt the rat,
blocking my retreat.
Death at the city’s wall—
no escape, no flight.

**Dà Guò (大过):**
Laughter not yet faded,
calamity strikes suddenly.
Bound in black, roped in red,
shackled and confined.

**Kǎn (坎):**
Yin accumulates unceasing,
clouds brew into wanton rain.
The flatlands are ravaged,
people left without shelter.

**Lí (离):**
Mountains, forests, thickets—
no place for men.
Birds and beasts lack propriety,
bittering my heart.

**Xián (咸):**
A new tomb freshly raised,
steep and treacherous to climb.
Three colts push the cart—
stumbling, they wound their jaws.
*(Variant: "陷" as "险," perilous.)*

**Héng (恒):**
The soul wanders, faint and weeping,
journeying where sound fades.
Yet suddenly, the path opens wide—
life returns anew.

**Dùn (遁):**
The joyful son brings ruin,
Bo is slain in punishment.
Zhou Xu flees to Chu,
abandoning his homeland.

**Dà Zhuàng (大壮):**
The arrogant Hu dog,
crafting evil and violence—
nothing achieved,
only self-destruction.

**Jìn (晋):**
Words convey the heart,
bringing stability, averting collapse.

**Increase glory, enhance reputation,**
**to achieve success and fame.**

**Jiā Rén (家人):**
Three catalpas bear no jujubes,
the household stores no weeds.
Send the turtledove to seek a bride—
stubborn, they refuse me.

**Kuí (睽):**
Beware misfortune, dread calamity;
Yanzi alone becomes the warning.
Yet he finds peace and endures.
The pen’s gate binds the sheep—
only then can it receive fortune.

**Jiǎn (蹇):**
The deer finds sweet grass,
calls to summon its friends.
The nine clans live in harmony,
no fear of hunger or want.

**Xiè (解):**
Jade lost, deer gone—
no knowing where they hide.
Profit lies in avoiding peril,
preserving my life’s fortune.
Timely sweet rain descends,
the year’s harvest is assured.

**Sǔn (损):**
Meeting the times, accumulating virtue,
the body receives blessings and joy.

**Yì (益):**
The crane longs for its mate,
desiring to follow the phoenix east.
Aligning feathers and wings with principle,
it soars at noon the next day.
Yet it lingers in the northern town,
then returns to its own home.

**Guài (夬):**
Threads looped on the loom,
a dou measure clings to the mouth.
Where poverty and lowliness dwell,
the heart grows cold with sorrow and grief.
*(Variant: "绪" as "堵," a wall.)*

**Gòu (姤):**
Alone and solitary,
no one to rely on for aid—
the heart toils, the will suffers.

**Cuì (萃):**
Millet serves as Yao’s envoy,
westward to see the Queen Mother.
Bowing, he begs for a hundred blessings,
granted a joyful son—
long-lasting joy, boundless wealth.

**Shēng (升):**
Disaster strikes the withered branches,
northward flee the dogs to the Hu.
Left lapels become the norm,
the kingdom named the Xiongnu.
The lord’s head is shorn,
he is made Chanyu.

**Kùn (困):**
Severed, then reconnected,
though perilous, not exhausted.
In the end, the wish is fulfilled—
Ji and Jiang follow together.

**Jǐng (井):**
The yang well rages madly,
drawing a sword to wound itself,
bringing calamity upon its own body.

**Gé (革):**
Square and round differ,
hard and soft dwell apart.
Digging a well, one strikes stone—
labor in vain, no success.

**Dǐng (鼎):**
Riding wind, driving rain,
together with the crying crow.
Moving a thousand *li*,
I see my beloved mother.

**Zhèn (震):**
The Three Roads, the Five Peaks,
Yangcheng and Mount Tai Shi.
Upheld by divine clarity,
free from war and weapons.

**Gèn (艮):**
The partridge weds a bride,
deep-set eyes, a graceful form.
Bending at the waist yet unyielding,
she clashes with her elder brother.

**Jiàn (渐):**
Wheels turn on the track,
the journey nears but does not end.
At dusk, entering the gate,
laughing and speaking with you.

**Guī Mèi (归妹):**
Seeking profit harms the state—
flee north, away from me.
Returning to its city,
it no longer threatens us.
*(Variant: "难" as "离," separation.)*

**Fēng (丰):**
The path of sun and moon—
wherever one goes, one arrives.
No misfortune, no blame,
peace and safety without peril.

**Lǚ (旅):**
Guan Shu meets Huan,
obtaining his heart’s desire.
The cross-eyed man slays the squinting one—
adjusting his cap, free from care.
Barking with joy, yet not dignified,
empty words and reckless deeds.
*(Variant: "丰之困," "Feng’s distress.")*

**Xùn (巽):**
Entering and exiting with measured steps,
moving in accord with heaven’s timing.
Bowing and rising with restraint,
misfortune and disaster do not come.

**Duì (兑):**
Collapse within, wounds in the center,
chaos above, no constancy.
Though there be grain,
I cannot eat it.

**Huàn (涣):**
Pursuing misfortune to remove calamity,
embodying Dao and divine immortality.
Suppressing evil a thousand *li* away,
fortune ever before me,
the body at ease and joyful.

**Jié (节):**
The startled horse bolts,
upheaval above and below.
Drums sound without cease—
Lord Qing flees in defeat.
*(Variant: "项" as "顷," a moment.)*

**Zhōng Fú (中孚):**
Westward to the Nine Slopes,
coming and going, lingering.
The heart awaits its time,
the numinous and virtuous unite.

**Xiǎo Guò (小过):**
The tiger, enraged, seizes the sheep,
claiming it cannot resist.
Yet it does.

**Jì Jì (既济):**
A bubbling spring, trickling ceaselessly,
flowing south without end,
it becomes a river, a sea.

**Jiàng (将):**
The army launches a surprise attack,
capturing its vile foes.

**Wèi Jì (未济):**
Peachwood bow, reed spear—
eliminating the cruel, expelling evil,
the enemy submits in servitude.

#23 "Eight" (*bā*), *The Hundred Schools Compendium* renders as "enter" (*rù*).
#24 Original text reads "cloth" (*bù*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "a market" (*yī shì*).
#25 "Pavilion" (*gé*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "open" (*kāi*), which is correct.
#26 "Sever" (*duàn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* also reads "sever" (*duàn*), which is correct.
#27 "Clam" (*xiǎn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "draw" (*wǎn*), which is correct.
#28 "Countenance" (*yán*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "wish" (*yuàn*).
#29 "Sun" (*rì*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "eye" (*mù*).
#30 Original text reads "wolf" (*láng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "fierce" (*hěn*). Alternatively, "復狠" (*fù hěn*) is rendered as "obstinate and cruel" (*bì hěn*).
#31 "Its breath" (*zhī xī*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "heralds the dawn" (*sī chén*).
#32 Original text reads "colt" (*jū*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "colt" (*jū*).
#33 "Level" (*píng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "end" (*zú*).
#34 Original text reads "follower" (*tú*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "move" (*xǐ*).
#35 Original text reads "thousand" (*qiān*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "shield" (*gān*).
#36 Original text reads "emerge" (*chū*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "hidden" (*yōu*).
#37 "Dusk" (*hūn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "marriage" (*hūn*).
#38 Original text reads "exalt" (*chóng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "haunt" (*suì*).
#39 "Soil" (*rǎng*); should read "jade ornament" (*xiāng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "outside" (*wài*).
#40 Original text reads "increase" (*zēng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "loathe" (*zēng*).
#41 "Tongdun" (*tóng dùn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "cocklebur" (*cāng ěr*).
#42 "Move" (*xǐ*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "follow" (*cóng*).
#43 "Road" (*lù*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "halt" (*dùn*).
#44 Original text reads "certain" (*mǒu*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "haunt" (*suì*).
#45 Original text reads "firm" (*jiān*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "firm" (*jiān*).
#46 Original text reads "first" (*xiān*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "elder brother" (*xiōng*).
#47 Original text reads "steal beams" (*dào liáng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "rice and millet" (*dào liáng*).
#48 Original text reads "life" (*shēng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "master" (*zhǔ*).
#49 Original text reads "model" (*shì*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "caution" (*jiè*).
#50 "Flower" (*huā*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "splendor" (*huá*).
#51 "Breath" (*xī*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "body" (*shēn*).
#52 Original text reads "cloud" (*yún*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "depart" (*qù*).
#53 Original text omits the variant "hand" (*shǒu*) for "from" (*cóng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, supply.
#54 "Utter sincerity" (*chū zhēn xīn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "King Jun plows" (*wáng jūn gēng*).
#55 Original text omits the variant "self-complete" (*zì wán*) for "gate" (*mén*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, supply.
#56 "Forbid and embank" (*jìn dī yǔ*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "Chu follows closely" (*chǔ gēn shèn*).
#57 "Love" (*ài*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "receive" (*shòu*).
#58 Original text reads "halt" (*dùn*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "head" (*tóu*).
#59 Original text reads "comet" (*bó*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "perverse" (*bèi*).
#60 "Sun one" (*rì yī*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "moreover" (*qiě*), though "sun one" (*rì yī*) is correct.
#61 Original text reads "examine" (*jī*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "point" (*zhǐ*).
#62 Original text reads "winnowing basket" (*jī*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "without" (*wú*).
#63 "Long sojourning guest" (*jiǔ liú lián kè*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "sojourning long guest" (*liú lián jiǔ kè*).
#64 Original text reads "moreover" (*qiě*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "sun one" (*rì yī*).
#65 "Change" (*gǎi*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "complete" (*chéng*).
#66 "Expand sister" (*tuò mèi*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "wicked and seductive" (*jiān yāo*).
#67 Original text reads "entrust" (*wěi*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "bow frame" (*qíng*).
#68 Original text reads "behead" (*zhǎn*); emend to "sedan chair" (*jiào*). "Halt and behead" (*dùn zhǎn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "collapse and perish" (*tuí háng*).
#69 "Lodge" (*sù*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "sit" (*zuò*).
#70 Original text reads "blessing" (*fú*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "misfortune" (*huò*).
#71 Original text reads "follower" (*tú*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "cause" (*shǐ*).
#72 "Float" (*fàn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "lack" (*fá*).
#73 Original text reads "rely" (*yīn*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "distress" (*kùn*).
#74 Original text omits "calamity" (*xiōng*) after "anxiety" (*yōu*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, supply.
#75 Original text reads "blessing" (*fú*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "misfortune" (*huò*).
#76 Original text reads "perhaps" (*huò*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "barbarian" (*yí*).

#77 Original text reads "go" (*wǎng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "mad" (*kuáng*).
#78 Original text repeats "act" (*wéi*) after "act"; according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, delete the repetition.
#79 "Above" (*shàng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "earth" (*tǔ*), and "earth" is correct.
#80 "Regret" (*chàng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "resentment" (*hèn*).
#81 "Chant" (*chàng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "lead" (*chàng*).
#82 Original text reads "garrison" (*shù*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "war" (*róng*).
#83 This edition’s *Dùn* hexagram’s *Zhōng Fú* forest verse is *The Hundred Schools Compendium*’s *Dùn* hexagram’s *Jì Jì* forest verse.
#84 Original text reads "await" (*dài*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "proceed" (*xíng*).
#85 This edition’s *Dùn* hexagram’s *Jì Jì* forest verse is *The Hundred Schools Compendium*’s *Dùn* hexagram’s *Zhōng Fú* forest verse.
#86 "Not yet" (*wèi*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "come" (*lái*).
#87 "Have" (*yǒu*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "separate" (*lí*).
#88 Original text reads "Yí Míng"; according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "Míng Yí."
#89 Original text reads "moreover" (*qiě*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "day-one" (*rì yī*).
#90 Original text reads "fire" (*huǒ*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "great" (*dà*).
#91 Original text reads "filial" (*xiào*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "old" (*lǎo*).
The character "sun" (*rì*) below should read "sun" (*rì*).
#92 "Sharp ears" (*cōng bìn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "sharp whiskers" (*cōng liè*).
#93 "Sideburns" (*rán*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "intent" (*yì*).
#94 "Stings me" (*shì wǒ*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "stinging thief" (*shì zéi*).
#95 "Elder" (*bó*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "hegemon" (*bà*).
#96 Original text omits "four" (*sì*) before "one" (*yī*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*’s appended note "four collapses, one edition suspects as *huí* collapse," supply.
#97 "Yǔ"; *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "rain" (*yǔ*).
#98 "Time" (*shí*); an alternate reading is "uncle" (*shū*).
#99 Original text reads "next" (*cì*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "Kǎn."
#100 Original text reads "two" (*èr*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "one" (*yī*).
#101 Original text reads "house" (*jiā*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "swine" (*shǐ*).
#102 Original text reads "this" (*shì*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "flee" (*zǒu*).
#103 Original text omits the appended note "abandon, suspected as *biàn*" after "regret" (*huǐ*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, supply.
#104 Original text reads "compare" (*bǐ*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "north" (*běi*).
#105 "Treasure" (*bǎo*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "august" (*huáng*). Neither is correct; it should read "fruit" (*shí*).
#106 "Strong" (*qiáng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "stiff" (*jiāng*), and "stiff" is correct.
#107 "Generation" (*shì*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "origin" (*yuán*).
#108 "This comparison" (*zhī bǐ*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "with the north" (*yǐ běi*).
#109 Original text reads "fire" (*huǒ*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "great" (*dà*).
#110 "Life" (*shēng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "its" (*qí*).
#111 Original text reads "not yet" (*wèi*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "grain" (*hé*).
#112 "Clothing" (*yī*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "origin" (*yuán*).
#113 "Not" (*bù*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "ford" (*shè*).
#114 Original text reads "Yáo"; according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "dawn" (*xiǎo*).
#115 Original text reads "reverent" (*gōng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "millet" (*shǔ*).
#116 "Full" (*yíng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "increase" (*yì*).
#117 Original text reads "snake" (*sì*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "self" (*jǐ*).
#118 Original text includes "entangled" (*lí*) after "male" (*xióng*), a redundancy; according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, delete.
#119 "Supreme" (*tài*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "great" (*dà*).
#120 Original text reads "treasure" (*zhēn*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "heel" (*gēn*).
#121 "Owl" (*xiāo*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "celebration" (*qìng*).
#122 Original text reads "order" (*lún*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "elm" (*yú*).
#123 "Husband" (*fū*) should read "lose" (*shī*).
#124 The appended note at the end of the *Jiě* hexagram, "water, one edition reads wood," is irrelevant to its forest verse and is likely a redundancy. Alternatively, the appended note should be emended to "wood, one edition reads water."
#125 Original text reads "fourth earthly branch" (*mǎo*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "egg" (*luǎn*).
#126 "Crow" (*yā*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "poison-fowl" (*zhèn*).
#127 Original text reads "turtledove" (*gū*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "pigeon" (*gū*).
#128 "State" (*guó*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "garden" (*pǔ*).
#129 Original text reads "enter village" (*rù cūn*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "eight talents" (*bā cái*).

#130 Original text reads "crow" (*wū*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "cry" (*wū*).
#131 Original text reads "bestow" (*shī*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "revolve" (*xuán*).
#132 Original text reads "profit" (*lì*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "autumn" (*qiū*).
#133 Original text reads "win" (*yíng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, unchanged as "win" (*yíng*).
#134 Original text reads "caution" (*shèn*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "fear" (*jù*).
#135 Original text reads "earth" (*dì*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "within" (*lǐ*).
#136 "Virtue/power" (*dé*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "gain" (*dé*).
#137 "Transmit" (*zhuàn*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "await" (*dài*).
#138 "Substance" (*shí*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "august" (*huáng*).
#139 "Ink and ink" (*wén mò qiě mò*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "patterns of ink" (*wén wén mò mò*).
#140 "Ink" (*mò*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "black" (*hēi*).
#141 "Bo Shu" (*bó shòu*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "Shi Yuan" (*shì yuán*).
#142 "Does not deign to look upon me" (*bù wǒ kěn gù*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "does not look upon me" (*bù kěn wǒ gù*).
#143 *The Hundred Schools Compendium* includes an appended note after "regret" (*huǐ*): "Shi, one edition reads Bo."
#144 "Chamber" (*shì*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "treasure" (*bǎo*).
#145 "Teacher" (*shī*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "yang" (*yáng*).

#147 "Chestnut" (*lì*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "crevice" (*xì*).
#148 "Death" (*sǐ*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "able" (*néng*).
"Death and weeping" (*sǐ kū*), one edition reads "able and laughing" (*néng xiào*).
#149 "Lead" (*qiān*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "rope" (*suǒ*), though "lead" is deemed correct.
#150 Original text reads "rice" (*mǐ*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "gate and bundle" (*mén shù*).
#151 "Journey and vastness" (*xíng kuàng*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "connect and continue" (*shǔ xù*).
