#153 "Fault" (*yóu*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "friend" (*yǒu*).
#154 Original text omits "dū" after "make" (*zuò*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, add "dū."
#155 Original text reads "command" (*mìng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "profound" (*yǎo*).
#156 Original text reads "sun" (*rì*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "eye" (*mù*).
#157 "Kill and slant" (*shā xié*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "glue and mouth" (*jiāo kǒu*).
#158 Original text reads "pass" (*guò*); emend to "obstruct" (*è*).
#159 "Slope" (*bēi*); *The Hundred Schools Compendium* reads "trash" (*jī*).
#160 Original text reads "say" (*wèi*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "cunning" (*huá*).
#161 Original text reads "companion" (*péng*); according to *The Hundred Schools Compendium*, emend to "submit" (*fú*).

*Yi Lin*, Scroll 2 (Part 2), "The Household" (*Jiā Rén*), Hexagram Thirty-Seven

**The Household (Hexagram Thirty-Seven)**

The king’s command: a red horse is given to the lord at the appointed time.
Marching to punish the unruly, slaying the lord’s arrogance—
what worry remains in dwelling?

**Qian:**
A thousand-year-old locust root, its body scarred by axes.
Wounded, uprooted, hacked—
no branches or leaves remain.

**Kun:**
Dark and boastful, tiger and leopard snarl.
Fearful and trembling, they hold their breath—
no harm or evil befalls in the end.

**Zhun:**
Marrying into the Jiang and Lü clans, the groom welcomes the new bride.
The young Qi maiden stands at the gate—
husband and wife rejoice.

**Meng:**
Fertile soil, rich and moist, the people greatly delight.
Fitting and prosperous for dwelling—
long peace brings fortune.

**Xu:**
The lord possesses sagely virtue, matching the Great Ultimate on high.
The august spirit establishes the center—
bestowing blessings upon me.

**Song:**
The aged grow dull, seeing neither east nor west.
The young do not admire them—
the lord does not consult them.
Hanging up the carriage to retire,
they withdraw to their village home.

**Shi:**
Three madmen journey north, encountering a great wolf on the road.
Lodging at dusk in a troubled house,
they are harmed by misfortune.

**Bi:**
At dawn of the new year, sweeping away calamity and ruin.
New garments and proper robes—
receiving blessings and fortune.

**Xiao Xu:**
The bright white sun is devoured by the moon.
Diminishing the superior, harming the superior—
Zheng Zhao flees in exile.
*(Note: "Superior" above and below may refer to the upper line.)*

**Lü:**
The nobleman loses favor, the petty man gains power.
Chaos and sorrow arise together,
treacherous women and villains block the way.
Though a hundred Yaos may come,
the downfall cannot be saved.

**Tai:**
Virtue and kindness overflow, grace extending to foreign lands.
Blessings spread to distant regions—
hidden fortune abounds.
The silkworm spins early, yet does not weave—
in cold, nothing is gained.

**Pi:**
Seeking gold and jade in the east, one finds only worthless stone.
Called "unfit," named "ugly"—
despised and scorned by all.

**Tong Ren:**
Drums sound, battle is joined—
the soldiers flee in cowardice.
Authority collapses, my success is undone.

**Da You:**
Mid-spring to early summer, harmony dwells within.
It nurtures my great fortune—
the land knows no ruin or strife.

**Qian:**
Yin, Boqi of the House of Yin—
father and son torn apart.
Though innocent, they are condemned—
a long tongue brings disaster.

**Yu:**
The five grains do not ripen, the people suffer extreme hardship.
Driving them to a new city—
fine grain is obtained.

**Sui:**
Ascending the heights, gazing at poverty, evening brings no meal.
The eldest son is garrisoned in the south—
estranged from me in life.

**Gu:**
In the eastern markets of Qi and Lu, merchants journey south to Chu.
Feathers, fur, hides, and leather—
become my treasured wealth.

**Lin:**
Moderating emotions, curbing desires, taxation is measured.
Households are provided for, the people are content—
Lord Liu grows rich.

**Guan:**
Reverent, generous, trustworthy, and diligent—
merit extends to the four seas.
Banishing misfortune, joy comes from the mother.

**Shi Ke:**
Arrogant and reckless, encountering evil.
Desires unfulfilled—
I alone meet misfortune.

**Bi:**
Painting a dragon’s head and neck, the design is incomplete.
Sweet words and fine speech—
deceptive words bear no name.

**Bo:**
Riding dragons and mounting phoenixes, ascending to meet the divine lord.
Peng Zu receives the decree, Wang Qiao aids in communion.
Wu Xian takes his place—
endless blessings are bestowed.

**Fu:**
The warm and benevolent nobleman, where loyalty and filial piety reside.
Eight lands as neighbors—
no calamity arises.

**Wu Wang:**
Authority scatters, crows circle at night.
The flock obscures the moon—
the great one is slain and wounded.

**Da Xu:**
Studying the numinous for three years, sagely and spiritually enlightened.
Foreknowing good fortune—
joy and blessings abound.
A divine bird appears, announcing boundless news.

**Yi:**
Leaving the eastern mountains, the wife at home misses her husband.
Silverfish fill the room, long-legged centipedes crowd the door.
My lord delights me—
yet the days of service are not done.

**Da Guo:**
Jaws open wide, tongue severed from teeth.
Promises unkept, governance in chaos—
no order remains.

**Kan:**
Blowing horns, the high state loses cattle and sheep.
The people are alarmed—
cautious and wary of blame.
Rectifying conduct averts disaster.

**Li:**
Journeying south beyond the city, the world’s virtue brings blessings.
The three Ji sisters marry into Qi—
their desires fulfilled.

**Xian:**
Heart mad, will perverse, ears follow the crowd.
Policies lack constancy—
the people multiply in suffering.

**Heng:**
Peaceful and fitting for office, promoted nine times in a day.
Leading the Yu and Yue peoples,
shepherding the Changshan region.

**Dun:**
The eastern neighbor marries off her daughter, becoming the king’s consort.
Duke Zhuang builds a palace to serve the queen mother.
Returning to the capital, Ji Jiang rejoices.

**Da Zhuang:**
The sixth Jia has no son, losing its Wu.
The fifth Ding grows distant, Geng loses its great-grandson—
Gui flees out the gate.

**Jin:**
Dark mist obscures clarity, corrupt governance confounds the people.
Early spring to late summer—
floods destroy my home.

**Ming Yi:**
Riding a pig in pursuit of sheep, the goal remains unseen.
Cutting through the tiger’s den—
life lost, the lamb gone.

**Kui:**
Thick mats and soft cushions, yet no long rest.
Abandoning my joyful feast,
I am beset in the southern land.
The sorrow of casting aside the shuttle—
no disaster comes to pass.

**Jian:**
The four directions and four corners, peaceful and secure.
Fitting for dwelling—
safeguarding the king’s daughter.

**Xie:**
A western merchant in Ba and Shu, cold snow reaches the axle.
Unable to advance, he returns to his chamber.

**Sun:**
Firm and yielding call to each other, two clans become family.
After the frost descends, they unite—
bestowing kindness and benevolence upon me.

**Yi:**
Heavenly horses on five roads, flanking the great divide.
Coming and going, ascending and descending—
following one another in weeping and song.
How dire the misfortune!

**Guai:**
Leaving home with sorrow, ascending the eastern mound of misfortune.
Encountering evil, I bring disaster upon myself.

**Sheng:**
Journeying west in search of jade, hoping for a fine uncut gem.
Instead, I meet misfortune—
startled and bewildered.

**Cui:**
Leaving home, no destination—
actions bring no advantage.

**Xian:**
Bearing sorrow, harboring misfortune,
it leaves me much withered.
*(Variant: "entering" for "gate"; "reckless" for "arrival.")*

**Sheng:**
A lofty tower without pillars—
soon it will collapse and fall.
Zhou lost its three sages,
and perished at Muye.

**Kun:**
Avoiding calamity, fleeing disaster,
I preserve my body unharmed.
The noble fall ill and stumble;
blossoms fall, doomed to decay.

**Jing:**
Baring fangs, glaring eyes,
rage and fury surge.
A mad horse tramples a hound—
the path is startled, the wing is wounded.

**Ge:**
The spring dries, the dragon frets;
Jizi becomes a slave.
Gan Shu meets his end—
Yin’s house is shattered.

**Ding:**
Facing the feast, drinking wine,
fine guests gather in assembly.
A propitious lamb, a great stew—
the nobleman abounds in plenty.

**Zhen:**
The yellow ox shuns its calf,
bound and walking, its horn snaps.
Hoping for a hundred blessings,
instead my sack is lost.

**Gen:**
The road bristles with thorns,
stepping pierces my foot.
Unfavorable for travelers—
it poisons the heart.

**Jian:**
Grasping the axe, splitting kindling,
I send a matchmaker to seek a bride.
Two clans unite in harmony—
together they pour the wedding wine.
Calling neighbors and kin,
parents and in-laws rejoice.

**Guimei:**
Driving the carriage forth,
timely heading west.
Fortune blesses my person—
peace and safety, no harm.

**Feng:**
Sunrise, binding the sheaves—
the Dipper’s handle brings misfortune.
The Han Terrace becomes Qin’s—
it keeps me long seated.
*(Variant: "moves" for "rises.")*

**Lü:**
Hills and burial mounds,
souls haunt empty chambers.
Essence and light exhausted—
long estranged, none perceive.

**Xun:**
A child greedy for bait,
lured by profit.
Reaching into the pot for rice,
his arm is scalded.

**Dui:**
Why wait for the season?
Shutting the door, grieving alone.
Earthworms move in winter—
they free me from care.
Silkworms fail to thrive—
the woman’s work comes to naught.

**Huan:**
Dissolving wounds, dispelling alarm,
scattering my robes—
the lord cannot secure the realm.

**Jie:**
Harming governance, nurturing bandits,
turning from the king to transgression.
Lame and unsteady,
the state faces peril.

**Zhongfu:**
Misfortune flees, calamity hides—
joy becomes my fortune.
Evil vanishes, disasters cease.

**Xiaoguo:**
An old horse treated as a colt,
a sick hen bears no chicks.
Three hens roost alone—
profit lies north of the mountains.

**Jiji:**
Dancing wildly between heaven and earth,
dawn disrupts the spirits’ abode.
Dwelling in joy, no fault arises.

**Weiji:**
Foreign lands, alien customs—
hearts do not align.
Metal and wood turn foes;
chieftains seize control.

---

**Kui (Hexagram 38):**

**Kui:**
Granaries overflow, stores in the millions—
millet and sorghum thrive.
Years of plenty, harvests ripe—
the people rest in peace.

**Qian:**
Adorned in patterned robes,
roaming by wine pools.
Ascending the hall, offered a cup—
joy as if meeting a brother,
my sorrows vanish.

**Jian:**
*(See Hexagram 13, Tongren.)*

**Kun:**
Lady Jiang, daughter of Shu,
the celestial patterns in her grasp.
Her fate tied to Shen and Chen—
enfeoffed as Marquis of Jin.

**Tun:**
The branch changes, the leaf transforms;
the meal cools, uneaten.
Heroes vie for strength—
the first receives fortune.

**Meng:**
Fragrant herbs descend from the heights,
illustrious virtue ascends.
The earth spirit grants favor—
commanded to be a great neighbor.

**Xu:**
An old wolf, a white colt,
a long-tailed fox.
Stumbling forward and back—
advancing and retreating, it meets curses.

**Song:**
Mountains sink, hills float,
land becomes water, fish.
Swallows and sparrows lose their nests.

**Shi:**
Duke Yi, shallow and foolish,
rejected wise counsel.
Without aid, he lost his state—
destroyed by the Di.

**Bi:**
The tripod’s ears glow red,
too hot to lift.
The great road blocked—
travelers’ hearts ache.

**Xiaoxu:**
Foul words, vile sounds—
unbearable to hear.
The nobleman abandons them—
departing, they wound my heart.
*(Variant: "evil" for "doubt.")*

**Lü:**
At dusk, mounting the carriage,
treading peril, stepping into the ditch.
Losing the herd, the goods—
both axles snap.

**Tai:**
In the south, fine fish—
harnessing the yellow, seizing the gills.
Plump and sleek—
profit comes without sorrow.

**Pi:**
Barred by nine mountains,
coming and going is laborious.
The heart’s knot remains tied—
joy is lost.

**Tongren:**
Dwelling downstream is hard;
the madman wears many guises.
The steadfast, gentle, and kind—
their years are not prosperous.

**Dayou:**
Foxes, pheasants, hares—
fearing men, they flee.
Scattering, hiding—
nowhere to be found.

**Qian:**
Different bodies, separate customs,
each with their own kin.
The western neighbor’s widow
wishes to lodge in my home.
The mistress scolds and slanders—
in the end, she cannot.

**Yu:**
Anger not from resentment,
greed for a rotting rat—
calling hawks and falcons,
he loses his own bait,
ensnared in trouble.

**Sui:**
Five hearts, six minds,
forked paths teem with strangeness.
Not the lord’s true intent—
it breeds my regret.

**Gu:**
Three stripes, six blacks—
sharing a room, eating together.
Days lengthen, months grow—
my house gains virtue.

**Lin:**
A square boat readied for water,
fires lit by the river—
a lifetime without misfortune.

**Guan:**
Behind screens, whispering alone,
deaf to court and market.
Profitable for seclusion—
yet in the end, shut out.

**Shike:**
Dwelling in unease,
returning only brings trouble.

**Fu:**
Stripped, carved, shorn, and mutilated—
despised and cast aside.
Defiant words—
my heart is not at ease.

**Gaoxiong:**
Fields of millet and hemp,
mounds of grain.
Clothing and food sustain me—
my household abounds.

**Two eyes lose sight—
day by day, light is stolen.
Lame and limping,
unable to walk—
collapsing by the hillside.**
*(Variant: "baseless delusion.")*

**Jin:**
The golden city of Shuofang—
foreign lands hold many sheep,
yet departure brings sorrow.

**Lü:**
Frost out of season—
the great beast hides its madness, unhealed.
Chaos breeds disaster.
Zhou’s tyranny and excess—
Shang’s ruins lie shattered.

**Yi:**
Ghosts wail at the altar,
grieving the loss of heirs.
At dawn on jiazi,
Tang of Yin’s sacrifices ended.

**Daguo:**
Winds rise in a sudden gust,
chariots race, robes flutter.

Discarding the ancient, chasing the lost,
losing harmony and measure—
the heart grieves, choked with sorrow.

**Kan:**
The aged, sightless elder,
hears the good yet will not follow.
Self-inflicted downfall—
reversal brings calamity.

**Li:**
Riding the wind, mounting the dragon,
encountering fortune at every turn.
Three foxes taken in a day—
the Lord of Shang reaps merit.
In the city of Chongchong,
Chang’an knows no misfortune.

**Xian:**
Three oxen, five omens,
double brightness brings blessing,
granting me gain.
Sickness enters the prison—
anguish lodges in heart and belly.

**Da:**
First month, second day—yi-chou.
One calls out to Master Ni.
Virtue’s light fades to nothing—
tyranny and chaos multiply.

**You:**
A hundred branches of flowering crabapple,
dissolving darkness, waning to feebleness.
Essence and radiance spent—
suddenly like ash or withered deer.

**Dazhuang:**
The hawk soars, the pheasant retreats,
the hare crouches, unmoving.
Foxes bare their fangs, wolves howl—
wild fowl startle in terror.

**Jin:**
Battling at Heaven’s Gate—
what peril could there be?
Household intact,
joy unlost.

**Mingyi:**
The Shu clan slaughters oxen,
their conduct foul and rank.
The spirits turn their backs, gazing west—
the mandate of declining Zhou is severed.
The altar of Bo burns in disaster—
the people of Song are annihilated.
Foul stench—
or *Worse Than Corruption*.

**Jiaren:**
Yin and Yang distinguish expansion,
two clans unite in marriage.
The union flourishes—
bearing fortune and blessing.

**Jian:**
Bound eastward to the sea’s mouth,
following the current northward.
Rising and falling—
the five-hued city has no master.

**Ten days and six nights, perishing in water and dust.**

**Jie:**
The ruins of Gubuzhu—
a wife lost, no husband remains.
Grieving at Hanhua,
he sees not his wife.
Dongguo Tang Jiang—
Wuzi is gone.

**Sun:**
The eastern ruins of Heaven’s Gate,
all is consumed by disaster.
Treading in darkness and deafness,
the Earl of Qin suffers calamity.

**Yi:**
Relying on the radiance of the former,
receiving the blessings of fortune.
Though beset by chaos and collapse,
narrowly escaping peril.

**Jia:**
Tongue broken, eyes shut—
or *like the sun obscured*—
the noble Shu unseen.
A three-legged lone crow,
far off yet without loss.
*Shi’s Meng.*

**Shen:**
Seven in one chamber,
brothers sharing food.
Harmonious and joyful,
each attains their desire.

**Cui:**
Heir apparent guards the fief,
indulgence ousts the worthy.
Lord and minister in dissipation—
the Xia clan loses itself.
At the side chamber’s gate,
fortune and blessing arrive.

**Sheng:**
The old fox bends its tail,
east and west it becomes a ghost.
Afflicting my eldest daughter,
weeping and wailing, pointing in scorn.
Now west, now east—
great change brings seduction.

**Kun:**
The great tree’s offspring,
a hundred branches share one mother.
In the sixth month of summer,
branches and leaves flourish.
The luan and phoenix shelter beneath—
the Duke of Shao seeks shade.
So balanced, so fitting,
each finds their place.
*Daguo’s Xu.*

**Jing:**
Misty waters carve the land,
the state teems with violence and ruin.
The King of Qin loses his place,
breaking my great altar.
*(Note: "Carve" should likely read "profit.")*

**Ge:**
Harnessing yellow, trading gray,
welcoming profit in accord.
The heart secures its hold,
no burden to brothers.

**Ding:**
Granaries brim with countless stores,
millet and sorghum thrive in season.
Years of plenty, harvests ripe—
the people rest in peace.

**Zhen:**
Born in the Horse’s Depth,
long-lived and divine.
Soaring to the heavens,
lodging in the Xuan Yuan,
dwelling in joy and ease.

**Gen:**
Thoughts and wishes find their way,
meeting the hour at last.
Washing away old sorrows,
I bow to joy’s arrival.

**Jian:**
The crooked and askew strike true,
first bringing ruin and woe.
The noble lingers in distress,
bound by water and broth.
Seeking gold in the eastern mountains,
profit lies in lush lands.
The market yields gain,
a son carries his mother on the road.

**Gui Mei:**
A leaden blade carves jade,
drilling and chiseling without fail.
The dragon’s form fully rises,
Lu Ban lends his aid.
Three sages assist the task—
all sought is met with delight.

**Feng:**
Joy arrives like clouds,
the household rejoices as one.
Talented gentlemen,
fortune fills the gate.

**Lü:**
Echoes without form,
bones and body unformed.
In secret, decline and decay—
vanishing without a name.

**Xun:**
Stagnant waters do not warm,
the northern wilds bitter with cold.
Sleeping in dew, winds assail—
the noble one’s heart grieves.

**Dui:**
A yellow horse, a green carriage,
driving to the great capital.
Recommending talent and skill,
freeing me from care.
*(Note: "Recommending" should likely read "advancing.")*

**Huan:**
Following the wind to set fire,
orchids and mugwort perish together.
Three harms gather,
Shu Zi is struck down.

**Jie:**
One body, three hands—
no aid to support.
Two feet share a joint,
unable to act with agility.

**Zhong Fu:**
Facing south in a humble chamber,
wind and rain enter as one.
Dust and dampness accumulate,
the Queen Mother’s blindness and paralysis.
Half-paralyzed, heart afflicted—
my household falls to disorder.

**Xiao Guo:**
Gathering ferns, setting out in chariots,
thinking of fish and deer’s first catch.
Urgent above and below,
the noble one harbors sorrow.

**Ji Ji:**
First easy, then difficult,
fortune’s market is revealed to me.
Restless and self-tormenting,
longing to correct again.

**Wei Ji:**
Born where earth’s milk flows,
the Supreme Sovereign rejoices greatly.
Exalting my blessings,
noble longevity knows no end.

---

**Jian (Hexagram 39):**

**Jian:**
Crossing together, then parting midway,
losing my foremost man,
alone with grief and hardship.

**Qian:**
Shu Pan bears injustice,
Qi Zi flees his fief.
Rushing to resolve the crisis,
Yang She escapes—
relying on this, he survives whole.

**Kun:**
Hares gather in the eastern outskirts,
hounds all give chase.
The encirclement breaks—
nothing is gained.

**Zhun:**
Building a house at the mountain’s root,
people deem it secure.
One night it collapses,
ruining my provisions.

**Meng:**
Fierce winds stir the dust,
disrupting my beginnings.
The strong and great overwhelm the small—
first hardship, then joy.

**Xu:**
Purifying and bathing,
cultivating bright virtue.
Once Duke Gong’s timidity,
the Feng clan retreats north.

**Song:**
Barren, thin soil,
a mound without catalpa—
it brings me no joy.

**Shi:**
Wearing armor to ford the river,
the stream’s flow deep and swift.
Relying on the boatman,
I cross safely without harm.

**Bi:**
Escorting my youngest daughter
to the broad road.
The Qi maiden day and night,
lingering long in delay.

**Xiao Xu:**
Three grandsons, six sons—
no suffering befalls them.
Yet the central storehouse decays,
losing what I employ.

**Lü:**
Winds sweep the grass flat,
dust and dirt rise together.
Pure and turbid scatter,
the loyal and upright retreat.

**Tai:**
Traversing peril, climbing danger,
the road is long, the toil exhausting.
Leaving home to return,
struggling through great waves.

**Pi:**
The gate of the Six Arts,
benevolence and righteousness both dwell.
A foundation of iron meets the hour—
Yao and Shun as rulers.
From cold and heat to warmth,
descending to the Yellow Springs.

**Tong Ren:**
Clad in patterned robes,
roaming wine pools in leisure.
Ascending the hall to see the cup—
joy as my elder brother,
banishing my sorrows.

**Da You:**
Born at an inauspicious time,
heaven’s mandate brings calamity.
Bound by the axe’s mark,
toiling through the night in hardship.

**Qian:**
Heaven’s gates open wide,
the prison’s doors stand empty.
Bolt and lock undone,
the captive is freed.

**Yu:**
River depths are treacherous,
water brings me woe.
Many words, little substance—
mistaking a deer for a colt.
The foundation of Dao and virtue,
the noble one meets the hour,
profit in resolving doubt.

**Sui:**
Meeting the season in one’s village,
life’s appointed time.
Branches and leaves flourish,
the noble one knows no sorrow.

**Gu:**
Six swans retreat in flight,
an omen of decline and ruin.
*(Note: "Ruin" should read "defeat.")*

**Shi:**
The armies join in battle,
the left thigh wounded.
Collapsing, unable to rise—
the hegemonic enterprise fails.

**Lin:**
The Thunder Lord prepares his journey,
rumbling westward in retreat.
Endless rains pour down,
swelling into rivers and streams—
the southern lands face dire misfortune.

**Guan:**
Teeth sprout from gums,
yang flourishes without.
Left hand grasps the key,
the lord bestows rank and cup.

**Shi Ke:**
Fire rises at the earthen gate,
yet spares my home.
Leaping free, unbound,
I alone survive unscathed.
Ill-omened to venture near,
plagued by sickness and woe.

**Bi:**
All undertakings fail,
no gain in marching forth.
Words go unheeded,
the crowd grows discontent.

**Bo:**
Old wolf, white donkey,
long-tailed fox.
Stumbling forward, tripping back,
advance and retreat meet misfortune.

**Fu:**
The sun sinks to its limit,
the weary find rest.
The troops return in ranks,
I reclaim my home in Yan.

**Wu Wang:**
Mountains, forests, marshes—
no place for men.
Beasts and birds show no propriety,
grief weighs upon my heart.

**Da Xu:**
Store profit, amass blessings,
daily renew your virtue.
The Gaos feast in abundance,
no sorrow shall befall them.

**Yi:**
Nets spread for a hundred days,
the birds cannot flee north.
Necks drawn in, wings pinned,
trapped in a land of distress.
The noble one cultivates virtue,
earning praise and fortune.

**Da Guo:**
Elder Tiger, Second Bear,
their virtue and righteousness run deep.
They spread the Five Teachings,
yin and yang follow their course.

**Kan:**
The lame and the halt follow,
oxen weary as dusk falls.
The rear guard lags behind,
fortune lost, the female gone.

**Li:**
The Ying clan strays from goodness,
sending Meng to seek arms.
War drags on without end,
defeat comes at the hands of Qi’s ministers.

**Xian:**
Sun and moon dwell together,
ever dim and faint.
Lofty peaks collapse,
hills become valleys.

**Dai:**
Crows and magpies feast on grain,
beaks open for feeding.
Blessed by grace and virtue,
they grow strong and thrive.
Gentle and yielding, upright and true—
lord and minister in harmony.

**Guai:**
Though stumbling, one rises again,
teeth unbroken.
The hare’s wound heals,
woes vanish, no illness remains.

**Da Zhuang:**
Grass and trees wither yellow,
the year ends without shelter.
Tyranny breeds ruin,
the great lose their fortune.

**Jin:**
Fleeing misfortune to the east,
one turns back into disaster’s maw.
Seized by fangs and claws,
bones reduced to ash and dust.

**Ming Yi:**
Longing to fly but unable,
the heart labors in bitter toil—
fortune does not come to me.

**Jia Ren:**
Lamb’s fur, leopard’s trim,
eastward I meet good fortune.
My brother arrives in a chariot,
bearing gifts of black and yellow steeds.

**Kui:**
Plowing east, the plow breaks;
westward, a good wife is lost.
Disaster cannot be avoided.

**Xie:**
A poor household lacks means,
fish and deer lose their place.
Crows and flies suffer hardship,
the marsh holds no reeds or rushes—
the state of Jin grows desolate.

**Sun:**
A hare without hooves,
three steps, five halts.
Southward progress stalls,
the later market brings toil.

**Yi:**
The journey is not yet done,
new tasks arise again.
Ji and Jiang labor without rest,
no respite to be found.

**Guai:**
Facing the sun, light shines bright,
fire reigns as king.
Metal melts, weapons are laid down,
chariots of thunder retreat and hide.
The rains do not fall,
the people settle in their villages.

**Kun:**
The bit is cast aside, reins let loose,
the galloping horse uncontrolled.
Law abandoned, treachery rises—
the lord loses his throne.

**Cui:**
The Lord of Fate does not wander,
joy dissolves my cares.
The Queen Mother loosens her sash,
the infant laughs with delight.

**Sheng:**
The Yellow Emperor sets forth,
riding dragons and steeds.
Eastward he ascends Mount Tai,
passing south through Qi and Lu—
all the commanderies rejoice.

**Kun:**
What is past brings no joy,
sorrows gather like misfortune’s knots.
The northern door becomes a bane,
no place to voice grievance.

**Jing:**
Bearing baskets, living in seclusion,
to escape chaos and collapse.
A lifetime without office,
preserving purity and clarity.

**Ge:**
The pestle pounds millet,
yet the lord goes unfed.
Scratching the heel for an itching head—
no remedy for the ailment.

**Ding:**
Roots planted but not firm,
flowers and leaves fall away,
leaving a withered tree.

**Zhen:**
The gate of misfortune births strife,
the prison holds many wrongs.
Barren sands, toothless jaws—
I am brought to ruin.

**Gen:**
Ascending mountains, treading valleys,
encountering tigers.
The swift one serves as clerk,
the slave flees north—
deliverance to a land of joy.

**Jian:**
Where the qilin and phoenix soar,
the land knows no harm.
The market yields tenfold profit,
returning to the village of kindness.

**Gui:**
The path is perilous, the way treacherous,
water flows before me.
Advancing brings no gain—
turn the chariot back.

**Feng:**
Craning necks toward the city,
longing for home.
Pavilions unfinished,
no rest to be found.

**Lü:**
Brambles and thorns entangle,
thistles catch my beard.
Petty men grow jealous,
kindness cannot prevail.

**Xun:**
Southward to hidden realms,
lurking in deep concealment.
Wisdom and insight sealed,
one joins the ranks of the dead.

**Dui:**
Traps and bait are set,
schemes plotted against Ziliang.
Fan Shu’s greed brings ruin—
calamity befalls him.

**Huan:**
Riding out from the valley,
roaming the bitter wilds.
The path is steep and rough,
no profit to be gained.

**Jie:**
The western state grows strong,
becoming tiger and wolf.
Eastward it devours Qi and Chu,
seizing their kings.

**Zhong Fu:**
Ascending the mountain to fell timber,
a tiger lurks at my side.
The prince feels no fear—
benevolence sees no threat.

**Xiao Guo:**
In the sixth month, all watch keenly,
each striving to arrive.
The latecomers are not yet strong—
wait for tomorrow’s dawn.

**Ji Ji:**
The road crosses many slopes,
oxen and horses falter.
The cart cannot bear its load,
requests go unanswered.

**Wei Ji:**
One mouth, three tongues,
hindering without benefit.
A flock of sheep, a hundred omens—
no show of strength.
A lost horse, a missing foal—
the household dwindles with the times.

**Xie (Hexagram 40):**
Setting out on a journey,
crows fight before the chariot.
Strife and ruin follow,
soldiers and horses approach.
Turn the chariot back swiftly—
thus may you avoid sorrow.

**Qian (Hexagram 1):**
Dwelling in the great capital,
nothing is lacking.
Embracing cloth to trade for silk,
all sought is surely gained.

**Kun (Hexagram 2):**
Glued to wood, bound in chains,
never leaving the inner chambers—
household and home dwell in peace.

**Zhun (Hexagram 3):**
Meng Bo eats his fill, yet grows,
fearing the king’s awe.
Relying on Four and Five’s shield,
he bears fortune back to his chamber.

**Meng (Hexagram 4):**
A rotted carriage, emaciated steeds,
unfit to bear bit or bridle.
The noble one dons it—
how lightly he speaks of ease!

**Xu (Hexagram 5):**
Betrothed, then wed,
profit and blessing rest upon her.
Marrying Hui to bear Huan,
she becomes our lord of Lu.

**Song (Hexagram 6):**
Entering the gate, great joy—
ascending the hall, she sees her mother.
Wife and children all present,
brothers abound in wealth.

**Shi (Hexagram 7):**
Pushing the cart up the mountain,
strength cannot bear the task.
Stumbling, slipping, falling—
wounding my heart within.

**Bi (Hexagram 8):**
The hawk flies away,
refusing to feed its young.
Even birds act thus—
how can man claim honor?

**Xiao Xu (Hexagram 9):**
Fortune flees, abandoning me,
profit cannot be grasped.
The reclusive one finds advantage in constancy—
in the end, no resentment or deceit.

**Lü (Hexagram 10):**
Husband and wife glare,
unable to govern the household.
The duke says, "Go south,"
the lady says, "Return north."
Two queens, two heirs—
dual rule sows chaos in the state.

**Tai (Hexagram 11):**
Yang wanes, concealed in hiding,
yin’s excess becomes a thief.
Fortunately, the king’s grandson
reaches home and state at last.

**Pi (Hexagram 12):**
Diving into water to seek jade,
neither gem nor rough stone found.
From dawn till dusk—
labor yields no gain.

**Tong Ren (Hexagram 13):**
Phoenix bells chime on four steeds,
driving forth for the royal hunt.
The quarry meets the standard,
offered to the lord with wine.

**Da You (Hexagram 14):**
With a flip of the hand, lifting a calf—
ease turns to accomplishment.
On the first day of the first month,
peace brings forth blessings.

**Qian (Hexagram 15):**
Three fires blaze bright,
rain extinguishes their light.
The high position invites ruin,
arrogance courts destruction.

**Yu (Hexagram 16):**
Wrapping roots in lotus leaves,
fortune meets opportunity.
Soaring high, the gain is made—
the noble one secures good fortune.

**Sui (Hexagram 17):**
Water and earth in harmony,
all things flourish and multiply.
Rich is the nurturing rain—
the noble one reaps reward.

**Gu (Hexagram 18):**
The Dao in harmony, all is well,
no one harms another.
The noble one advances—
joy, profit, and good fortune abound.

**Lin (Hexagram 19):**
The Son of Heaven, child of the gods,
dwells with sun and moon.
Radiant in the world,
blessings and prosperity overflow.

**Guan (Hexagram 20):**
Clinging to rank, unfit for the seat,
the leg breaks, the cauldron overturns—
my lord is wounded.

**Shi He (Hexagram 21):**
The magpie retreats mid-flight,
undertakings fail to succeed.
Hold fast to virtue and power—
lest all be lost.

**Bi (Hexagram 22):**
Crowning with mulberry and jujube,
pride swells without end.
Jie and Zhou, deluded and confused,
slander harms the worthy—
the state topples into chaos.

**Bo (Hexagram 23):**
Shen and You retreat, stumbling,
dark rain falls ahead.
Branches and blossoms,
muddied, no longer white.

**Fu (Hexagram 24):**
The lowly rise to serve,
enduring bitter toil.

**Wu Wang (Hexagram 25):**
Fishing and weaving by the river’s edge,
waters swell without bound.
Shaking out robes, returning in vain—
above and below lost in confusion,
the lord’s path grows perilous.

**Da Xu (Hexagram 26):**
The embryo nurtured, life stirs,
first signs take shape.
Struck by thunder and lightning,
horns break, necks snap.
Yet in the mountain chamber,
all stands firm, unshaken.

**Yi (Hexagram 27):**
Spring’s yang withers,
summer’s floods overflow.
Frost and hail descend together,
harming my millet and grain—
the year’s harvest brings hardship.

**Da Guo (Hexagram 28):**
Three ears, six teeth,
pain and illness unceasing.
Rot and decay gnaw away—
the dwelling collapses.

**Kan (Hexagram 29):**
Out of season, without companions,
a fine mate departs—
like a dog bereft of its master.

**Li (Hexagram 30):**
Proclaiming care for the humble,
the year brings joy, the harvest bountiful.
The state knows no fault—
the noble one rests in peace.

**Xian (Hexagram 31):**
Ascending the steps, mounting the chariot,
driving four steeds southward.
Alliances shift and scatter—
Yan and Qin grow strong.

**Heng (Hexagram 32):**
Birds gather in lush trees,
hearts glad, desires fulfilled.
Crows and magpies gape,
receiving food from the beak.
Gentle and yielding, favorable and upright—
moved to gratitude for the compassionate mother.

**Dun (Hexagram 33):**
The first sprouts emerge,
all things flourish in beauty.
Fortune’s blessings not yet complete—
the market’s traders gain no profit.

**Da Zhuang (Hexagram 34):**
The arrogant Hu dog,
creating evil, committing violence.
Nothing is accomplished—
it destroys itself.

**Jin (Hexagram 35):**
In a foreign land, distant soil,
a fine steed appears.
It flees like a painted arrow—
harm cannot touch it.

**Ming Yi (Hexagram 36):**
Dutiful and respectful, striving in office,
the heart harbors no deceit.
The lord is enlightened, the minister loyal—
the people rely on their fortune.

**Jia Ren (Hexagram 37):**
Three maidens seek husbands,
waiting by the mountain’s edge.
Guan Pass remains unseen—
long they sigh in sorrow.

**Kui (Hexagram 38):**
Riding fortune, borne by joy,
eastward to a blessed land.
Bearing blessings, journeying south,
leaving home to dwell in peace.

**Jian (Hexagram 39):**
Four traitors bring ruin,
the road to Lu grows harsh.
The vanguard bears the labor—
guard well, and know no harm.

**Sun (Hexagram 41):**
Below, worry; above, vexation.
Worms gnaw at governance—
famine comes, the year yields naught.

**Yi (Hexagram 42):**
The hen’s chicks are lost,
ever fearing the fox.
At Huangchi, the covenant is sealed—
Yue’s kingdom shall prosper.

**Yang (Hexagram 45):**
Hard ice, yellow birds,
ever wailing in grief.
No grain is seen—
only thistles and weeds.
Magpies and crows startle,
stirring my heart’s distress.

**Shen (Hexagram 46):**
Jade-sharp iron jaws,
granaries lie empty.
The market swells with profit—
yet turns against me as foe.
The source of wealth eludes me,
loss becomes my labor.

**Cui (Hexagram 45):**
Usurping name and rank,
dwelling where one does not belong.
Frost strikes, fruit withers—
seized by yin’s treachery,
three years without a home.

**Sheng (Hexagram 46):**
Betraying kindness, wounding virtue,
Heaven’s wrath denies its blessing.
The household altar is cut down,
its foundational city lost.

**Kun (Hexagram 47):**
All things harmonize and thrive,
buried creatures stir to life.
Titles rise, fortune grows—
daily joy is received.

**Jing (Hexagram 48):**
Where harmonious qi arises,
nothing decays.
Sages hold office—
the land knows no misfortune.

**Ge (Hexagram 49):**
Dragons dance, phoenixes soar,
the year brings joy to the people.

**Ding (Hexagram 50):**
Step by step, constrained,
next to the elder’s lodge.
Dwelling in peace, fearless—
what worry for wife or concubine?

**Zhen (Hexagram 51):**
Waters too deep to swim,
frost too cold to cross.
The traveler lingers.

**Gen (Hexagram 52):**
Orion and Antares lose their advantage,
the lame and the blind follow one another.
At dusk, the ox is spent.
Crossing the hills brings injury—
profit lost, the female gone.

**Jian (Hexagram 53):**
One ox, nine locks,
entwined in mutual restraint.
The market gleams bright,
yet nothing can be bound.
Seeking recognition brings retribution—
by midday, punishment falls.

**Gui Mei (Hexagram 54):**
Spring peaches bloom,
the youngest daughter finds a home.
Blessings abound—
her son becomes a lord.

**Feng (Hexagram 55):**
Thunder drums the eastward march,
crops wither and fade.
The minister governs,
the lord praises his wisdom.

**Lü (Hexagram 56):**
A lord of the declining age,
his land in chaos, he wanders in excess.
Disaster strikes swiftly—
the people share his ruin.

**Xun (Hexagram 57):**
Drawing the bow, warming the sun,
rain passes, lodging in the chamber.
Timely harmony spreads—
nothing remains blocked.

**Dui (Hexagram 58):**
A great merchant on the waters,
seeking ten thousand in profit.
No traders arrive—
the market stands empty.

**Huan (Hexagram 59):**
Spring grasses sprout,
all things flourish in splendor.
Yin and yang harmonize—
the land rejoices, free of care.

**Jie (Hexagram 60):**
Left eye blind, right eye dim,
vision obscured.
The people suffer affliction,
the lord loses his way.

**Zhong Fu (Hexagram 61):**
Joy within brings peace,
no advantage in venturing out.
Worries dissolve—
what fault lies with the lord’s grandson?

**Xiao Guo (Hexagram 62):**
The written decree is true,
words bear no falsehood.
Exchanging my scaled steed—
the noble one holds virtue.

**Ji Ji (Hexagram 63):**
Governance falters and shakes,
pests and blight arise as one.
My fine grain is harmed—
the year’s end yields no harvest.

**Wei Ji (Hexagram 64):**
Banners and flags wave,
standards raised in the wilds.
Though jade and treasure abound,
no path leads to their delivery.

**Sun (Hexagram 41):**
The road bristles with thorns,
each step pierces my foot.
No fortune for the traveler—
bitterness fills the heart.

**Qian (Hexagram 1):**
Carp, sturgeon, and bream,
a bounty of fish, fortune amassed.
What was lacking is supplied—
my impoverished home grows rich.

**Kun (Hexagram 2):**
Auspicious stars illuminate the hall,
unicorns wander, phoenixes soar.
Benevolence spreads far—
hymns of praise arise.

**Zheng (Hexagram 16):**
The traveler lacks clarity,
losing favor and light.

**Yu (Hexagram 16) → Jie (Hexagram 60):**

**Tun (Hexagram 3):**
The sheep’s gut path winds ninefold,
pushing forward step by step.
Only the lord’s grandson may reach heaven.

**Meng (Hexagram 4):**
Four hands share one body,
none lose their purpose.
Yet in constant exchange,
action loses its advantage.

**Xu (Hexagram 5):**
Waters flow downward,
rushing eastward.
Seeking what I possess—
the merchant offers millet and carp.

**Yi (Hexagram 42) → Wu Qie (No Hexagram):**

**Song (Hexagram 6):**
Spring chestnuts, summer jujubes,
mountain delicacies, rare and few.
Weighing thousands, measuring ten thousand—
too precious to be cheap.

**Pi (Hexagram 12) → Jian (Hexagram 53):**

**Shi (Hexagram 7):**
Morning gone, evening returned,
aiding one another in gathering—
no misfortune befalls.

**Bi (Hexagram 8):**
A great serpent blocks the road,
filling the youngest with dread.
Fire and scalding disaster—
my flesh is seared.
By Heaven’s grace,
I return to my home.

**Tun (Hexagram 3) → Jing (Hexagram 48):**

**Xiao Xu (Hexagram 9):**
Fleeing on foot from the city,
chaos drives me into Chen.
Fearful, I hide—
buried deep in concealment.

**Lü (Hexagram 10):**
The sea, source of all waters,
wise and sagely.
A hundred streams return to it—
none rebel, ever abundant.

**Tai (Hexagram 11):**
Summer wheat withers,
frost strikes its awns.
The ailing lord ruins his state—
the year suffers great harm.

**Tai (Hexagram 11) → Ze (Hexagram 21):**

**Pi (Hexagram 12):**
Autumn chariots, winter wings,
treading frost again and again.
The male dog howls at night—
the household knows no peace.

**Tong Ren (Hexagram 13):**
Delighting in kindness, exalting virtue,
eastern neighbors admire righteousness,
coming to settle my land.

**Da You (Hexagram 14):**
Pursuing sorrow, dispelling calamity,
mud gives rise to beams—
low fields become rivers.

**Qian (Hexagram 15):**
Darkness and obscurity,
words twisted in transmission.
Ghosts and demons dwell here—
who knows what lies beyond?

**Yu (Hexagram 16):**
Southward to Jade Mountain,
eastward to Jade Pass.
Ascending the hall of fortune,
drinking the wine of ten thousand years.

**Sui (Hexagram 17):**
Paired eyes, four wings,
coming to secure my land.

**Xun (Hexagram 57):**
Drawing the bow, warming the sun,
rain passes, lodging in the chamber.
Timely harmony spreads—
nothing remains blocked.

**Fu Shan (Fortune and Virtue):**
Ascending the hall of blessing,
dwelling with me in the same grove.

**Gu (Hexagram 18):**
Riding an ox in pursuit of a steed,
day wanes yet it does not arrive.
Resting on the road, many fears—
losing its carved words.

**Lin (Hexagram 19):**
Supremely auspicious, without blame,
secure and peaceful, free from peril.

**Guan (Hexagram 20):**
Flapping wings, beating pinions,
soaring beyond the frontier.
The Dao distant, lingering in vain—
returning to the warm chamber.

**Shi He (Hexagram 21):**
The River Lord weds a bride,
a maiden of the Eastern Mountains.
Three days into the marriage,
floating clouds scatter rain.
Dew moistens my thatch and reeds—
ten thousand realms receive blessing.

**Bi (Hexagram 22):**
An infant seeks milk,
a kind mother returns to her child.
The Yellow Demon rejoices,
finding sweetness and satiety.

**Bo (Hexagram 23):**
A destitute ghost guards the gate,
shattering my jars by day.
Broken urns, cracked vases—
emptiness, no offspring.

**Fu (Hexagram 24):**
Bearing a heavy load,
discarding it in the wild.
No one to lend a hand—
only self-inflicted toil.

**Wu Wang (Hexagram 25):**
A male fox slinks slowly,
ascending the towering peak.
Proclaiming its manifest merit,
great fortune truly arises.

**Da Xu (Hexagram 26):**
An infant’s startled laughter,
knowing nothing yet.
A cunning youth stirs strife—
disordering my governance.

**Yi (Hexagram 27):**
Ten pellets cast together,
seized by a pheasant’s beak.
Only one escapes,
whole and unharmed.

**Da Guo (Hexagram 28):**
A fox crosses the stream, its tail soaked,
seeking oranges but finding chess pieces.
Ji Jiang regrets her haste,
the abalone’s hall stands empty of fish.

**Kan (Hexagram 29):**
Resting weary feet, easing shoulders,
no difficulty is feared.
A city of gold, walls of bronze,
forged into impregnable gates.
Barriers and screens encircle,
safe and free from harm.

**Li (Hexagram 30):**
Bearing Yao, supporting Yu,
with Peng and Qiao, the ancient ones.
Passing west to the Queen Mother,
the road is smooth and easy—
none dare oppose.

*(See Song and Jia Ren for continuation.)*

**Xian (Hexagram 31):**
Granaries of the capital overflow,
millet and sorghum in abundance.
Travelers arrive swiftly,
their hunger and thirst sated.

**Heng (Hexagram 32):**
The worthy man and Kong Ji,
coerced to ascend the tower.
Chai Ji offers no support,
Wei Zhe flees in haste.

**Lü (Hexagram 56):**
What Heaven bestows,
fortune and blessing ever abide.
No fear of peril or danger.

**Da Zhuang (Hexagram 34):**
Moving, entangled in Heaven’s net—
horse dead, chariot broken.
No refuge remains,
mired in poverty, roots severed.

**Jin (Hexagram 35):**
A leaden blade cuts jade,
unyielding, impossible.
Exhausting all my strength,
calloused hands bring only affliction.

**Ming Yi (Hexagram 36):**
Mu meets Bai Li,
urging Meng to martial prowess.
The general leads the army to battle,
defeated at Ban’s Mouth.

**Jia Ren (Hexagram 37):**
One pursues a fugitive,
concealed by another’s words.
Found before the day is out.

**Kui (Hexagram 38):**
The treasury’s wealth,
the king distributes in relief.
Fishing in rivers and seas,
the nets yield abundant catch.

**Jian (Hexagram 39):**
The swan flies along the land,
the lord returns no more.
Bo Shi lodges as a guest.

**Xie (Hexagram 40):**
Passing a thatched hut of rice,
sweet and fragrant, rich with grain.
Though startled, it does not flee—
Tian Jun bears the worry.

**Yi (Hexagram 42):**
The Rain Master weds a bride,
Huang Yan’s youngest son.
The rites completed, the marriage sealed,
they call to each other and journey south.
Timely rains and fertile soil—
a year of great abundance and joy.

**Guai (Hexagram 43):**
Stores overflowing,
Ji’s land abandoned.
How splendid the offerings!
Emerging with a lofty chariot.

**Zhen (Hexagram 51):**
Gates barred, watchmen’s clappers struck,
armed guards stand vigilant.
Though another path exists,
though startled, no fear.

**Cui (Hexagram 45):**
The great city’s royal market,
teeming with people and treasures.
Gongsun trades wisely,
his wealth multiplied ten thousandfold.

**Sheng (Hexagram 46):**
Autumn gathers, winter takes flight,
repeatedly touched by harsh frost.
Armor and weapons fill the halls—
all things cease to grow.

**Kun (Hexagram 47):**
Summoning misfortune and calamity,
coming to sting my land.

Pain in hands and feet,
no rest, no peace.

**Jing (Hexagram 48):**
Qin loses its deer,
the swift-footed seize it first.
Brave men admire righteousness,
noble ones lead in submission.

**Ge (Hexagram 49):**
Mountains and hills block all four sides,
barring my path.
Wanting to advance but unable,
I return to my old place.

**Ding (Hexagram 50):**
One finger eats meat,
the mouth gains nothing,
the tongue craves for the belly.

**Zhen (Hexagram 51):**
Startled day and night,
not knowing where to stop.
The August Mother aids me,
and I finally find peace.

**Gen (Hexagram 52):**
Capturing the wolf’s words,
speech comes to naught.
It misleads my white horse,
bringing a parched mouth.

**Jian (Hexagram 53):**
Summon the spirit, call the soul,
life revives without sorrow.
Illness fades, healing comes,
dissolving my suffering and grief.

**Guimei (Hexagram 54):**
Herding sheep to chase hares,
making fish catch mice.
Entrusting tasks to the wrong person,
the year ends without success,
only toil and hardship.

**Feng (Hexagram 55):**
Ascending the upper chamber with blessings,
dwelling with fortune.
The imperial princess governs well,
the land is secure, free from worry.

**Lü (Hexagram 56):**
Yu summons the gods,
gathering at Mount Kuaiji in the south.
Holding jade, the myriad states bow—
the world is peaceful and at ease.

**Xun (Hexagram 57):**
Tai Si, the cultured mother,
gives birth to a sage son.
Prosperity flourishes, receiving the mandate,
becoming lord of all under heaven.

**Dui (Hexagram 58):**
Two rivals in one house,
the hare—who can it tell?
Clashing with the mad,
it suffers harm and evil.

**Huan (Hexagram 59):**
The peach-bird steals fat,
nesting on a slender branch.
Shaken, unsteady,
blown by the wind.
Chilled to the heart, trembling with fear,
ever in dread of danger.

**Jie (Hexagram 60):**
In the long days of spring,
the myriad things bloom and bear fruit,
joyful in fortune’s blessings.
*Alternatively:* Spring’s yang flourishes,
the myriad things mature.
Fortune and profit converge,
days pass in abundance.

**Zhongfu (Hexagram 61):**
Neighbors ignore me,
yearning for the jade maiden.
Afflicted with sores and scabs,
who would find me alluring?

**Xiaoguo (Hexagram 62):**
Drought parches the land, no rain falls,
the marsh dries, its streams cease.
Fish and turtles gasp,
but Heaven remains unmoved.

**Jiji (Hexagram 63):**
In the land of wolves and tigers,
daily strife and fierce disputes.
Greedy by nature, insatiable,
they tolerate no restraint.

**Weiji (Hexagram 64):**
Yin clings to yang’s illness,
water leaves its home.
Boats and oars stir greatly,
harming millet and grain.
The people hunger for food,
their hearts and bellies ache.

**Yi (Hexagram 42):**
**Yi:**
King Wen’s four breasts,
benevolence deep and sincere.
Raising ten sons,
none died young.

**Qian:**
Descending the hall, stepping through the gate,
east and west to the nine mountains.
Encountering fortune and joy,
finding peace and ease.

**Kun:**
A crow on the city wall,
cawing, it brings ruin to the house.
Summoning foul poison,
it becomes the land’s disaster.

**Zhun:**
Bo Hu and Zhong Xiong,
their virtue profound.
They spread the five grains,
yin and yang follow in order.

**Meng:**
Drinking wine, drunk in the streets,
leaping up to fight.
Elder and younger brothers fall,
the family prepares for mourning.

**Xu:**
Four eyes meet,
gradually drawing closer, joining hands.
After the sun sets,
I see my aunt.

**Song:**
Following the times, seizing opportunity,
not missing the gate of profit.
The spirit gains fortune,
wealth surpassing a lord’s.

**Shi:**
In Longxi and Jibei,
many fine steeds appear.
They depart like a flock taking flight—
harm cannot touch them.

**Bi:**
White dragon, black tiger,
rising and falling in fury.
They vow to battle in the heavens;
Chiyou flees in defeat,
dying at Fish Head.
*See* **Tongren**’s **Bi**, **Meng**’s **Kan**.

**Xiaoxu:**
The swan soars to the heavens,
escaping harm in the purple abyss.
Though sharp blades await,
they cannot endanger its life.

**Lü:**
The land is uneven,
the House of Xia stirs rebellion.
The Wuniao bow is loosed in secret—
Duke Ling meets his end.

**Tai:**
On the upper reaches of the Jiang and Han,
governance turns perverse, the people grieve.
Yin strikes at yang—
the mighty suffer calamity.

**Pi:**
The eastern household slays its swine,
reeking of foul stench.
The spirits turn in anger, heedless—
the mandate of the failing state is severed.
The temple of Bo burns,
Duke Song is slain.
*See* **Kui**’s **Mingyi**.

**Tongren:**
The western campaign meets defiance,
relying on brute strength.
Doubling back to pursue the foe,
the army flees in rout.

**Dayou:**
One woman, six husbands—
chaos reigns, no order.
Zhang, Wang, Ji, and Zhuang—
none is fit to rule.
The Way of governance is blocked and choked;
the lord of Zhou loses his state.

**Qian:**
A match is arranged, a union sought—
profit lies in the four directions.
The wedding set for dusk,
the bright star shines resplendent.
Joyful and discerning,
their words find right accord.

**Yu:**
The ape falls from the lofty tree,
yet lands unscathed.
Clutching gold, cradling jade,
it returns to its chamber.
*See* **Meng**’s **Sui**, **Song**’s **Gen**, **Pi**’s **Lin**.

**Sui:**
With collar drawn, he withdraws from the world—
benevolent virtue brings no harm.
The Three Sages act as one—
the state of Zhou flourishes in glory.
*See* **Xu**’s **Zhen**.

**Gu:**
Escaping peril, freed from distress,
secure and without fear.
Ascending the hall of fortune and joy,
I see my delight.

**Lin:**
Girded with Ji’er’s goodness,
the hour favors martial might.
The generals join in battle—
the enemy cannot withstand them.
Zhao and Wei grow strong.

**Guan:**
The magpie longs for its mate,
yearning to follow the phoenix east.
Aligning both wings with principle,
it emerges at midday.
Yet it lingers in the northern town,
then returns to its nest.

**Shike:**
Like a startled deer,
unable to steady its hooves.
The household scatters,
each fleeing to hide like rats.
*Or* "together in fear."

**Ben:**
Jia, Yi, Bing, Ding—
all return to my courtyard.
Three fools, six sons—
the eight gates reveal their mother.

**Bo:**
Treading the flower’s peak,
gazing at drifting clouds.
The wind does not sway,
the rain does not lash.
The heart is at peace—
trouble brings no blame.

**Fu:**
Virtue flows and spreads,
profiting the four directions.
The Rain Master sprinkles the roads,
the Wind Earl drives off misfortune.
Patrolling the sacred mountains, offering at the altars—
success is proclaimed.

**Wuwang:**
Water flows downward,
forming the Eastern Sea.
Seeking what I possess—
I trade millet for carp.
*See* **Sun**’s **Xu**.

**Daxu:**
Harmonious qi converges,
moistening and nourishing with rich dew—
it brings forth my fine grain.

**Yi:**
Anxieties dispelled,
disaster does not take form.
Safety has come.

**Daguo:**
On solid ice, the yellow bird
laments in sorrow.
No sweet grain is seen—
only flowering mugwort.
Time and again, magpies and crows startle—
they weigh on my heart.

**Kan:**
Gathering and scattering,
truly it falls and collapses.
Its good name is extinguished—
its lifespan is not whole.
*See* **Tai**’s **Qian**, **Pi**’s **Li**.

**Li:**
Through misfortune, fortune is received—
joy fills its being.

**Xian:**
Dwelling on land a thousand *li* away,
no river or sea is seen—
no fish market exists.

**Heng:**
The deer finds sweet grass,
calling to its companions.
The nine clans live in harmony—
no hunger or want.
*See* **Yi**’s **Heng**, **Tongren**’s **Jian**.

**You:**
Leaving the gate, one finds the hall—
no misfortune is met.
Entering the door, one suffers alone—
no spears or halberds appear.
*Or* "clan."

**Dazhuang:**
Laden with honor, seated on fine mats—
the host commands me.
Fortune and blessing endure long—
no blame or misfortune is seen.

**Jin:**
The swans and geese take flight together,
heading north to the fish ponds.
Carp and bream, perch and bass—
the flock of birds grows abundant.
One cry yields two—
the gain is doubled.

**Mingyi:**
Facing the wind, it spreads its wings,
flying north with the crows.
Entering my homeland,
it sees my hall of celebration.

**Jiaren:**
Qilin and phoenix—
good governance brings auspicious signs.
Yin and yang harmonize—
the state knows no disaster.

**Kui:**
Chasing the fox to the eastern mountains,
water passes before me.
I probe but cannot ford it—
I lose the advantage behind.

**Jian:**
Chou, Xu, Hai, and Zi—
famine is born in these times.
Yin becomes a violent marauder—
the waters cut off my food.

**Xie:**
Foxes, pheasants, and hares
flee in fear of me.
Scattering, they hide—
their whereabouts unknown.

**Sun:**
Jie and Zhou, wicked men—
their deeds are blocked.
Scorching drought brings ruin—
the year’s grain is greatly harmed.

**Guai:**
The rabbit nurses its young in the chamber,
coming and going to feed the sparrows.
The tiger seizes my child—
endless wailing ensues.

**Gou:**
Earthen steps, a bright hall—
ritual and deference flourish.
Male and female unite—
I suffer no illness.
*Or* "affliction."

**Cui:**
Sending forth gold, losing the jade hare.
Coming and going at the well,
the urn is broken, the basin shattered.
*Or* "pill."

**Sheng:**
Chanting virtue, reciting merit—
glorifying Zhou’s flourishing might.
Adding its morning assistance—
the great one aids the central man.
*Or* "the lord."

**Kun:**
Theft and deceit destroy the self—
the two mothers grow distant.
The queen has no faction—
her sacred treasure is defiled.

**Jing:**
In the sixth month, restless clamor—
each desires to arrive.
The expedition is not yet prepared—
they await the bright dawn.
*Or* "six eyes stare blankly."

**Ge:**
The sparrow seeks grain,
mistakenly entering the net’s depths.
Thanks to the benevolent noble—
it is freed and returns home.

**Ding:**
Virtue is vast and bright—
misfortune and disaster do not harm.

**Qi:**
The sworn vow does not arrive—
the household bears sorrow.

**Zhen:**
The tortoise loathes river and sea,
traveling endlessly on land.
It brings itself to wither and dry,
losing its market in the city.
Worry and regret arise—calamity is born.

**Gen:**
The fox dwells alone,
with none to rely on for aid.
The heart is upright, truly steadfast—
the spirit toils, the will suffers.

**Jian:**
Elders linger in speech,
while the younger departs.
Who says there is no fault?
The lady of the house rejoices greatly.

**Guimei:**
At first, unease and disquiet—
later, laughter and fear.
Though fear remains, there is no harm.

**Feng:**
Waging war destroys the state,
the army disregards discipline.
The exalted fall in ruin—
Duke Qi, fierce and cruel,
bears its disaster and curse.

**Lü:**
A deer born in the marsh’s shallows,
a jackal wounds its fawn.
It weeps blood in lonely grief.

**Xun:**
Heaven and earth are sealed and shut—
benevolence and wisdom hide.
Merchants and travelers do not move,
profit and gain are hard to come by.

**Dui:**
The man of blessed virtue
rejoices day by day.
Yi Wu assists Duke Huan—
the Three Returns make him a minister,
his rewards flowing to his descendants.

**Huan:**
Above, no flying birds;
below, no running beasts.

Turmoil remains unresolved,
the people toil in labor.

**Jie:**
The moon wanes, the days decline,
the weaver’s hand leaves the loom.
The cosmos darkens, light fades—
the Three Luminaries vanish.
*See Hexagram Qian.*

**Zhong Fu:**
Wearing a basin, one gazes at heaven,
yet sees not the stars.
Fixating on the small, one loses the great—
fortune flees beyond the wall.

**Xiao Guo:**
Grasping the Dipper, turning the pivot,
following heaven without care.
In conduct, one cultivates virtue,
dwelling in joy as its companion.

**Ji Ji:**
Wielding a halberd to spear fish,
hair unbound, standing in sorrow.
The tiger snatches my chariot,
the wolf takes my robe—
horse lost, wealth gone.

**Wei Ji:**
Two men both drunk,
turn against each other in folly.
Hearts at odds, minds divided,
their strife clamorous.

---

**Guai (43rd Hexagram):**

**Guai:**
Bearing Yao, supporting Yu,
with Pine and Jo, Peng and Zu.
To the west, they meet the Queen Mother—
the road smooth and easy,
none dare oppose them.

**Qian:**
Fierce and cruel, yet plans excel,
no word unfulfilled.
Truly pleasing the heart of the Lord,
joy brings divine favor.

**Kun:**
At year’s end, blossoms fall,
yang enters the chamber of yin.
The myriad things hide in concealment,
utterly beyond reach.

**Zhun:**
The parrot misses its time to sing,
the lord is vexed with sorrow.
Dogs bark without cease,
travelers are detained.

**Meng:**
Startled by lightning, wandering Jing,
the noble one finds peace.
Bearing duty without fault,
fortune and blessings come to fruition.

**Xu:**
Thin as a fence’s skin,
a fierce wind blows it away.
Seeking to ascend, it cannot—
returns to its dwelling.

**Song:**
Eastward journey in a broken cart,
stepping into a perilous house.
The crossbeam sags, the door hangs askew—
none to take as master.
Selling robes to buy food,
yet husks and chaff leave no fullness.

**Shi:**
Black ox, white throat,
calling me to the fields together.
Beneath Li Mountain,
we may till abundantly.
At the season of harvest,
the people dwell in peace.

**Bi:**
Foreign lands, strange customs,
hearts do not align.
Metal and wood turn to foes,
a hundred bandits seize and slay.

**Xiao Xu:**
Yin and yang press close,
the high ripe grain snaps and falls.
Tending eggs, they hatch as ghosts—
first sprouting head and eyes,
the day brings great fortune.

**Lü:**
Hungry worms wreak harm,
entangling chaos unending—
autumn’s harvest cannot be reaped.

**Tai:**
Clear and bright as clouds,
leading the troops forward.
The people, whether in ease or urgency,
know not east from west.

**Pi:**
The cavalry turns the army home,
to rest their weary toil.
The conscripted men rejoice,
entering their doors to see their wives.

**Tong Ren:**
Sitting in dispute, rising in strife,
clamorous and contentious.
At last, calamity arises,
disorder reaches the lord’s house.

**Da You:**
The deer eats sweet grass,
roaming at ease to sate its hunger.
It wanders the mountain passes,
overstaying its time before returning—
glossy and fat, sated.

**Qian:**
Field mice and wild pheasants,
minds set on departure.
Bound in cages and pens,
they cannot stir.

**Yu:**
Pursuing the sun, pacing the moon,
circling through each lodging,
traversing peril to reach afar—
no difficulty arises.

**Sui:**
The grandson of heaven, child of the Lord,
dwells with sun and moon.
Glorious in the world,
fortune and blessings overflow.

**Gu:**
Morning wind, patterned wings,
takes flight toward warmth.
Passing my town,
Yi gains nothing.

**Lin:**
Born at dawn, dies at dusk—
called the infant ghost,
none dare look upon it.

**Guan:**
The sick and poor hope for favor,
sending Bo south to trade.
Opening the pen, selecting the sheep,
great fortune is attained.

**Shi Ke:**
The Great Wall, Mount Li,
the people suffer great harm.
Crossing the well, raising rebellion—
Tang Shu brings disaster.

**Bi:**
Wed to the Jiangs and Lü,
welcoming the bride in a carriage.
Shao Qi at the gate,
the master rejoices.

**Jie:**
Timely grasses and trees,
when the season comes, leaves rise.
Lush and spreading, branches of peach,
tall and flourishing, splendidly blooming.

**Fu:**
Ji and Jiang delight in joy,
the two clans wed.
Frost descends, yet love endures—
Xishi stands before them.

**Wu Wang:**
Wearing a bamboo hat, sleeping alone,
by day not seeing the sun.
Toiling without deception,
long labor brings sorrowful thoughts.

**Da Xu:**
First donning the cap of adulthood,
at twenty, striking the chamber.
Newly wed, joy abounds—
Bo and Ji possess virtue.

**Yi:**
The two solstices at Lingtai,
where the cultured wander and rest.
Clouds and omens all prepared,
enduring joy without care.

**Da Guo:**
Endless rain, ceaseless downpour,
muddy paths, mired travel.
Merchants cease their trade,
the market stands empty.

**Kan:**
The city crumbles, the border is pressed,
repeatedly afflicting Qi.
Invasion unceasing,
lord and minister vexed with worry.
High and low exhausted,
the people lack wealth.

**Li:**
The southern land flourishes,
millet and sweet wine.
One may feast and nourish,
delighting in worthy friends.

**Xian:**
Worry lodges in heart and belly,
inner collapse becomes illness.
Disaster rises within the walls—
the mind governs the state.

**Heng:**
Rotten roots, severed tree,
flowers and leaves fall away.
Suddenly meeting a great crowd,
they topple with the wind.

**Zhu:**
A tree’s shadow serves as altar,
laughing and speaking together.
No meeting at noon,
favor and glory are cast aside.

**Da Zhuang:**
Four legs all run,
the weak nag lags behind.
Twice battling without victory,
defeated by the eastern Chu.

**Jin:**
Holding the reins at court,
returning to the old place.
The wheat blossoms wound the heart—
the uncle has no sorrow.

**Ming Yi:**
Night long, day short,
yin as bandit to yang.
The myriad things wither and empty,
hidden in the northern land.

**Jia Ren:**
The turtledove’s seven chicks,
evenly reared, never endangered.
Grown to maturity,
abandoned yet harmonious.

**Kui:**
Three sheep ascend the mountain,
galloping to the great plain.
The yellow dragon bears the boat,
thus reaching Yi Yang,
exhausting its jade sack.

**Jian:**
Head and feet reversed,
tail and head inverted.

**Gong:**
The lord becomes a crone,
confounding his early wisdom.

**Xie:**
Ascending heights to gaze at home,
toilsome duties never cease.
Royal affairs lack rest—
no leisure for carefree wandering.

**Sun:**
Fearing dusk, he does not proceed,
waiting for dawn to act.
Hunting and burning bring fortune—
the elder relies on this blessing.

**Yi:**
Alone and solitary,
with none to depend on or aid,
his heart labors, his will suffers.

**Ni:**
Mountain stones rot and crumble,
collapsing into ruin.
Above and below, hearts divide—
the lord bears the curse.

**Cui:**
The cultured mother, the sagely son,
boundless in age and longevity,
rule as lords of all under heaven.

**Sheng:**
Stubborn and obstinate in form,
front and rear at odds.
Words like a turtle’s cough—
twisted and unknowable.

**Kun:**
Five dragons leap together,
the strong are routed in defeat.
My sprouts and crops exposed—
the year yields great abundance.

**Jing:**
Thunder dispels the fierce and swift,
yet healing proves difficult.
The steed exhausted by the salt cart,
ensnared by bit and whip.

**Ge:**
In the southlands, locusts swarm,
stinging my hands and feet.
Grievances twist and coil—
pain pierces heart and belly.

**Ding:**
The heart has no foothold,
shooting the deer but missing.
Much speech, little substance—
words accomplish nothing.

**Zhen:**
The lord is enlightened, his ministers virtuous,
calling out to seek their kin.
A governance of manifest power—
thus may one tread the earth.

**Gen:**
At peace in the land, fit for office,
promoted nine times in a day.
Surpassing all peers,
he tends and nurtures Mount Chang.

**Jian:**
Preserving words, resolving grievances,
cleansing away filth and defilement.
What once bred calamity
is now purged of cruelty and harm.

**Guimei:**
The old man raves, the crone is blind,
dragging each other northward.
Longing to return to the lofty city,
yet lost and bewildered.

**Feng:**
Drunk by the roadside,
delirious and sightless,
unfit for my life.

**Lü:**
Northward to Ghost Mound,
riding a dragon on an eastern journey.
The Queen Mother follows behind—
what worry for the civil and martial?

**Xun:**
Serene and untroubled,
playing at the Dao’s gate.
Consorting with spirits,
ever joyful and at peace.

**Dui:**
Exchanging hemp for silk,
clutching cloth to offer oneself.
Discarding rites, growing idle—
in the end, regret and sorrow.

**Huan:**
Adorned in robes and cap,
playing at the Dao’s gate.
Ending with propriety,
the body knows no disaster.

**Jie:**
Heaven’s marsh becomes dry land,
the shore turns to sea’s edge.
The noble one strays from his path—
the petty cling together.

**Zhongfu:**
The deep spring overflows,
a curse upon the town.

**Roads blocked, impassable—**
the child’s heart seethes with indignation.

**Xiaoguo:**
Ten li gazing at smoke,
scattered and dissolved in four directions.
Form and body perish—
one may plunge into the abyss,
yet never see their lord.

**Jiji:**
Rumors mislead,
no fine path to follow.
Beating drums to chase the wolf,
yet unaware how near it lurks.

**Weiji:**
Eastward, the great pearl is lost;
westward, cowardice is cast aside.
Times are often inauspicious,
leaving me to lag behind.

*End of Scroll Two, Part Two*

**#50** Originally written as *háo* (毫), amended to *Bó* (亳) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#51** Originally, *zhū* (诛) lacked the appended note *"Xíng nì, yī zuò wū chòu. Yì zhī pǐ"* (行逆，一作污臭。益之否); supplemented according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
