**#206** Originally written as *gǔ* (谷), amended to *shā* (杀) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#207** Originally written as *yē* (耶), amended to *luǎn* (卵) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#208** *"Kuān"* (宽), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"yuān"* (冤).
**#209** Originally written as *líng* (灵), amended to *luàn* (乱) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#210** *"Qián shì"* (潜视), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"dé sì"* (得祀).
**#211** *"Luó"* (萝), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"guàn"* (灌), and *"guàn"* is deemed correct.
**#212** Originally written as *bō* (拨), amended to *xiān* (祆) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#213** Originally written as *liàn* (练), amended to *shū* (舒) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#214** *"Hán"* (含), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"hé"* (合).
**#215** Originally written as *rú* (如), amended to *jiā* (加) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#216** Originally written as *yòu* (佑), amended to *yǒu* (友) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#217** Originally written as *sāo shí* (骚什), amended to *jiāng pū* (僵仆) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#218** *"Nú"* (驽), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"nú"* (奴).
**#219** Originally written as *rèn* (任), amended to *zài* (在) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#220** Originally written as *hé yú* (合於), amended to *ér hé* (而合) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#221** Originally written as *yòng* (用), amended to *yuán* (原) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#222** Originally written as *zhú* (逐), amended to *suì* (遂) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#223** *"Yáng"* (阳), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"shāng"* (伤).
**#224** Originally written as *wǎn* (宛), amended to *jiū* (究) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#225** Originally written as *qiě* (且), amended to *dàn* (旦) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#226** Originally written as *zhì yáng* (致羊), amended to *zhì kǔ* (志苦) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#227** Originally written as *suì* (祟), amended to *suì* (祟) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#228** Originally written as *suī* (虽), amended to *nán* (难) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#229** Originally written as *chū* (出), amended to *kùn* (困) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#230** *"Shí"* (实), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"xiě"* (写).
**#231** Originally written as *bù* (不), amended to *wēng* (翁) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#232** Originally written as *gōng* (公), amended to *bù* (不) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#233** Originally written as *chū* (出), amended to *lè* (乐) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#234** Originally written as *qíng* (情), amended to *duò* (惰) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#235** *"Tiān"* (天), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"dà"* (大).
**#236** Originally written as *chóng* (崇), amended to *suì* (祟) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#237** *"Fēn"* (分), the *Baizi Quanshu* has *"fāng"* (方).
**#238** The *Baizi Quanshu* includes an appended note under *"jūn"* (君): *"fāng yī zuò fēn"* (方一作分).
**#239** Originally written as *tán* (谈), amended to *wù* (误) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.
**#240** Originally written as *jīng* (经), amended to *jìng* (径) according to the *Baizi Quanshu*.

*Yìlín*, Scroll 3 of the Lower Volume, *Gòu* Hexagram, Forty-Fourth.

**Pregnancy**
The River Earl cries out in great clamor—
the ford cannot be crossed.
Going and returning, he shows the old cause,
and thus no great regret arises.

**Qian**
Veiled in grace and favor,
growing tall to achieve greatness.
Gentle, yielding, and rightly steadfast,
lord and minister unite in harmony.

**Kun**
Mount Shu to the east, Mount Xi to the west,
each rests in its own place.
Though they long to ascend and gaze afar,
they never share the same hall.

**Zhun**
Ascending the mountain, entering the valley,
encountering the tiger.
Claiming it as the Merit Officer,
Ban Shu flees north—
deliverance comes to the blessed land.

**Meng**
Stumbling and falling, unable to rise,
losing profit in the later market,
the fawn is not obtained.

**Xu**
Stringing pearls, clasping shoes,
humbling oneself in thought,
becoming the lord’s servant and maid.

**Song**
The parrot cries out, missing its time—
the people wander, weary and toiling.
The dog barks without cease,
travelers are delayed.

**Shi**
Chen Mao and Jing Zhong,
the north gives rise to Qi Jiang.
Yingqiu establishes the heir—
eight generations flourish greatly.
*(See Zhun’s* Shike *and* Bi’s *Yu.)*

**Bi**
The deer, fearing man, hides,
both entering the deep valley.
Short-lived, not long enduring,
seized by the tiger,
it dies in its jaws and belly.

**Xiaoxu**
Words without binding agreement,
no contract is formed.
The Yin lord’s younger sister,
contested by the Duke’s grandson.
Forcibly entering to present the betrothal gifts,
his heart finds no joy—
thus he goes to Zinan.

**Fu**
Striking the zither, singing and dancing,
delighting in wine.
The dragon opens its mouth,
great joy comes afterward.

**Tai**
Calamity, sorrow, and disaster,
growing ever more manifest.
The misfortune cannot be saved—
the king retreats, wounded by Yi.

**Pi**
Water flows downward,
eventually forming the eastern sea.
The dragon opens its mouth,
seeking what I possess,
trading mutton for carp.

**Tongren**
Yin becomes a thief to Yang—
the lord cannot overcome it.
Actions lose their proper measure,
no profit is gained.

**Dayou**
The bed is overturned, the table lost—
the tortoise forfeits its wish.
No gathering in the marketplace,
Shu and Ji harbor resentment.

**Qian**
Dams and dikes obstruct,
water cannot flow.
Great caution in the face of Yang’s advance.
Yin’s rainbow hides in concealment,
first returning to its homeland.

**Yu**
The tortoise withdraws its belly, stretches its limbs,
riding the floating clouds eastward,
honored and favored before its mother.

**Sui**
The fruit sinks into the starry ruins,
severed by righteousness.
Next, Lu submits to punishment,
completing my hegemonic achievement.

**Gu**
Golden springs and yellow treasures—
fit for trading with me.
Marriage and childbirth bring increase,
profit comes after passing the mother.

**Lin**
Yu summons all the spirits,
gathering at Mount Kuaiji in the south.
Holding jade, the myriad states—
the world is at peace.

**Guan**
Three worms create decay,
treading their path alone.
Victory Mother, Thief Spring—
the noble person does not dwell there.

**Shike**
Flowers and leaves fall,
the lord returns to the ancestral hall.
Yi’s descendants lose the people,
purifying themselves, they do not eat.

**Bi**
Treading the loom, fearing destruction,
the prince is cast aside.
Yet in the end, his desire is fulfilled,
with no misfortune or harm.

**Bo**
The Dao is harmonious, virtue unharmed.
The noble person fares forth—
I gain good fortune.

**Fu**
Gourd and calabash share the pen,
Ji and Jiang dwell together,
long-lived and enduring.

**Wuwang**
The *Guanju*’s virtuous maiden,
worthy consort and sagely mate.
A harmonious household, a long-lived mother—
blessings and fortune endure.

**Daxu**
The fine colt sheds its milk,
unaware of its foal’s whereabouts.
Turning in sorrow, it cries out—
my heart is pained and grieved.

**Yi**
Knowing strictness, cutting off reason,
Yin’s treachery schemes against the king.
Ten days without food,
confined in Shen and Hai.

**Daguo**
Carving and chiseling jade,
nothing is not fittingly shaped.
The scaled phoenix takes form,
embodying the noble person.
Three men assist in the task—
what is sought will surely bring joy.
*(One version reads "benevolence.")*
*"Carving and chiseling jade"* refers to the work of shaping jade.
*"Nothing is not fittingly shaped"* means that carving will surely yield results.

**Kan**
At dusk, riding the carriage,
arriving at Bo’s home.
Crossing the Yu Bridge over the river,
safely delivered, no other mishap.

**Li**
I possess great millet,
heaped in the outer field.
With horns and a boxed carriage,
it is transported to my storehouse,
enriching my fine roots.

**Xian**
Rejoicing, laughing, and speaking,
unable to cover one’s mouth.
Titles and ranks arrive together,
celebrations fill the gate.

**Heng**
Mist, dew, snow, and frost—
the sun darkens, unclear.
Yin’s treachery brings illness,
the year’s harvest is greatly damaged.

**Geng**
My elder brother departs eastward,
his hair like flying tumbleweed.
Long nights of sighing,
tossing and turning in the empty grove.
Inwardly filled with sorrow and regret,
my heart breaks, my liver and bowels ache.

**Dazhuang**
Losing the sheep, seizing the pen—
the Zhang family loses its ox.
The swift steeds scatter,
the magpie steals my fish.

**Jin**
Selling rats and cages,
little profit, no plan—
hard to establish a household.

**Mingyi**
The Western Rong bring illness,
the secluded lord leaves his chamber.
Chen Zi raises the rebellion,
Xiang Bo completes the chaos.

**Jiaren**
Autumn wind stirs sorrow,
flowers fall, the heart grieves.
The royal house faces many troubles,
the Menggu clan declines.
*(One version reads "Yangshe.")*

**Kui**
Holding fortune, suppressing calamity,
removing great ruin.
Day lengthens, night ends—
a fine era receives grace.

**Jian**
Newly receiving great joy,
fortune and blessings return in abundance.
Joyful and growing daily in wealth,
resources suffice, riches overflow.

**Xie**
Formerly stumbling and tripping,
left foot falters, right foot resists.
Ascending high with a secure ladder,
one returns home once more.

**Sun**
Dreaming of rice yet still hungry,
wine yet to touch the lips.
Though the young woman is fair,
the matchmaker denies consent.

**Yi**
In the great capital’s market,
the crowd teems with treasures.
Gongsun should buy,
profiting a myriad-fold.
*(Disaster here reads as "goods.")*

**Fu**
Two men both drunk,
quarreling in confusion.
Hearts at odds, discordant,
their dispute rages fiercely.

**Cui**
Body without head or feet,
leaping and stumbling, all goes awry.
Unable to flee far,
midway exhausted, resting—
losing profit in the later market.

**Sheng**
Three walk together,
six eyes bright and clear.
On the road, they meet a fair maiden,
who bears me a fine steed.

**Kun**
A scholar taking office
would do better to return to the fields,
gaining longevity and preserving years.

**Jing**
First easy, then difficult,
I lose what I sought to buy.
Distressed and weary, self-tormented,
I long for my former affairs.

**Ge**
Su Qin speaks,
Han and Wei free from harm.
Zhang Zi’s persuasive words spread,
bringing peace to Yan and Qi.

**Ding**
The armory and military storehouse,
where armor and weapons gather.
Not a village or town,
one must not lodge here.
*(This is the "Jian" of "Shi.")*

**Zhen**
Two peaches for three mouths,
none knows with whom to share.
Playing the ox for the child,
the Tian clan courts disaster.

**Gen**
Western Mountain and Eastern Mountain,
each rests in its own place.
Though they gaze upon one another,
they never share the same hall.

**Jian**
Not altering branch or leaf,
harmonious qi flows smoothly.
Where the noble one dwells,
there is peace without fear.

**Guimei**
About to bind Xu to Hai,
Yang hides and does not rise.
The noble ones scatter in chaos,
the Supreme One faces peril.

**Feng**
The celestial offices array the stars,
the Five Spirits dwell in their chambers.
Palace gates secure and firm,
the lord rests safely in his abode.

**Lü**
Left hand grasping water,
like light or a ghost—
it cannot be moved.

**Xun**
Chasing the fox on Eastern Mountain,
water blocks my path ahead.
Too deep to ford,
I lose advantage in the aftermath.

**Dui**
Water channels and fish ponds
overflow into my town.
Breaching my home,
they frolic with the dogs.

**Huan**
Mountains steep and hard to climb,
ravines filled with stones.
The cart races, axles strike,
heavily laden, the axle breaks.
Bearing the load, one stumbles,
right foot faltering.

**Jie**
The trough empty, no substance,
the piglet’s snout cut, it will not eat.
The common folk exhausted,
they abandon their homes.

**Zhongfu**
Grasping heat, hands blister—
a great calamity arises.
Gongsun acts without restraint,
ruining our royal house.

**Xiaoguo**
Three tigers ascend the mountain,
biting and devouring one another.
Hearts not aligned in kinship,
they treat each other as foes and enemies.

**Jiji**
The western family marries off their daughter,
borrowing neighbors to send her off.
Praising my fair lady,
host and guest rejoice together.

**Weiji**
Cultivating the self, purifying the body,
encountering Yu’s imperial tour.
Bestowed with a dark jade tablet,
I bow and receive blessings.

**Hua 45**

**Cui**
Receiving auspicious fortune,
gaining something of worth.
Unfavorable to leave the city,
the sick are utterly exhausted.

**Qian**
The great rat with four feet
cannot fly onto the roof.
Yan Yuan’s virtue,
yet without rank or salary.

**Kun**
Newly receiving great joy,
fortune and office multiply.
Joyful and growing daily in wealth.

**Zhun**
Cultivating the self, purifying the body,
encountering Yu’s imperial tour.
Bestowed with a dark jade tablet,
I bow and receive blessings.
*(This is the "Weiji" of "Shen.")*

**Meng**
The basket misplaced, the basket lost,
the wheel broken, no support.
The Household Elder governs,
afflicting my lands below.

**Xu**
Words on the tip of the tongue yet unspoken,
the dull-witted cannot express them.
Qi and Lu become enemies,
I lose Kuiqiu.

**Song**
Losing the awl, the axe misplaced,
Gongshu lacks aid.
Holding his ritual vessels,
he seeks the noble one’s abode.
*(One version places the two lines of "Meng" below "Song," and the two lines of "Song" below "Meng.")*

**Shi**
Dwelling by the sea’s edge,
short oars struggle in deep currents.
Bo Shi finds travel difficult,
no wood to cross over.

**Bi**
Virtue flows and spreads,
benefiting the four directions.
The Rain Master sprinkles the path,
the Wind Earl drives away misfortune.
Touring and offering sacrifices at sacred mountains,
announcing success.

**Xiaoxu**
The basket overturns, the basket spills—
I fear my lord’s placement.
Jian Bo acts without propriety,
the Grand Tutor corrects the meal.

**Lü**
Mired in filth and disgrace,
cast aside into ditches.
Mocked by the crowd,
one never attains eminence.

**Tai**
Monkeys and hares scurry,
foul and restless, little flesh.
A leaking vessel filled with wine?
No profit to be had.

**Pi**
The deer fears men and hides,
together entering the deep valley.
Life short, not long—
seized by the tiger,
dying in its jaws and belly.

**Tongren**
Southern Mountain’s orchids,
the noble one’s possession.
The eastern family’s fair maiden,
bearing jade into my chamber.

**Dayou**
Pointing left, waving right,
gazing askance in extravagance.
Holding the tally without virtue,
the spirit lord perishes.

**Qian**
Rank and position unclear,
harmed by ministers.
The yin forces gather in crowds,
together eclipsing the sun’s light.

**Yu**
Piercing the nose, tethering to a post,
seized by the tiger.
The Queen Mother prays,
disaster does not come to pass—
suddenly, one breaks free.

**Sui**
A poverty-stricken ghost guards the gate,
daily breaking my pots.
The rat gnaws, the jar is damaged—
empty and childless.

**Gu**
King Xiang girds eastward,
relying on the men of Zheng.
Duke Zhuang’s ministers,
the Queen Mother’s joy and sorrow.

**Lin**
Zhaojun guards the state,
all Xia receives her virtue.
Though of different kind,
she does not harm our royal house.

**Guan**
Winter’s thickets rot and decay,
exposed to wind on the road.
Covered in dust,
left and right toil in hardship.

**Shike**
The six lines established,
the divine luminaries declare.

**Wen Ding**
Auspicious and propitious, Kang Shu receives fortune.

**Bi**
Tears flow in long farewell,
my heart finds no joy.
Far sent to the wilds of Wei,
returning to pay respects brings no blame.

**Bo**
Three nights without a host,
southward journey brings toil and hardship.
Bound in the village, losing profit,
treasure is lost.
This hexagram follows *Bo*.

**Fu**
The great axe splits the wood,
slanderous flatterers ruin the state.
Bound at the pass, a skilled artisan—
calamity befalls three sons.
The people of Jin throw the city into chaos,
Duke Huai flees in exile.

**Wu Wang**
Riding the wind to ascend the heavens,
serving the times with a noble carriage.
Circling ten thousand li,
I face trials and hardship.

**Da Xu**
A great tree with a hundred roots,
linked to the mountain’s side.
Lord Wen enacts righteousness,
receiving ten thousand years of fortune.

**Yi**
Yang lies hidden below,
yin governs and grants fortune.
Born out of time,
the hidden dragon lurks in concealment.

**Da Guo**
A disheveled head brings many worries,
scratching lice breeds sorrow.
The steward Zhongnian
leaves me desolate.

**Kan**
The Yangtze, the Yellow River, the Huai, the seas—
heaven’s markets.
Merchants receive fortune,
the nation grows rich.

**Li**
Mount Tai’s secluded valleys,
where the phoenix roams and rests.
Rites and propriety in order,
one may seek fortune.

**Xian**
Water and mountain rage violently,
beams collapse, pillars snap.
Travelers delay, journeys stall,
lingering in sorrow and hardship.

**Heng**
The wise minister harnesses the carriage,
Taiyi bears the journey.
Passing through time and lodging,
wherever one goes brings prosperity.

**Guang**
Three nights without a host,
southward journey brings toil and hardship.
Bound in the village, losing profit,
her treasure is lost.
This hexagram follows *Bo*.

**Da Zhuang**
Born without parents,
leaving home brings no joy.
Buying pepper, losing grain—
my great profit is gone.

**Jin**
Seated in the jade hall,
listening to music, passing the cup.
Drinking fortune by the ten thousand goblets,
daily receiving boundless blessings.

**Ming Yi**
Ascending peril, entering distress,
the four seasons shift.
Spring frost, summer snow—
all things wither and fall.

**Jia Ren**
Clothes threadbare, shoes worn through,
no means to ward off the cold.
Petty and impoverished,
unable to care for oneself.

**Kui**
Eyes cannot close,
worry comes—scratching the feet.
Fear and dread linger,
departing from the state’s borders.

**Jian**
Offering cowries to ransom the fox,
it does not heed my words.
Grasping the tiger’s whiskers,
it cannot be led away.

**Xie**
Boyi and Shuqi,
paragons of integrity and purity.
With virtue they ward off disaster,
sorrow and misfortune do not arise—
their fragrant names endure through time.

**Sun**
Zhang, Wang, Zi, and Ji,
contending over wealth, restraining one another.
Lord Shang, obstinate and stubborn,
knowing not the way forward.

**Yi**
The Great Wall stands complete,
the four barbarians submit in awe.
Exchanging peace and forging bonds,
Zhaojun brings fortune.

**Guai**
A thousand joys, ten thousand delights,
undertakings are decided.
Receiving fine blessings,
actions yield success.

**Sheng**
Plant one, reap ten,
daily growth and increase.
Benevolent governance wins the people,
the four states live in harmony.

**Sheng**
Lord An abounds in wealth,
the eastern state suffers no calamity.
Qi and Zheng make peace,
their alliance brings joy.

**Kun**
Nine li, ten mountains,
the path looms steep and treacherous.
Oxen and horses will not advance—
turning back, they return.

**Jing**
The turtledove staff supports the elderly,
clothing and feeding a hundred mouths.
The great-grandson lives long,
evil does not arise.

**Ge**
Mist, dew, snow, and frost,
the sun dims, its light obscured.
Yin’s corruption breeds illness,
the year’s harvest suffers great harm.

**Ding**
Wandering, retreating repeatedly,
knowing not east from west.
Yin’s strength turns violent and rebellious,
the road is blocked.

**Zhen**
Ascending the heights, climbing the mountain,
speaking to the king of my grievance.
Truth and reason clear my wrongs,
I receive office and favor.

**Gen**
Three generations of virtue,
heaven bestows the state.
Enfeoffing Shaohao,
bringing fortune to the Lord of Lu.

**Jian**
The towering tree offers no rest,
the Han maiden is hard to obtain.
The spirit of the catalpa
asks for your girdle-pendant—
turn your hand, and you part from her.

**Gui Mei**
Eastern neighbor, western household,
coming to consult with me.
Their message bears good faith,
bringing the lord peace and tranquility.

**Feng**
Tearing clothes to flee the house,
the heart longs to run.
The prince’s mother is alarmed—
this grants me long life.

**Lü**
Three days without drink,
distant waters hold no wine.
Day and night, a parched throat—
this brings me blame.

**Xun**
A thousand mouths melt metal,
false words prove untrue.
Rotten and foul, the rabbit unsold—
the eight markets see no trade.

**Dui**
The old woman wears a cap at the gate,
arguing with the elder.
The eastern household loses its dog,
its intent no longer exists.
Strife and chaos unceasing,
severing what I cherish.

**Huan**
Fortune favors the bright and virtuous,
bestowed upon our Zhou state.
Lord Liu and Lady Wen—
fortune flows to their descendants.

**Jie**
The needle’s tip pierces the hand,
a hundred illnesses vanish.
Pressing, kneading, applying moxa—
the dead revive.

**Zhong Fu**
The primordial tortoise, the elephant’s tusk,
great bribes become treasures.
Resolving doubts, weighing right and wrong—
decline gives way to resurgence.

**Xiao Guo**
The old house, the former hut,
dissipated, leaving no trace.
Better to build anew—
one may dwell there in joy.

**Ji Ji**
The old fox, full of guile,
behaves in uncanny ways.
A demon, a specter—
startling the Queen Mother,
yet in the end, no blame or regret.

**Wei Ji**
A beloved child, rich in talents,
rising at the frontier leaves it empty.
Avoiding harm like a spirit,
water cannot soak him.
*Sheng* the forty-sixth.

**Sheng Yu**
Yu carved Dragon Gate,
dredging the water’s source.
Channeling east to the blue sea,
the people found peace.

**Qian**
The white deer calls—
summoning young and old.
Delighting in lush grass,
rejoicing in our lord.

**Kun**
A hundred *li* southward,
dimness brightens again.
Leaving Yu for Qin,
he became Duke Mu’s minister.

**Zhun**
Should the king’s kin prosper?
Renown spreads, wealth grows.
The dragon’s son excels—
westward, he gains long life.

**Meng**
Painting a dragon’s head and neck,
the pattern remains unfinished.
Honeyed words, fair speech—
deceptive phrases bear no name.

**Xu**
The merchant’s son is unkind,
fostering resentment far and wide.
Drawing swords in strife,
blame falls on himself.

**Song**
Weak and old, worn to the extreme,
toothless, unable to eat.
Hemorrhoids and wasting sores—
he retreats to the shade’s chamber.

**Shi**
The mandarin duck born in Kuaiji
grows strong enough to fly.
Soaring over Gui Forest,
he becomes the flock’s leader.

**Bi**
Peace stands firm, unshaken,
bearing fortune, long life.
The noble one rests in tranquility.

**Xiao Xu**
Ox and thoroughbred share a trough—
the Guo clan perishes.
The state lies in ruins,
its lord flees in flight.

**Lü**
At high noon, bright virtue shines,
two lands flourish.
Sage and wise meet—
the lord receives their blessing,
his ministers gain lush honor.

**Tai**
The dwelling of Lord Liu,
the foundation of the Great King.
Here one may live long,
receiving titles of fortune.

**Pi**
The season withers, the year falls still,
the noble one ails.
The Song woman bears no guilt,
yet Zheng suffers the calamity.

**Tong Ren**
Crossing the river, escaping peril,
freed from maternal fear.
The Four Uncles serve as guards,
ensuring kindness endures.

**Da You**
Broken, incomplete,
crippled and maimed.
Lord Sun is imprisoned,
hobbling to the back gate.

**Qian**
Stretching his neck in distant gaze,
his eyes grow dim with strain.
Failing to see Auntie Shu,
Uncle Bo’s heart grieves.

**Yu**
Above, no flying birds,
below, no running beasts.
Turmoil lingers unresolved,
the people toil in vain.

**Sui**
Endless clouds, ceaseless rain,
muddy roads cling to travelers.
The people rest, markets stand empty.

**Gu**
The blind man’s eyes open,
the lame man rises to walk.
Gazing at sun and moon,
he welcomes his lord.

**Lin**
Grasping the Dipper, turning the pivot,
following Heaven brings no sorrow.

**With Joy Together Dwelling**
With joy together dwelling,
ten thousand generations celebrate.

**Guan**
Crops and harvests balanced,
double planting stands firm.
Cunning words betray loyalty,
wounding me like Shen Sheng.

**Shi He**
A city of metal, walls of jade,
above and below unite in strength.
Governance is just, the people rejoice—
bandits dare not plunder.

**Bi**
The sun’s mirror dims,
winter’s disaster brings great harm.
Stolen blossoms bear no fruit—
ten years of decline and ruin.

**Jie**
Widowed, orphaned, solitary,
fate’s blessings meager and bitter.
Entering the chamber without a wife,
Wuzi grieves, turning back once more.

**Fu**
Drinking wine to drunkenness and satiety,
leaping up in quarrels and brawls.
Elder brother wounded, younger brother felled—
the Ji family prepares for mourning.

**Wu Wang**
Jie summoned the lesser lord,
keeping the ruler from peril.
Two states unite in joy—
Yan and Qi find peace.

**Da Xu**
Neck bound, tail tied,
slandered and broken, nearly dead.
In this age without benevolence,
none know to whom to turn.

**Yi**
The crouching dragon poisons all,
yet knows not what it strikes.
North and south in dire straits—
the prince’s life hangs in peril.

**Da Guo**
The sickly, impoverished royal scion,
the northern pole loses its light.
Fate’s blessings meager and bitter—
two guardians stand at orphaned gates.

**Kan**
Gongsun rides a black steed,
journeying east to Qi.
Yanling bestows gifts,
leaving Ji with patterned robes.

**Li**
Wang Liang excels at driving,
Bo Le knows horses well.
King Wen hunts to the east,
capturing worthy and wise men.
Opening fortune to bless Zhou,
raising up the dawn to rise.

**Xian**
Sun and moon do not linger—
Chonger hastens to lodge.
Wandering Yan enters Qin,
and Jin’s state becomes hegemonic.

**Heng**
Borrowing the wings of literature,
following the wind to turn north.
Reaching the lands of Yu and Xia,
passing the legacy to Shun.
Years of great joy,
villages free of thieves.

**Kuang**
Southward running, northward fleeing,
stretching necks in search of food.
Opening mouths brings no gain—
burdening our descendants.

**Da Zhuang**
Markets open in celebration,
constructing affairs of profit.
Balancing goods and treasures,
the realm grows prosperous and rich.

**Jin**
Three dogs run together,
battling at the valley’s mouth.
The white one does not prevail—
dying beneath the ruins.

**Ming Yi**
The arrogant Hu dog,
creating evil and violence.
Achieving nothing,
it destroys itself instead.

**Jia Ren**
Bowing and kneeling, offering praise,
yet no relief from blame.

**The Grandee**
Obstinate vessels of the grandee,
bringing sorrow to my heart.

**Kui**
The celestial station descends to Lou,
the king’s grand hunt and tour commence.
Vast blessings bestowed, kindness spread—
the myriad states rejoice as one.
Descendants rise in honor,
long peace without peril.

**Jian**
Leading the fine jade upstairs,
roaming with fortune in tow.
Toiling to govern the realm,
secure and joyful, free of care.

**Xie**
A white crow holds the bait,
calling to its young.
Dropping its staff, spreading wings,
it comes to follow its mother.

**Sun**
Blind and deaf, sleeping alone,
none share their meal.
Aged and forsaken by men,
sickness festers in heart and belly.

**Yi**
Climbing trees, emerging from the deep,
gradually ascending to heaven.
Virtue radiant, utmost sagely—
the sun bears its brilliance,
favor and rank flourish anew.

**Fu**
Peng Li crossed the east,
banished to Shangyong.
Savage and unruly, without restraint,
forfeiting his honored merit.

**Ni**
Praising the yang, dancing upward,
the spirit bright, the qi upright.
Yu bowed to receive the blessing—
the lord employs my power,
dwelling in abundant emolument.

**Cui**
From head to foot,
divided into six parts.

**Household scattered, wandering south to beg for food.**

**Kun**
The people lose their way, disrupting my order and discipline.

**Kong**
Emptying the dry blossoms, the guest has nothing—first sorrow, then joy.

**Jing**
Carved and painted for adornment, a plain wall as Xi Shi—seeking service, surely attaining it.

**Ge**
Sun and moon dwell together, meeting darkness, unilluminated.
A long night wastes its use, severing its guiding threads.

**Ding**
Clothes and skirts inverted, summoned by the king.
Achieving success for Zhou in the east, enfeoffed as a great lord.

**Zhen**
Facing change, establishing authority, resolving calamity and peril.
Like ice melting away, the Six States find peace.

**Gen**
The Western Rong play *xun* and *zhai*, afflicting our land.
Upholding the yang’s rectitude, preserving the Qian’s virtue—
in the end, no distress or delusion.

**Jian**
Journeying south in pursuit of sheep, the son’s profit and joy are lost.
Yin’s corruption breeds illness, returning again to his state.

**Guimei**
Playing with benevolence and virtue, each day brings increasing fortune.
Ominous words do not arrive; evil omens vanish and cease.

**Feng**
Spring’s new marriage, approaching the yang, the sun grows warm.
Joy and bliss for ten thousand years, reaping great blessings.

**Lü**
Yin ascends, yang submits—ghosts wail in their chambers.
Food untouched, the nest rests on thorns.

**Xun**
Ministers exalted, lords debased, authority and prestige wane daily.
Encroachment dims their light; the Three Families expel the duke.

**Dui**
Perverse words breed treachery; the Rong woman brings misfortune.
Disordering our house and state, father and son turn against each other.

**Huan**
Welcoming fortune, opening the door, joy follows in my wake.
Kang Bo’s magnanimity governs the people with ritual.

**Jie**
The sun approaches the moon, radiant and meritorious.
Observing from the Spirit Terrace, the drum of virtue resounds.

**Zhongfu**
A hundred grasses and fine blossoms sprout forth.
Insects stir at the door—yang’s brightness prevails.

**Xiaoguo**
Heaven’s protection and aid: fortune arrives, misfortune departs.
What sorrow remains for the lord?

**Jiji**
The destitute man loses his home, clinging to his old hut.
First anxiety, then inner dread—throughout the day, vigilant,
without regret or fear.

**Weiji**
Buying jade, obtaining stone, losing what was desired.
Carrying the basket, striking the chime—muffled, soundless.

---

**Kun (Hexagram 47)**

**Kun**
A mat of many thorns—no place for rest.
A burden to oneself, every move brings regret;
words and deeds alike transgress.

**Qian**
Crows and magpies eat grain, gaping to receive their feed.
Enveloped in kindness and virtue, they grow large and achieve.
Gentle, yielding, favorable, and upright—lord and minister in harmony.

**Kun**
Six ducks retreat in flight, an omen of defeat for Xiang.
Deploying troops, joining battle, the left thigh is wounded.
Thus he perishes, his hegemonic ambition unfulfilled.

**Tun**
Crawling forth in flight, terrified and trembling.
A white tiger bears young, its meager catch trailing behind—
dwelling within, no blame.

**Meng**
A shelter dimmed, obstructing rites and virtue.
The woman’s corruption disorders the state; tyranny harms benevolence.

**Xu**
The great rat with four feet cannot climb the roof.
Yan’s virtuous power remains without rank or emolument.

**Song**
Escorting the youngest daughter to the debauched path,
the Qi lord lingers day and night, tarrying long.

**Shi**
The deer follows the herdsman, sated, returning to its home.
Resting at the next lodge, delighting in freedom.

**Bi**
Gazing toward Shang and the Grand Steward, the Grand Tutor, the Duke of Zhou.
Serving as a screen and aid, fortune and emolument arrive together.

**Xiaoxu**
Expanding the great lineage, the king’s near dwelling.
Raised by the prince, meritorious virtue awaits its time.

**Lü**
Eightfold assembly in the great capital, abundant and rich.
Pacifying the people, benefiting the state—one may dwell long.

**Tai**
Dark clouds from all directions, the sun at the center.
Though others wander in mist, I alone remain bright.

**Pi**
Thinness brings calamity and cruelty; a great wind blows it away.
Seeking to ascend, unable—returning again to its abode.

**Tongren**
Gleaming yet obscure, no faithful guest.
Words multiply, reversing black and white.

**Dayou**
Three women conspire, roaming the lofty state.
Abandoning their chambers, wandering by night, laughing with the elder.
Disaster rebounds upon them; no place to appeal their grievance.

**Qian**
Treading corpses, lingering ghosts—the great axe’s gaze.
Wenchang examines transgressions; Duke Jian dies in chaos.

**Yu**
Long legs and great feet, profit lies in the road.
Granaries filled, teeth sparse—skilled in trade.
Wealthy with coin, affairs yield ten thousandfold.

**Sui**
Baskets, jars, tripods, and cauldrons—
the river spans a hundred *li*.
The Yi’s vessels and stands give rise to great fortune.

**Gu**
Ascending heights, gazing afar, seeking signs.
Driving to the northern town, joy comes to aid.

**Lin**
Employing that fine guest, governance is level and just.
No locusts arise; the people dwell in peace.

**Guan**
The peach blossoms in youthful splendor, marriage brings joy to the house.
The nobleman delights in harmony, long profit in stillness.

**Shike**
Journeying east, losing one’s company, not knowing where to turn.
Returning west, no companion—none to share laughter.

**Bi**
Playthings confound the eyes, clever sounds deceive the ears.
Treachery overthrows the upright; the lord suffers its harm.

**Bo**
Radiant virtue, vast and fine, enduring ten thousand years without decline.
Riding the dragon, touring the realm, the king finds his peace.

**Fu**
Same root, different leaves—peace in benevolence, esteem in virtue.
The eastern neighbor admires righteousness, reviving the ancient state.

**Wuwang**
Wearing the mountain’s towering peaks, the sun rises high without decline.
The lord’s abundant virtue is rewarded with a fine state.

**Daxu**
Building chambers in harmony, a thousand *li* without peril.
The Duke of Zhou for ten thousand years protects us three—
longevity stretches far.

**Yi**
Raising parrots to hatch chicks, breeding horses to bear foals.
Bright halls and grand academies—where the noble dwell.

**Daguo**
Thunder pursues in chase, never resting.
Battling on the plains, overthrown by the Yi.

**Kan**
Winding along the river, reaching the northern sea’s edge.
Traversing distant wilds, yet unharmed in the world.

**Li**
The swan’s cry, its gaze far-reaching, soars in divine transformation.
What was dark now shines—thus fortune’s work is fulfilled.

**Cheng**
Paired eyes, four wings—securing our state.
Above and below free from peril, a blessing for our house.

**Heng**
Shi Gu and Yin Ji conspire against Huanzi.
Leading troops, they provoke battle—defeated by the Jing.
Disobeying the marshal, they march to challenge—crushed by Chu.

**Zhu**
Three heads, six feet, scheming to plunder the state of Shu.
With Yanzi in the court, disaster is averted before it forms.

**Da**
Green mountains raise their trees, but midway they plunge into the valley.
The child and the lost labor—one morning’s yellow bird.

**Jin**
In the south, fine fish abound; harness the yellow steeds to net their fins.
Fat carp teem—profit comes without care.

**Mingyi**
Dark clouds gather deep, shrouding the great ministers.
Ears blocked, eyes shut—the men of Yin suffer harm.

**Jiaren**
Lifting robes, hastening on wings, gazing toward the southern land.
Necks stretched, then withdrawn—nothing gained.

**Kui**
Frogs in the marsh, now full, now empty.
Three nights, two dawns—their forms vanish without trace.

**Jian**
A youth shoots or drives, uncertain of his aim.
Consulting tortoise and milfoil—who can say what to avoid?
The land is secure, its people content; it is best to stay and dwell.
No bandits arise, no folk stir in distress.

**Xie**
Yin’s excess brings cold sickness; water floods the house.
Boats and oars multiply—millet and grain are harmed.
The people hunger for food, none spared from illness and hardship.

**Sun**
Friends part, companions sever; cunning words sow slander.
White is blackened, jade defiled—Yan Shu weeps in grief.

**Yi**
A maiden without matchmaker should not stir from her place.
Secure in her chamber, what has she to fear from her governess?

**Fu**
Forging misfortune, crafting calamity—the northern pavilion mires in poverty.
Bound to fortune’s thread, yet the left root is wounded.
*(Or: The tree is felled.)*

**Gou**
Facing east and south, the door—wind and rain keep away.
Cherishing the good, father and son preserve one another.

**Cui**
Wild hair, beastly heart—hard to be neighbors.
Coming like a whirlwind, departing like a snapped string—devoured by wolves.

**Sheng**
Heaven covers, earth bears; sun and moon turn in their course.
Yin and yang harmoniously arise—all within the four bounds prospers.

**Jing**
Jie’s chaos and tyranny scatter the people.
Forsaking home, abandoning hearth, the lord flees alone.

**Ge**
At the hour of *shen* and *you*, yin’s hidden sprouts emerge.
Reeds and rushes bear the flock—mud stains, nothing stays pure.

**Ding**
Ankles twisted, feet wounded; the left toe festers.
Missing the journey’s time, profit flees and does not return.

**Zhen**
Four legs all flee, the weak nag lags behind.
Together they fight, yet none prevail—defeated in the eastern wilds.

**Gen**
A broken cart on the road, a homely girl without a matchmaker.
No fit partner—she dwells alone in hardship.

**Jian**
Clapping flanks, laughing wildly, heedless of peril.
Opening the great road, he is summoned by the king.

**Guimei**
The elder lord travels east, meeting fortune along the way.
Having met the hour, who does not know him?

**Feng**
Traveling east to the thief’s house, the Lord of Zheng loses his words.
The state lacks steadfast goodness—the lord suffers its harm.

**Lü**
Bent forward, arched back, the body tense and strained.
Bound with black ropes, trapped in the clear chamber.

**Xun**
Beating wings in great joy, journeying to wed and feast.
Blessed are those Jiangs—delighting our royal forebear.

**Dui**
The fox howls toward the city; three dawns it wails—
the lord of the town is greatly alarmed.

**Huan**
Virtue bright and keen, Chong Hua is promoted.
Fang Xun is employed—his wisdom receives blessing.

**Jie**
Autumn’s end, winter’s flight—repeatedly struck by harsh frost.
Armor and weapons fill the court; ten thousand things cease to grow.
Pheasants and dogs cry at night—the people are greatly disturbed.
*(Or: Doubt arises, filling the space.)*

**Zhongfu**
Silk threads and woven cloth—what people wear.
The maiden’s hands card and spin, weaving and sewing.
The southern land abounds—take from it and it yields.

**Xiaoguo**
The phoenix has ten chicks, sharing their mother’s nest.
In fear, they guard one another.
The market’s rich quarter teems with wealth and grain.

**Jiji**
The male cock does not crow at dawn; the hen crows in its stead.
Will and heart diverge—three armies grieve.

**Weiji**
Brilliant light leaves the city; the Chenbao pheasant cries.
Yang brightness loses the Way, unable to hold fast—
dissolving into misfortune.

**Well (Forty-Eighth)**
Stumbling, not yet risen—losing profit in the later market,
failing to obtain the beloved child.

**Qian**
Left aide and right minister—gold and jade fill the hall.
Ever full, never lost, wealth like a granary’s store.

**Kun**
The Rain Master weds his bride, the Yellow Cliff’s youngest daughter.
The rites complete, the marriage sealed, they call to each other as they ascend south.
Fat rains nourish the earth below—great joy for the year’s harvest.

**Zhun**
Moth-worms turn traitor, harming my fine grain.
The center lies empty, the household has nothing to eat.

**Meng**
Lame tracks make walking hard; the road does not reach the inn.
Sleeping exposed in marsh and pond, losing one’s proud boast.

**Xu**
The great officer splits the father’s land, treading every place without bounds.
For my earth-divining, none compares to Han’s bliss.
Here one may dwell and abide—enduring peace and abundance.

**Song**
Young orphan without father, grown and bereft of a loving mother.
Weary and toiling alone, none to pair with.

**Shi**
A tilted cap, a drunken guest, a long tongue stirring trouble.
Hair unbound, wandering at night, lost and confused, one another misled—
home and dwelling lost.

**Bi**
The horse bolts, the carriage breaks; the king falls into the deep ford.
Body severed, soul departed, parted from house and hall.
In peril’s truth, no safety.

**Xiaoxu**
Bound on the road, reporting duties, punishing the unyielding.

**Qin**
Invading Qi, striking Chen, the street walls made servants—
the hound returns in triumph.
The hound is fit to be great.

**Lǚ**
A hundred feet move as one, mutual aid makes strength.
Three sages assist the cause, the royal house shines in favor.

**Tai**
Roots not firm, blossoms and leaves fall away—
once more a lone widow.

**Pi**
Tending sheep in the rice fields, hearing the tiger’s roar.
Fearful and vigilant, yet in the end no disaster.

**Tongren**
Treading rank, seizing power, no rift or ruin.
Plotted against by bondsmen, ranked with the common folk.

**Dayou**
The great chariot thick with dust, petty men harm the worthy.
Minister Huangfu, the lord loses his house.

**Qian**
Steadfast as Mount Tai, blessings and fortune arrive in abundance.
Though wolves and tigers prowl, they cannot endanger the body.

**Yu**
Kin of one breath, gates apart, each goes west or east.
Southward meets misfortune, northward harms its grandson.

**Sui**
The molting serpent shows ill omens, calamity arises in my village.
Travelers tremble in fear, village guests flee and hide.

**Gu**
Raising tigers, keeping wolves, they turn and wound their keeper.
Seeking no trouble, yet inviting disaster—self-inflicted woe.

**Lin**
Wind fans the flames, fortunate to cling to the steed’s tail.
Easy the labor, reaping fortune through another’s power.

**Guan**
The Five Peaks, the Four Rivers, their moisture a virtue.
Acting without straying from principle, the people rely on grace and favor.

**Shike**
Yanling’s keen wit, listening to music with the Grand Scribe.
The phoenix sings to the great state—Jiang receives blessing.

**Bi**
The divine bird of five hues, the phoenix as sovereign.
Alighting in the royal realm, the lord finds his place.

**Bo**
The matchmaker lacks clarity, though the tryst is set, it fails.
Qi’s eldest daughter, she disorders my order.

**Fu**
Bright moon turns day, the great one loses his home.
The night sky swarms with stars, none knows where to stand.

**Wuwang**
Shaokang rises, slays Jiao, restores his ancestors.
The faint is extinguished, the light returns—palace rites honor Great Yu.

**Daxu**
A thousand gates, ten thousand doors, the abode of great fortune.
The yellow canopy, the left banner—Dragon Virtue alone holds the right.

**Yi**
Qian makes the sagely son, Kun the wise daughter.
Their union brings fulfillment, long dwelling in joy.

**Daguo**
Yi draws the crow’s bow, the shell-arrow startles the wolf.
Bells and drums sound through the night, the general’s heart swells.
Zhao’s warriors bold, dying in battle at Rongyang.

**Xie**
The cauldron sears fish, the bronze vessel watches for the night rat.
Unable to bear the savor, the trap springs—misfortune strikes,
misfortune at the neck.

**Sun**
The pheasant soars high, heedless, grasping where it lands.
Rot and decay become its bane, harming itself.
Or: usurping rank for glory, inner filth beneath outward purity.
Now favored, now slighted—daily calamity grows.

**Xian**
The leaden blade attacks jade, hard and unyielding.
Exhausting sinew and strength, calluses and blisters bring affliction.

**Heng**
Square-beaked, eloquent, sagely wisdom and benevolence.
Unraveling the tangled, lifting the fallen—through the land, peace and prosperity.

**Dun**
Hesitating north and south, straying into a land of mourning.
Du Ji gathers troops, wounds my heart and core.

**Dazhuang**
Gongsun’s governance, kind yet unburdensome.
Qiaozi’s rise in the state—throughout life, no peril.

**Jin**
The bow drawn full, the road cut off, impassable.
Petty thieves and bandits—nobles blocked and choked.

**Mingyi**
The halberd-hidden chamber, the great boar receives fortune.
Abundant fat, rich marrow—descendants flourish.

**Ge**
Eight children of one household share the nest,
hearts laboring in longing, yet the pheasant suffers no sorrow.

**Kui**
Following principle, raising the hand, seeking the proper gift.
Six bodies in harmony—no misfortune or blame.

**Gongzi**
Prince and scion, sling in hand, pellet poised.
Each shot brings gain, the household abounds.

**Jing**
The islet brings regret, the molting serpent becomes a portent.
Not swiftly fleeing the village, the house suffers its woe.

**Sun**
Zheng’s go-between speaks loudly, the state falls into chaos and ruin.
Had Hongming foreseen it early, he would have stopped the music.

**Yi**
Breaching the chamber, piercing the wall—
unjustly provoking strife.
Tearing clothes to cross the river, though toiling, no success.

**Tai**
Eggs hatch, rabbits nurse—growing, they achieve.
The noble one for ten thousand years, every move brings profitable gain.

**Guai**
Five hearts divided, each draws its own right and wrong.

No one takes the lead, roads are blocked and congested.

**Cui**
A hundred pillars bear the beam, enduring a thousand years without decay.
Great vows bring fortune, civil and martial flourish.

**Sheng**
The city of Luoyi was built, founded by the Duke of Zhou.
Thirty generations linked, spanning seven hundred years.
Blessings abound in fullness, firm and unyielding.

**Kun**
With my uncle on a journey, we dine at Shuchang.
The joyous elder delights, sharing with me fragrant orchid.

**Ge**
Losing ears, deaf and blind, unaware of sound or taste.
Entrusted with the cauldron and platter, only then does chaos stir.

**Ding**
Opening the gate of Zi’zou, cranes sing and caps are brushed.
Literary works advance, the *Shun* dance harmonizes with bells.
Three sages aid governance, the state knows no disaster.

**Zhen**
Wandering souls of six children, born of a hundred trees.
Three sons follow their father, three daughters their mother.
At six they are complete, each finds their place.

**Gen**
Two mountains sprout, the lord of Pu diminishes his favor.
The royal daughter and eldest wife bear many sons and grandchildren.

**Jian**
In the wilds of Huangling, the worthy lord resides.
Rong Yan serves as minister, the state knows no disaster.

**Guimei**
Breaching roads and clearing dwellings, building the lord’s abode.
Opening the gate of fortune, joy dwells in my neighbor.

**Feng**
The winds of Shang arise, the world grows dark and dim.
Drought and demons rage, seven armies mobilize.

**Lü**
From Wei returning to Lu, the time does not favor me.
Ice and fire dwell apart, the Way of humanity is blocked.

**Xun**
Spring’s yang revives the grass, summer lengthens the branches.
All things flourish and multiply, filling and increasing in abundance.

**Dui**
Six serpents flee, rushing into the lush grass.
Startled by the long-dwelling one, they fear the snapping jaws.

**Huan**
The bright moon illuminates the night, turning darkness to day.
The state has wise and virtuous men, the lord is honored as before.

**Jie**
Fleeing eastward, one turns back into the tiger’s maw.
Grasped by claws and fangs, bones turn to dust.

**Zhongfu**
Collapsing and stumbling, the weak run and fall.
Meng Zhi lacks goodness, losing his favored light.

**Xiaoguo**
After ten years, all appear—yellow-headed ones lead.
At the year’s end, the people are at peace, the state rejoices without fault.

**Jiji**
Gazing into the wind, they enter the gate, arriving at my neighbor’s.
Spreading my nurture evenly.

**Weiji**
Ascending high, then turning back, the distant view is lost.
The tiger’s jaws do not open, harm and bandits vanish.

---

**Ge (Hexagram 49)**
A horse with long legs, fit for good trade.
All receive blessings, gaining threefold in gold.

**Qian**
Lofty plateaus and towering peaks, land vast with scarce springs.
Grasses, trees, and forest groves rejoice in their abundance.

**Kun**
One gate, two locks, knotted cords bring no ease.
Steep paths diverge, by dusk one does not arrive.

**Zhun**
Worries dissolve, joy arrives in celebration.
Sitting and standing by the gate, delight becomes a neighbor.

**Meng**
Distant kin on separate paths, hearts do not long for one another.
Cow and bull, widow and widower—none have a household.

**Xu**
King Tai as father, King Ji filial and kind.
Wen and Wu sagely and bright, benevolent governance arises.
Extending prosperity to four lands, bearing fortune in abundance.

**Song**
By the river seeking carp, the bait is lost in vain.
Holding breath and stilling gasps, no carp is caught.

**Shi**
Seeking profit and fortune, none surpass the southern state.
Where virtue dwells, gold and jade are treasured.

**Bi**
White tiger and red wrath, gazing upon the royal court.
Palace gates are armored, great and small march to war.
The world is troubled and vexed, even the young cannot be shielded.

**Xiaoxu**
Ziche’s tiger is caged, good men are endangered.
The yellow bird mourns in song, the state lacks support.

**Lü**
Both eyes lose sight, entering dusk without light.
Feet lame and steps faltering, one cannot walk, stumbling by the hillside.

**Tai**
Nets spread on four sides, birds have nowhere to soar.
Expeditions exhaust their strength, hunger and cold leave none fed.

**Pi**
Boyi and Shuqi, paragons of integrity and purity.
With virtue they ward off calamity, no sorrow or disaster remains.

**Guimei’s Lin, Qian’s Tai, Bi’s Bo.**

**Tongren**
The poor long for fortune, sending the elder to trade.
Opening the pen to choose sheep, great fortune is attained.

**Guan’s Yu, Kan’s Pi.**

**Dayou**
The poplars of Nanshan, their leaves lush and full.
The noble and joyous lord brings honor to the state.

**Qian**
Eastern walls hold lingering light, yet it dims and fades.
The mistress is jealous and overbearing, disrupting my affairs.

**Yu**
Wandering by night, the path is heavy with dew.
Drenched and weakened, steps grow ever heavier.

**Sui**
Eyes bright and feet swift, joy arrives in an instant.
The whole household is favored.

**Gu**
Hawks and falcons hunger, pheasants and hares are desperate.
Necks stretched to show their tails, they fall prey to me.

**Lin**
The nose shifts to the neck, withered leaves harm life.
Below withers, above flourishes—household disturbed, not at peace.
The golden fortress is lost.

**Guan**
Not flying far, you harm yourself within.
Nurtured but not enriched, no disaster befalls in the end.
The lord rests in goodness.

**Shike**
Foundations overturned, tongues double in malice.
Hair unbound through the long night, confusion and error abound.
Preserving nothing, dwelling brings fortune.

**Bi**
Zi and Wu clash, affairs and order collapse.
The people cannot act.

**Bo**
Wild elk fear men, fleeing together into mountain valleys.
Life is short, not long—seized by the tiger,
dead between its jaws and belly.

**Fu**
Autumn and winter, nests are probed,
but magpies and cranes are not found.
Biting a finger and heading north,
ashamed before my young concubine.
*See* **Zhun**.

**Wu Wang**
Two birds seen flying together, wishing to return to the rice pond.
Passing through Qu Marsh, struck by an arrow,
wounding my flank.

**Zhun** and **Lǚ** share the same *Xian*.

**Da Xu**
Heaven’s gates open wide, prison doors stand vast.
Bonds loosen, fetters fall—
the captive is freed.
*See* **Tai** of **Xiao Xu**, **Jian** of **Qian**.

**Yi**
Father Ni, Confucius,
skilled at angling carp.
With one cast of the net, ten thousand heads are caught,
enriching my household.
*See* **Ming Yi** of **Jian**.

**Da Guo**
Peng Sheng stirs as a demon, the fierce dragon brings calamity.
They steal Yao’s robes, gather weapons in haste.
The green bird lights the night—
after two dawns, all is lost.

**Kan**
Flowery words and windy speech,
deceiving one another in chaos.
Yet no misfortune comes—
peace remains as before.
*See* **Yi** of **Xian**.

**Li**
Neck stretched to see the feet, body trapped in shame and disgrace.
Wishing to hide from foes,
destroyed by harm.

**Xian**
No feet, heels severed—
dwelling is not secure.
Vicious and cruel, they ravage.
Lord and minister align,
or as one version has it: *Lord and minister find peace,
harmonizing with Heaven.*
Preserving the low, establishing the high,
great mutual concealment.

**Heng**
Three walk together, seeking great omens in the north.
The eldest suffers a foot ailment,
the youngest carries the root.
The virtue of Liuxia—
not losing the black or yellow.

**Zhu**
Retreating flight reveals omens,
wounded, defeated, shattered, and fallen.
Guarding the small, losing the great,
merit and fame unfulfilled.

**Da Zhuang**
Relying on the heart’s fear and anger,
easily swayed and restless.
Not settled in place,
treasures scatter and dissolve—
no profit remains.

**Jin**
Dragging the tail, not advancing,
acting against principle, losing ministers.
Hui Shu flees.

**Ming Yi**
Wealth like the Duke of Zhou,
establishing a state east of Luo.
Father and son both enfeoffed.

**Jia Ren**
The lord has eight men,
trustworthy, sincere, earnest, and keen.
Recommended by Yao.

**Kui**
Long overcast with ceaseless rain,
muddy paths and overflowing streams.
Merchants cease their trade,
the market empty and bare.

**Jian**
Footless, heels severed,
dwelling unsettled, restless.
Calamity and cruelty bring ruin.
*Centrality and Excess.*

**Xie**
The horse stumbles, the cart overturns,
the wife’s malice destroys the household.
Flies sully the white,
Gongzi departs in solitude.

**Sun**
The boastful words of the hunchbacked—
none match my walls.
Fear and joy, steadfast and firm,
can bring enduring peace.
*Qian’s Kun, Da You’s Zhun, Fu’s Yi.*

**Yi**
Duke Yi, shallow and foolish,
rejects profound counsel.
Without support, he loses his state,
destroyed by the Di.

**Yang**
Qilin and Lü’er,
brilliant and swift, Zao Fu’s steeds.
Feng Bo’s tribute,
Xiang continues the legacy.
Assisting Wen, becoming a count,
serving as Jin’s chief minister.
*Jie’s Tai.*

**Gou**
Driving ten li,
seeking fresh bream and carp.
Not his proper dwelling,
he brings ruin upon himself.

**Cui**
Seeking fine game in a fine land,
the ill terrain halts the journey.
The path turns back midway,
returning to the forest.

**Sheng**
Sending the turtledove to bear the load,
drunk by the roadside.
Unknowing of whose domain,
my clothes and bag are stolen.

**Kun**
Ascending Kunlun,
entering the Gate of Heaven.
Passing the Mound of Dregs,
lodging at Jade Spring.
Opening the *Hui Guan*,
beholding the benevolent lord.
*Bi’s Gou, Zhen’s Ge.*

**Jing Shui**
The bed of Heaven,
afflicted, weary, unable to rise.
Jibo walks by night,
encountering goodness.

**Ding**
The daughter of the Wusun clan,
deep-set eyes, dark and plain.
Desires unaligned,
past her time, no match.

**Zhen**
Ziyin holds the qilin,
the *Spring and Autumn* records its omen.
The primal sage nears his end,
Confucius grieves in his heart.
*Yu’s Da You.*

**Gen**
Scorching fire, spring’s grandson,
fishing and weaving atop the mountain.
Fish cannot be caught,
the fire refuses to burn.
*Ding’s Lü.*

**Jian**
Heavenly steeds on five paths,
flames linger long.
Coming and going, ascending and descending,
composing texts, restraining the self.
Clothing of hemp and silk,
laughing and singing together—
how can misfortune befall?
*Gui Mei*
The partridge breaks the axe,
striking dangerously close.
By Dan’s loyal virtue,
misfortune turns to fortune,
peril restored to stability.
*Pi’s Gu.*

**Feng**
The male pheasant takes flight, the pass opens,
great troubles dissolve,
no personal disaster.
*Xu’s Dui, Tong Ren’s Yang.*

**Lü**
Stone Gate opens at dawn,
carrying a basket, eating in poverty.
Withdrawing from the world, living in seclusion,
never meeting the times.

**Xun**
Rabbits wed in the eastern corridor,
hounds all give chase.
The encirclement incomplete,
nothing can be caught.

**Dui**
Three sheep run in a flock,
pheasants and hares startle.
Not what they fear,
yet they bring labor upon themselves.

**Huan**
Wings and feathers wounded,
no strength remains.
Duke of Song, meager in virtue,
defeated at the Hong River.

**Jie**
Young Ji and Jiang,
three dine together.
Discussing benevolence, debating fortune,
to stabilize the royal house.

**Zhong Fu**
Where sincerity resides,
spirits and men lend aid.
Virtue’s teaching dispels harm,
spanning generations, enduring long.
Three sages in succession,
receiving abundant blessings.

**Xiao Guo**
Qi and Zhou at the sea’s edge,
solitude brings joy, no sorrow.
A place to evade disaster,
preserving life and wealth.

**Ji Ji**
Alone and solitary,
no one to rely upon,
the heart labors, the will suffers.

**Wei Ji**
Gazing from the tower,
the mind ever seeks escape.
Marrying Xin on a *chou* day—ill-omened,
the wife unsettles her husband.
*Ding’s Fifty*

**Ding**
A lord of accumulated virtue,
benevolent governance, gentle and warm.
Yi and Lü as his arms,
the state prosperous, the people at peace.

**Qian**
A basket of *juan’er*—
sorrow cannot harm.
The heart thinks of the ancients,
mourning the lost mother.

**Kun**
Que and Shu borrow and trade,
their conduct brings much regret,
no profit to be gained.

**Zhun**
Lame feet, mad and limping,
strange and broken, unable to walk.
Abandoning and harming the common folk,
their names erased from the records.
*Alternatively: Fleeing, forsaking the common folk, their names unrecorded.*

**Meng**
King Wen’s four breasts,
benevolent and deeply kind.
Raising ten sons,
none die young.

**Xu**
Accommodating the people, nurturing the multitude,
never parting from their lord.

**Song**
Three fledglings chase one another,
a fly falls into the pot.
Boiled in bubbling water,
they join their mother in death.

**Shi**
The gaze turns outward,
the tripod’s decree arrives.
Wiping the goblet, cleansing the vessels,
cooking food in anticipation—
no cause for the youngest’s sorrow.

**Bi**
Dwelling on high ground, scarce springs,
mountains without clouds.
A thousand *li* journey,
mud soils your wheels—
a trouble for me as well.

**Xiao Xu**
Tying the household’s ox,
blood splatters, stench fills the air.
The spirits turn away, looking west,
the mandate of declining Zhou ends.
The altar of Bo burns,
the people of Song executed.
*Kui’s Ming Yi.*

**Lü**
The eldest son enters prison,
the wife spins, the mother weeps.
Frost descends, ten days pass,
at dusk, the law is enforced.

**Tai**
The pine on Warm Mountain,
evergreen, never falling.
The phoenix shelters beneath,
finding joy and delight.

**Pi**
Beneath the great roof,
many lords gather in the morning.
Virtue spreads, nurturing all,
Song receives its blessings.

**Tong Ren**
Nets spread, eyes arrayed,
the encirclement nearly complete.
The hunt yields nothing,
fish and birds escape.

**Da You**
Lambskin robes, leopard garments,
elevating my halls.

**Junzi**
The noble one maintains goodwill,
to old age free from care.

**Qian**
A great head, bright eyes,
bearing blessings and joy.
Three sparrows fly in,
meeting with fortune’s favor.

**Yu**
Melting blades into plows,
releasing oxen and horses.
Arms laid down, weapons dispersed,
husband and wife keep each other safe.

**Jin** *(same as above)*

**Sui**
Auspicious days, chariots advance,
hunting yields a double catch.
King Xuan feasts with wine,
announcing his triumphant merit.

**Gu**
Merchants travel on the road,
possessions utterly spent.
Chasing cowries for profit,
lingering in the royal market.
The axle hub secure within,
what fault befalls the noble one?

**Lin**
Fire enters the well’s mouth,
yang’s radiance grows horns.
Passing through Heaven’s Gate,
glimpsing the Supreme Subtlety.
Ascending the Jade Grove,
the household changes its lord.

**Guan**
Autumn gathers, winter soars,
repeatedly struck by harsh frost.
Armies fill the court,
all things cease to grow.
The male pheasant crows at night,
the people thrown into great alarm.

**Shi He**
Bound to march west,
losing one’s lodging.
At Qianhou’s wild well,
Zhaojun mourns her dwelling.

**Ben**
Swollen veins, ailing belly,
fallen into the privy, defiled and shamed.
Life short, time exhausted,
the orphaned child weeps for a single dawn.

**Bo**
Cutting skin, near disaster,
the tiger severs my whiskers.
Petty men act with violence,
what calamity befalls the noble one?

**Fu**
A woman’s chamber brews poison,
becoming my heart’s affliction.
Harmony cannot cure it,
the people of Jin rush to report.

**Wu Wang**
Troops march on Da Yuan,
northward through Jade Gate Pass.
Clashing with the Hu raiders,
west of Pingcheng’s road.
Seven days without grain,
the body nearly perishes.

**Da Xu**
Ten sons, nine wives,
none fit to dwell with.
A steadfast heart unexpressed,
to this day the name stands alone.

**Yi**
The carriage rolls through rice and wheat,
arriving at home and kingdom.
The joyous land free from disaster,
what worry has the noble one?

**Da Guo**
Building a chamber at the mountain’s root,
meant for security and peace.
One night it collapses from the peak,
shattering my treasured meal.

**Kan**
Six men travel together,
each losing their sack.
The yellow crane drops its pearl,
nothing left to illuminate.

**Li**
Bo Sai and Shu Mang,
none to guard the luggage.
I lose my robes and furs,
this is the land of yin.

**Xian**
Excessive favor breeds resentment,
ruining governance and toppling the house.
Overturning my ancestral state,
Qin extinguishes the Zhou court.

**Heng**
Deceptive words, twisted speech,
enmity and disaster converge.
Ice enters the charcoal chamber,
melting ceaselessly away.

**Guang**
Peng Sheng becomes a demon,
the violent dragon brings calamity.
Stealing Yao’s robes,
marauders gather with weapons in hand.
The luminous bird lights the night,
three days and Yifang falls.

**Da Zhuang**
Morning and evening,
sun and moon pass like four horses through a gap.
Years short, time fleeting,
the moment cannot be regained.

**Jin**
Ears deaf, the Dao lost,
endeavors fail, desires unmet.

**Ming Yi**
Shen Gong fears Chu,
perilous and insecure.
Chong’er flees into exile,
his soul shattered in grief.

**Jia Ren**
Southward ascending Mount Tai,
stranded in the barren mulberry.
Left with sand, right with stone,
oxen and horses have no fodder.

**Kui**
The eastern sea’s distant shores,
where fortune and blessings reside.
Gentle and refined, proper in ritual,
what fault lies with the Nine Yi?

**Jian**
Yang spring gives birth and growth,
all things flourish and thrive.
Late autumn spreads its leaves,
the noble one emulates its virtue.

**Xie**
Lowering the head, stealing glances,
fearing to be seen.
Actions bring misfortune,
wine sours, fish spoils,
none dare to indulge.

**Sun**
Left aid, right support,
gold and jade fill the hall.
Ever full, never lost,
wealth like a granary’s store.

**Shi** *(same as Gui Mei)*

**Yi**
Sitting in court, curtains drawn,
governing the people with virtue.
Yu Shu receives the mandate,
the Six Directions live in harmony.

**Guai**
Bound to march west,
losing one’s hounds and horses.
Seeking the swift black steed,
the carriage lost beneath the forest.

**Shen**
Honing virtue, sharpening talent,
truly destined for Cheng Zhou.
Receiving the great mandate,
enfeoffed as Marquis of Qi.

**Cui**
Westward meeting the Queen Mother,
she cherishes my nine sons.
Facing each other with joy,
the royal grandson with ten thousand households,
the family receives blessings.

**Sheng**
Sitting at ease on the jade couch,
listening to the *Shao* while raising cups.
Drinking to ten thousand years of fortune,
days of longevity without end.

**Kun**
Ascending heights to gaze at home,
labor’s tasks never cease.
Royal affairs without respite,
no leisure to wander free.

**Jing**
Beating drums, breaching the pass,
unable to aid one another.
Adorning caps with cultured virtue,
fortune prevails, calamity dissolves.

**Ge**
Pursuing the fleeing, chasing the routed,
calling back the youngest uncle.
Arriving and returning,
regaining his chamber.

**Zhen**
The old rogue’s great deceit,
bound to steal the pearl,
trapped in the jaws of the dragon,
barely escaping.

**Gen**
Yu summons the myriad spirits,
at Mount Kuaiji in the south.
Holding jade, the ten thousand states,
the world lives in peace and safety.

**Shen** *(same as Lin)*

**Jian**
Enduring sorrow, near despair,
as if life cannot be preserved.
The grace of millet and sorghum,
Ling Zhe survives,
securing life and preserving years.

**Meng** *(same as Sun)*

**Gui Mei**
Marquis Shu rises to power,
Ji Zi grows wealthy.
Illuminating the land of Chu,
the Man and Jing are pacified.

**Feng**
A white horse, swift and black,
unceasingly renewed.
Enriching our merchants,
profit heaped like a mound.

**Lü**
Fire burns at the spring’s source,
fishing and weaving on the mountain’s peak.
Fish cannot be caught,
the fire refuses to burn.

**Ge** *(same as Gen)*

**Xun**
Avoiding disaster east and west,
turning back into the gate of misfortune.
Chaff and husks insufficient,
worry stirs my heart.

**Dui**
Our king favored many,
the merchants trembled in fear.
Nurturing treacherous intent,
placing me in peril,
yet in the end, no disaster.

**Huan**
The tiger hungers to feed,
but seeing suspicion, it crouches low.
Yu dredges Dragon Gate,
avoiding blame and dispelling misfortune,
Yuan Chou finds peace.

**Jie**
Pacifying the people, they call to the pool,
jade grove and grand feast.
The spring flows like white honey,
one embrace fulfills the wish.

**Zhong Fu**
Transformed, mandarin ducks appear,
following in flocks.
Southward to the lush marsh,
feasting on fish and fine grain,
the noble one enjoys longevity.

**Xiao Guo**
The Marquis of Cai pays court to Chu,
lingering by the river isles.
Jade gleams through the months,
longing for his lord and sovereign.

**Ji Ji**
The glue-bound cart harnessed eastward,
meets the rain along the way.
Five chestnuts scatter and fall,
a lone peach sits withered,
worry brings personal calamity.

**Wei Ji**
Moth larvae turn traitor,
harming our crops and harvest.
All the grain, millet, and wheat ruined,
autumn yields nothing.
*(Same as* **Jie** *of* **Tong Ren** *and* **Qian** *of* **Yu**.)*
End of *Yi Lin*, Scroll Three.

*(This section consists of textual variants and editorial notes from collation sources, rather than continuous Classical Chinese text for translation. As such, it does not require a literary or interpretive translation. Below is the rendered version preserving its scholarly apparatus format:)*

1. 『示』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『尔』.
2. Originally 『上』—emended to 『山』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
3. Originally 『狷』—emended to 『谓』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
4. Originally 『同』—emended to 『国』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
5. Originally 『卓』—emended to 『卑』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
6. 『思』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『鬼』.
7. Originally omitted 『屯之噬嗑，比之豫』—supplied from *Baizi Quanshu*.
8. Originally 『充』—emended to 『克』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
9. Originally 『这』—emended to 『动』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
10. 『先』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『走』.
11. 『实』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『皇』.
12. Originally 『伐』—emended to 『墟』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
13. 『神』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『侯』.
14. 『花』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『华』.
15. 『卒』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『子』.
16. Originally 『巳』—emended to 『己』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
17. Originally 『文』—emended to 『久』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
18. Originally 『骥』—emended to 『骥』 following *Baizi Quanshu* (repeated for clarity).
19. 『王』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『主』.
20. 『凿』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『监』.
21. 『薄』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『昧』.
22. Originally 『捕土』—emended to 『补牢』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
23. Originally 『秩』—emended to 『疾』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
24. 『乱』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『就』.
25. 『花』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『华』.
26. 『蒙古』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『羊舌』.
27. Originally 『六』—emended to 『大』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
28. Originally 『在』—emended to 『左』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
29. Originally 『道』—emended to 『逆』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
30. Originally 『来』—emended to 『未』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
31. Originally 『日』—emended to 『口』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
32. Originally 『难』—emended to 『虽』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
33. Originally 『中』—emended to 『之』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
34. Originally 『之』—emended to 『中』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
35. Originally 『日』—emended to 『目』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
36. Originally 『山』—emended to 『止』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
37. Originally 『三』—emended to 『二』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
38. Originally 『西』—emended to 『田』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
39. Originally 『戍』—emended to 『戌』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
40. Originally 『过』—emended to 『遏』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
41. Originally 『淑』—emended to 『涉』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
42. 『实』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『皇』, but 『实』 is retained as correct.
43. Originally 『于』—emended to 『手』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
44. Originally 『巳』—emended to 『己』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
45. Originally 『上』—emended to 『圭』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
46. Originally 『巳』—emended to 『己』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
47. Originally 『堂』—emended to 『圭』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
48. 『畏』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『丧』.
49. 『室』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『宝』.
50. Originally 『自』—emended to 『脱』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
51. Originally 『绶』—emended to 『缸』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
52. 『束』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『叔』.
53. 『破』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『砍』.
54. 『工』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『五』.
55. 『义』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『人』.
56. 『年』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『允』.
57. 『妳』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『珍』.

#69 Originally 『际』—emended to 『疗』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.

#71 『实』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『皇』, but 『实』 is retained as correct.
#72 Originally 『八』—emended to 『入』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#73 『召』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『绍』.
#74 『究』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『冤』.
#75 Originally 『比』—emended to 『北』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#76 Originally 『骚』—emended to 『骊』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#77 Originally 『故』—emended to 『说』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#78 Originally 『且』—emended to 『旦』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#79 Originally 『八』—emended to 『入』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#80 『背』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『偕』.
#81 『传』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『得』.
#82 『圾』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『阪』.
#83 Originally 『火』—emended to 『犬』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#84 Originally 『坎』—emended to 『次』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#85 『狩巡』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『巡狩』.

#105 Originally 『中在』—emended to 『在中』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#106 『薄』—should read 『魅』.
#107 『国』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『园』.
#108 Originally 『困合』—emended to 『困仓』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#109 Originally 『活』—emended to 『阔』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#110 Originally 『吕』—emended to 『里』 following *Baizi Quanshu*. *He huo bai lü* may also read *ke huo bai kou*.
#111 『古』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『吾』.
#112 Originally 『于』—emended to 『子』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#113 Originally 『桃』—emended to 『挑』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#114 Originally 『速』—emended to 『邃』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.

#115 Originally 『熟』—emended to 『龟』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#116 Originally 『熟』—emended to 『孰』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#117 Originally 『保』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『保』.
#118 Originally 『狠』—emended to 『狼』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#119 『耦』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『偶』.
#120 『清』—*Baizi Quanshu* reads 『请』.
#121 Originally 『请』—emended to 『诸』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#122 Originally 『色』—emended to 『邑』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#123 Originally 『被』—emended to 『放』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#124 Originally 『准』—emended to 『年』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.

#127 『鸡具』—alternatively 『呜且』.
#128 Originally 『巳』—emended to 『亡』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.

#172 『尾』—should read 『美』.

#199 Originally 『垠』—emended to 『跟』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#200 Originally 『缺』—emended to 『央』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#201 『夫之大过』 should not be appended to the line statements of *Ge*’s *Sai*—its line statement (*"Long overcast with rain, roads awash in mud. Merchants halt, the market empty"*) is unrelated to *Ge*’s *Sai*. Note by the collator: 『央之大过』 should be appended to the line statements of *Ge*’s *Kui*.

#212 Originally 『取』—emended to 『比』 following *Baizi Quanshu*.
