*Yilin*, Scroll 4 (Part 2), Hexagram *Zhen* (The Arousing, Fifty-First)

**Hexagram *Zhen* (The Arousing, Fifty-First)**

**Zhen**   | A withered gourd does not decay; it serves to ferry a boat.
Crossing the Yu River and seas, one need not fear drowning.

**Qian**   | Sunken in mud, drowned in water, fire burns my shoes—
layers of woes weigh heavy.

**Kun**   | Born at dawn, dead by dusk, called the infant ghost—
one cannot mourn such a fate.
*(See *Xiaoxu* → *Sheng*, *Yang* → *Lin*.)*

**Tun**   | Dredging water and drilling deep, the stone is made pure white.
Clad in white with a vermilion lining, one roams the marshlands in play.
The lord’s desire is fulfilled, the heart’s will delights in joy.
*(See *Yu* → *Taiguo*.)*

**Meng**   | A flock of birds cries out in unison—something great and strange appears.
Nine bodies share no head; the soul flees in terror, the spirit departs.
One cannot dwell here.

**Xu**   | Severed roots, withered stumps, flesh does not regrow.
The illness lies in the heart; the body withers away.

**Song**   | The treasury’s wealth is vast; the king aids the poor.
Fishing in rivers and seas, the nets haul in great catches.
*(See *Sun* → *Kui*, *Kan* → *Taiguo*.)*

**Shi**   | A single stalk bears nine shoots, yet they are tangled and bound.
Resting at night, looking up and down, one cannot move east or west.
The appointed time is missed; at noon, punishment is meted out.

**Bi**   | The aged suckle their backs, teeth loose and trembling.
Near the earth, far from heaven, they descend into the Yellow Springs.

**Xiaoxu** | She-yu Shu Hu, wild at heart and quick to rage,
greedy for bribes without end, brings ruin upon himself.

**Lǚ**   | Eight sons scheme and deceive, each plotting against the other.
Guan Shu’s good governance is unseen; no wicked schemes come to pass.

**Tai**   | The fugitive is not far, yet heart and words contradict.
Niqiu turns back to his home, where the thatched hut blooms with red blossoms.

**Pi**   | Clams and oysters wear pots on their heads, unable to climb the mountain.
Stumbling and tripping, lame and bruised, their faces are battered.

**Tongren** | Morning dew does not last; favors are few.
The rich moisture is spent; blame lies in withering and decay.

**Dayou** | The merit of the River Lord unites the Nine Provinces.
Six hundred carriages bear offerings; his glory knows no end.

**Qian**   | Three men journey north, beholding great brightness.
On the road, they meet a fair maiden, who gives me a fine steed.

**Yu**   | The golden essence flares in anger, a sword at his side past noon.
He paces the high granary, lodges beneath the trees.
Two tigers face each other; bows and crossbows fill the fields.

**Sui**   | The Yangtze, the Yellow River, the Huai, and the seas—
the heavens’ hidden treasuries.
Where all profits gather, one may grow rich, dwell in peace, and know no sorrow.

**Gu**   | Unforeseen calamity arrives at the gate.
Sudden death strikes; illness wounds my heart.

**Lin**   | The dragon’s head and horns are drawn, but the pattern is incomplete.
Sweet words and fine speech persuade, yet the interpreter gains no fame.

**Guan**   | Broken and incomplete, the embryo’s egg does not hatch—
no omen of punishment appears.
*(See *Jin* → *Yi*.)*

**Shi Ke** | The path is not far, but after three *li*, one turns back.

Fear and malice fill the heart; at noon, one halts for rest.

**Bi**   | Four borders unsettled, war and arms bring disaster.
They plunder my wife and children; the household suffers hunger and cold.

**Bo**   | Joy arrives like clouds; the whole family is enveloped in happiness.
Talented noblemen gather; auspicious fortune fills the gate.
*(See *Kui* → *Feng*.)*

**Fu**   | Carrying gold to trade for dogs, profit flees and abandons me.
Hidden in the depths of the abyss, misfortune arises from concealment.
*(See *Sui* → *Ge*.)*

**Yuanwang**   | At midday, a market forms; each clutches what they possess.
Exchanging goods and wealth, they hold pearls in their palms and treasure in their bosoms, hearts filled with joy.

**Da Xu**   | Moving day by day, month by month, one traverses each lodging in turn.
Journeying far, no difficulty arises.

**Yi**   | Yang brightness loses its time; yin congeals into sorrow.
The lord weeps in mourning, bereft of his foremost marquis.

**Da Guo**   | As the year declines and the season wanes, the refined spirit wanders away.
Form and countenance wither; scattered, the children call to one another.

**Kan**   | Young, without merit; old, beset by misfortune.
Lame and limping, unsteady, one knows not where to stand.

**Li**   | Eyes wide with alarm, trembling in constant motion.
Binding oneself, one heads west, unable to find peace.

**Huan**   | The treasury scatters; no profit remains.

**Xian**   | Demanding cowries to ransom a raccoon, they heed not my words.
Seizing the tiger by the whiskers, one cannot pull it back.
*(See *Xu*, *Kui*, *Pi*, *Ge*, *Tong Ren Pi*, *Sui Shi*.)*

**Dan**   | An old wolf with a white furnace, long-tailed and great-bearded.
Stumbling forward and back, the people of Qi rejoice.

**Chi**   | Turning their backs, they despise one another; hearts and wills differ like fire and metal.
The lord is fierce, his ministers cowed; the tiger prowls while the hare cowers.

**Da Zhuang**   | Xia Terrace and Beautiful Li, where Tang and Wen met their distress.
The joyful brew of Ghost Marquis brings delight to the people of Qi.

**Jin**   | Teeth sprout from gums; the mantis opens the door.
The reclusive one finds advantage in constancy, drumming his wings to dance.

**Ming Yi**   | A烈女 without a husband, grieving in sorrowful longing.
The Qi maiden lacks goodness, filling my heart with sorrow.

**Jia Ren**   | Treading through peril and hardship, one escapes calamity.
Entering the gate of fortune and joy, I behold my great lord.
*(Or: the great sea.)*

**Kui**   | A broken arm, hands clasped—unable to offer wine.
The staff lies idle; the spirits are angered and displeased.

**Jian**   | Ants seal their nests; a great rain is about to gather.
Magpies cry repeatedly; the hen pheasant sighs in her chamber.
The male pheasant lies dead; the father arrives on the road.

**Xie**   | The customs of the Hu and Rong, accumulated by the Great Yin.
Bitter cold and freezing stillness—no gentleman remains.

**Sun**   | Collapsing and crumbling, gradually toppling into ruin.
One’s good name is extinguished; the body does not remain whole.

**Yi**   | Pestilential insects become thieves, harming my crops.
All the grain and wheat are devoured; in autumn, nothing is reaped.

**Yang**   | Three crows fly here, meeting me in my time.
Advancing together, the first to arrive gains great profit.

**Shen**   | The dragon-horse ascends the mountain, where no springs flow.
Lips and throat parched, thirst cannot be spoken.

**Cui**   | In spring, the young are born and nursed; all things flourish.
Where the nobleman gathers, no disaster or misfortune arrives.

**Sheng**   | The king’s grandson and Ji Zi, friends in mutual trust.
Bright, sincere, and steadfast, they are promoted and recommended.
*(See *Da You* → *Guo*.)*

**Kun**   | Six lights shine together; governance enters order.
The warring states of Qin and Chu bring suffering to the people.

**Jing**   | The concubine and the weaver stand by; flatterers lead astray.
Women’s favors run rampant; the right path is blocked.

**Ge**   | Ascending Kunlun, entering the gate of heaven.
Passing the wine dregs’ mound, lodging at Jade Spring.
Opening the gate of kindness, beholding the benevolent lord.
*(See *Bi* → *Kun*, *Ge* → *Kun*.)*

**Ding**   | Heavy and unable to fly, one cannot cross the pass, remaining within empty walls.

**Gen**   | Dark and yellow, the viper hisses; travelers grow weary.
Laborers are haggard; only at the appointed time do they return.
*(See *Qian* → *Ge*, *Shi* → *Lin*.)*

**Jian**   | Virtue like jade, emerging from the hidden valley.
Soaring to the high trees, drumming its wings, its radiance illuminates the land.
*(See *Tong Ren* → *Kan*.)*

**Gui Mei**   | Though fire blazes, it is behind me.
Though bandits are many, they are to my right.
Safe and secure, no danger threatens.

**Feng**   | The land of fur and stench, where rites and decorum are unadorned.
Mounted on horseback, bow drawn, they attack our capital.

**Lü**   | With hair unbound at eighty, one offers submission in twilight virtue.
The borderlands are not alarmed, bringing peace to the royal state.

**Xun**   | The heart finds what it loves; the mouth ever desires to smile.
The lord’s grandson with moth eyebrows, the parrot sings through the night.

**Dui**   | The horse turns west, bearing its load, seen in the fields of the village.
Reaping millet and rice together, joy and no fault arise.

**Huan**   | Flying high to look below, where greed and gluttony reside.
Rot and stench bring harm, afflicting the body.

**Jie**   | Bound and walking west, one loses their lodging.
At Qianhou’s wild well, the Bright Consort perishes.
*(See *Ding* → *Shi Ke*.)*

**Zhong Fu**   | The divine crow with five colors, the phoenix as king.
Gathering in the mountain valleys, they make the years fruitful.

**Xiao Guo**   | At dawn, the stone gate opens; the merchant carries his load, eating in poverty.
Withdrawing from the world to live in seclusion, one never meets the times.
*(See *Ge* → *Lü*.)*

**Ji Ji**   | The oyster and the clam quarrel; the impoverished ghost demands payment.
No ease or joy remains; nine knots form in a single day.

**Wei Ji**   | The white sun shines brightly; the thunder chariot hides.
Clouds and rain do not move, halting in their land.
*(See *Gen* → fifth line.)*

**Gen**   | The lord lives in solitude, weak and unsupported.
This is called hardship and suffering.

**Fu Xin** | The heart’s aid wells forth like a spring. Rolling and rolling, like a mountain.

**Qian** | Anxiety and alarm run deep, yet misfortune brings no disaster. Since then, all has been secure.

**Kun** | Piercing the gourd, embracing ice, the reed-pipe’s mother kindles fire. Exhausted and spent, hunger and thirst become calamity.

**Zhun** | The lame ox breaks its horn, unable to bear the load. Disasters cannot be avoided; the year yields no grain. The city of Meng will become a wasteland—dwelling there brings peril.

**Xu** | The tree’s roots are severed, its blossoms and leaves fallen. Suddenly, a crowd of flames arises; with the wind, all collapse.

**Song** | The supreme ruler’s greed exhausts the people’s strength. Those in power act perversely, and the Yi overthrow them.

**Shi** | On the northern mountain grows millet; let Shu live long and prosper. The eastern ridge abounds with grain—go forth and trade in the market. The soaring pheasant brings profit and joy wherever it alights.

**Bi** | High plateaus and towering peaks, where earth yields little water. Forests and groves of grass and trees—fine crops meet with disaster.

**Xiao Xu** | The celestial bodies enter Lou, and the king sets forth on his tour. Broadly bestowing virtue and favor, the land is at peace, free from care.

**Lü** | The carriage’s axle and canopy fray as the year draws late. Favor and renown are cast aside; the lord declines in his position.

**Tai** | The bit is loosed, the reins abandoned; chaos runs unchecked. Laws and norms shift without constancy—the lord loses his place.

**Pi** | Alone, I ascend the western wall; none share my laughter or words. The autumn wind carries much sorrow, grieving my heart.

**Tong Ren** | The sinews contract, the thighs cramp—I cannot leave the house. At dusk, the wandering horde arrives; surely, it will bring harm.

**Da You** | Truth and deceit are hard to discern, making me partial and biased. With petty men in office, what fault can even the wise avoid?

**Qian** | Millet and wine, pure and rich, are reverently offered to the mountain’s spirit. The gods relish the feast; sweet rains and auspicious omens follow. All things flourish in abundance; the time knows no disaster or fault. Alone, I receive blessings.

**Yu** | The prince and his noble sons take up the sling and grasp the pellets. Every shot brings gain; the household overflows with plenty.

**Sui** | Yin ascends, Yang recedes; Shun loses his home. The common people, red and starving, go hungry together.

**Gu** | Seven orifices in a dragon’s body, crafting the *Yi*’s eight trigrams. Following Heaven and modeling Earth, bestowing grace in accord with the seasons. Drawing harmony and honoring elders, they enrich and endure forever.

**Lin** | Chasing the fox on the eastern mountain, water blocks my path. Too deep to ford, I lose advantage and miss the later opportunity.
*(See *Sun* → *Jian*, *Meng* → *Gu*.)*

**Guan** | Bearing a mandate, I am shamed by the mission. Unable to endure the task, I fall midway and am made to bear the burden anew.

**Shi He** | The warm and benevolent lord, steadfast in loyalty and filial piety. Entering the inner palace as a model, no misfortune or disaster arises.

**Bi** | Spring brings abundant moisture; summer’s blessings are rich and deep. The harvest ripens, and each acre yields a hundred *hu*. The army marches without discipline—hegemonic ambitions go unfulfilled.

**Bo** | Two women share a chamber, their hearts too troubled to eat. Their hair stands wild as thistledown; sorrow lingers within.

**Fu** | Building a tower on a rocky peak, establishing the wellspring’s source. Illness persists, unrelieved; old and solitary, I dwell beside it.

**Wu Wang** | Seeking to avoid the gate of misfortune, I instead draw near to disaster. Overturned and uncontrolled, pain sears my heart.

**Da Xu** | Creeping and peering, I hide in fear. The fox’s head stays low, lurking—night is its advantage.

**Yi** | A face with nine mouths, a long tongue like an axe. It severs and shatters the coral, cutting off Yin Shang’s posterity.

**Da Guo** | Harmonious qi intermingles; moisture and essence nurture my fine grain.

**Kan** | Smelting metal to cast weapons, the thunder chariot does not roll. The people rest secure in their villages.

**Li** | The words of Qin’s counselors resolve the state’s troubles. One persuades Yan to submit; Qi’s minister gains power.

**Xian** | At dawn, the wise assist the king—Zhou’s virtue shines brightly. Yue Shang presents pheasants; the myriad states know peace.
*(Zhou Gong Dan, Shao Gong Shi.)*

**Heng** | Weak feet, severed heels—no profit in going out. Trade brings no gain; loss and ruin follow.

**Dun** | Hard ice, yellow birds, ever wailing in sorrow. No sweet grain is seen—only flowering mugwort. Startled again and again by crows, my heart is filled with care.
*(See *Qian* → *Shi He*, *Yi* → *Da Guo*.)*

**Da Zhuang** | The soul fades, faint and trembling; the thread of weaving is cut. Suddenly, all becomes clear—I live again.

**Jin** | Yin gives birth to the deer in Kang Valley; mice dance in Ghost Gorge. The sacred tortoise dwells on land; the cauldron’s rice is mixed with dirt. The people foresee the state’s ruin—Jie’s chaos knows no order.

**Ming Yi** | Gathering stones to carve jade, none remain uncut. I raise the dragon’s form; Lu Ban is my aid. The qilin and phoenix take shape—their virtue mirrors the noble one.

**Jia Ren** | Mountains shift to become the sky; dry land turns to sea’s mouth. The people cannot rest in peace.

**Kui** | The east wind opens the door; hidden, I fear yet rejoice. The sprouts receive favor—I regain my child.

**Jian** | A hundred branches of flowering lamps, planted in darkness, wane and dim. Their radiance nearly spent, they fade like ash or dust.

**Xie** | Thirty and still unwed, I lodge in the mulberry grove. The eldest daughter of the upper palace—no shared joy is ours.

**Sun** | The egg battles the stone; surely, it shatters. Toiling brings regret—no timely exit is found.

**Yi** | Qin’s armies contend in strength, losing their integrity and goodness. They defeat my homeland of Ban.

**Guai** | The cruel remove the good and suspect the loyal—difficult to cure. The thoroughbred, trapped in a washbasin cart, is tormented by bit and whip.

**Jian** | Grasping a bamboo shoot to strike the fox, shouldering a bow to shoot the fish.

Not its proper vessel or use—it wearies the heart of its own accord.

**Cui** | The covenant at Kuiqiu, tribute offered in Jin’s court. Seeing the Grand Steward’s plea, the chariot is turned back.

**Sheng** | Sun Bin deceives Pang Juan, carving words on wood to feign favor. The ambush is sprung at last—arrows fall like rain. The Wei army panics in chaos; its general is taken captive.

**Kun** | Journeying south beyond the city, the world gains great fortune. The royal princess returns to Qi, her desires fulfilled, bringing peace to the state.

**Jing** | Winter gathers fern and orchid, the earth frozen hard. Though one flees in haste, by dusk nothing is gained.

**Ge** | Wang Qiao is free of illness, yet the dog’s head aches not. Sandals lost, shoes misplaced—I lack those to send me off.

**Ding** | The swift-footed horse races blindly, guided by a sightless master. Eyes see no path; by midnight, they fail to arrive.

**Zhen** | Seeking profit in a troubled land, I flee northward. Anxious, I return to my city—only to become its foe.

**Jian** | The four-winged paired fish bring peace to my state. Above and below, no peril—this is my blessed fortune.

**Guimei** | The eight talents ascend, accomplishing great deeds. The dragon descends to the palace courtyard; the land knows no disaster.

**Feng** | The thatch wears thin, holes gaping—no one upholds the ancestral home. Servants and maids flee; son west, father east—calamity befalls the self.

**Lü** | Crows dance over the city walls, the town trembles in sudden fear. Virtue unnurtured, it is overthrown by those below.

**Xun** | The five grains fail to ripen; the people suffer hardship and distress. Driving southward, joy and gain are found.

**Dui** | Yellow robes establish the era; virtue and power reside within. Blessings overflow, enfeoffed as lord of Qi. The market knows no gate—wealth and honor abound.

**Gua** | Qi binds the thatch of Guo’s hut, marrying into the Luo capital. Fine and fair, the profit is ten thousandfold.

**Jie** | A bed of comfort, thick quilts—yet one cannot stay long. Forsaking my joyous feast, I am stranded in the southern land. The worry of casting the shuttle—no true disaster comes.

**Zhongfu** | The inner collapses, the body harmed; chaos within, no constancy. Though fine grain abounds, none may eat it.

**Xiaoguo** | Stepping out, I meet misfortune—enmity with disaster. Another bears a sharp blade; my fingertip is wounded.

**Jiji** | Moving in and out with timely measure, no cares in south or north. The traveler arrives at once; those abroad return home.

**Weiji** | The duke’s grandson drives the chariot, touring eastward to Qi. Yanling praises the estate, leaving Ji with stored robes.

---

**Jian (Hexagram 53)**

**Jian** | Parting and scattering, the eldest son joins the army. Uncle Ya falls to bandits; the widow and elder live alone—none plant melons.

**Qian** | Sowing beans at dawn, by dusk they become thick soup. The heart’s desire is fulfilled—joy and contentment abound.

**Kun** | The leopard flies, the gate opens—great troubles dissolve, no harm to the self.

**Zhun** | East mountain, west mountain, each at rest. Though they gaze upon one another, they never share the hall.

**Meng** | Where the flock of crows gathers, a great monstrosity lurks. Nine bodies without heads—the soul startled, the spirit flees. No place to dwell.

**Zhen** | To Meng: Chaos and strife intertwine; the people are desolate. Pursued to the west of Ji, the Di’s maidservants take advantage.

**Song** | Where the qilin and phoenix soar, the land knows no misfortune. The market yields tenfold profit, returning to a land of kindness.

**Shi** | Digging a well for jade, not the treasure of the Bian clan. The body is shamed, the name dishonored—labor yields no gain.

**Bi** | The mountain’s striped tiger and leopard, plump and rich with fat. The noble scion attains his wish—blessings towering high.

**Xiaoxu** | The prosperity of Zhou Cheng: punishments set aside, evil removed. The Grand Steward bestows favor; the noble practices benevolence.

**Lü** | Jade tablets and scepters, holding gifts to meet the king. Nurturing the people of a hundred li, answering the summons of Qi and Qin.

**Xu** | Collapsing, leaking, broken and worn—shattered pillars, cracked tiles. The potter cannot mend them; the bricklayer does not chisel.

**Pi** | The swan flies along the shore; the lord departs, never to return. Uncle Bo lodges as a guest.

**Tongren** | Frogs gather in throngs, beseeching heaven for rain. Thunder rumbles, lightning strikes—timely, the rain falls, fulfilling their wish.

**Dayou** | The old and weak, childless, cannot care for themselves. Though the people grieve, in the end, they do not escape blame. When Guanzi governed the state, the feudal lords submitted as guests. Eight hundred chariots bore him, exalting our Lord Huan’s virtue.

**Qian** | The plum tree’s branches sway and break, parting from its mother, forever estranged, never to know one another.

**Yu** | Abundance within does not cease, yet in decline and old age, clumsiness returns. Fullness and excess bring loss; sores fester while the gall grows fat. Zheng Zhao lost his state, while Chong’er rose to power.
*Alternate text:* When prosperity departs, decline follows; when emaciation leaves, fatness returns. Zheng Zhao lost his state, while Chong’er seized the moment.

**Sui** | Hearing the tiger has entered the town, the heart flees in terror. Running to Yangzong, I do not see Huo Shu—freed from all hidden woes.

**Gu** | Following the times, seizing opportunity, never missing the gate of profit. Gaining much, blessed with fortune, richer than a lord of the marches.

**Lin** | Yu cast the sacred tripods, while Boyi pointed the way. The axe’s blade now broken, the pillar stands alone, leaning. Goods brought to market unsold—withered and withering, a curse.

**Guan** | Spring swans fly east, exchanging horses for gold. Tenfold profit gained, heavily laden, they return home.

**Shike** | Golden teeth, tempered jaws—long life befits the household. Years and harvests overflow. The greedy gain, though troubled, suffer no blame.

**Bi** | Bathed in rich moisture, washing away disgrace. Shaking off disaster and blame, renewed with longevity and fortune.
*Variant:* Bathed in virtue.

**Bo** | Treading in harmony, ascending the palace steps, rising high and steep. Blessings and fortune overflow, upheld by heaven’s might.

**Fu** | The earth’s profound virtue, the teeming multitude flourishes. Peace, prosperity, and uprightness bring great fortune, securing boundless blessings.

**Wu Wang** | Distant lands, divergent paths, filled with dread and fear. Startling me, leaving me flustered—longing for my old home.

**Da Xu** | Swaddled in infancy, now girded and grown. Stepping forth as a guest, what worry do parents hold?

**Yi** | A single span, a hundred joints, bound fast in tangled knots. Fingers plead for release, yet cannot break free.

**Da Guo** | Hawks and falcons hunt their prey; pheasants and hares, exhausted, flee. Head exposed, tail trapped—seized by man’s snare.

**Kan** | Sitting in peril until dusk, entreaties unanswered. No life-giving rain descends; governance proceeds without doubt.

**Li** | The hard and the soft call to one another, two clans become one household. Frost descends, and together they bestow kindness with benevolence.

**Xian** | A loving mother cherishes her child, feasting and bestowing upon the virtuous scholar. The southern tribes submit; the people rejoice in fear.

**Heng** | The good man and Lady Kong, trembling, ascend the tower. Le Ji does not assist; Wei Zhe flees in haste.
*Variant:* Zhai Ji.

**Lü** | The elder son, loyal and upright, is betrayed by the Ji clan. Disaster strikes, leaving no heir; the Minister of War loses his fortune.

**Da Zhuang** | The virtue of festive celebration does not tread in chaotic lands. Though dimmed and without luster, the people receive great fortune.

**Jin** | Driving sheep southward, I encounter misfortune. Wolves startle my horse; tigers steal my child—grief and regret, self-blame.

**Ming Yi** | Father Ni, Confucius, skilled at angling carp. With one cast of the net, ten thousand fish are caught, enriching my home.

**Jiaren** | The root not firm, blossoms and leaves fall away, leaving only a solitary widow.

**Kui** | Setting nets to catch fish, instead I snare a pig. Yuan’s loyalty exhausted, the Wu clan is annihilated.

**Jian** | Swift and agile, like an ape leaping through trees. Though the vermilion bow is tuned, in the end, nothing is caught.

**Xie** | Donning cap and sash, journeying south, I meet fortune as promised. Welcomed in a blessed land, I am granted rank and seize the moment.

**Sun** | A year of abundance, harvests ripe, governance benevolent, the people joyful. Entering office, I gain fortune.

**Yi** | Building towers on rocky peaks, foundations laid by water’s source. Illness lingers, unwell; old and solitary, without neighbors.

**Guai** | Chasing the fox eastward to the mountain, water blocks my path. Too deep to ford—I lose advantage and return.
*Variant:* Meng’s Gu, Shen’s Xun, Gen’s Lin.

**Shen** | The qilin’s young, the phoenix’s chick, born and raised in a blessed land. Where harmonious qi dwells, peace and joy, warmth and kindness abound. The state teems with sages.

**Cui** | Journeying west in search of jade, I find no Bian uncut gem—only ill fortune and malevolence, startling and confounding me.

**Sheng** | Heart wild, will perverse, hearing and sight deaf and blind. The proper mandate falters; the common folk teem with affliction.

**Kun** | The southern state’s youngest son, gifted and fair of mien, seeks my eldest daughter. Scorned for his lowly station, I refuse—only to receive one foul and vile, and later grieve deeply.
*Variant:* Shi Ke’s Guai.

**Jing** | Winding through high plains, the family elder acts recklessly, throwing the five officials into chaos.

**Ge** | Expressing gratitude, bowing in virtue, I journey east back to my homeland, where joy and fortune await.

**Ding** | The parrot takes flight with the flock, longing for a mate yet finding none. Clutching the jade pendant, I seek an audience—let none prevent this union.

**Zhen** | Calamity weighs heavy, sorrow deepens; the body bears punishment and guilt, and even the spirits cannot absolve it.

**Gen** | Tigers and leopards, bears in abundance, roam and play in the mountain valleys. The benevolent and worthy nobleman attains his heart’s desire.
*Variant:* Qian’s Zhong Fu.

**Guimei** | At the sea’s edge, the distant northeast—fortune and prosperity arrive. Gentle and refined, blessed with grace, what fault lies in the Nine Yi?

**Feng** | Hua Peak’s mountain, where immortals roam the Dao. Favorable for dwelling—long free from fault or sorrow.
*Variant:* Qian’s Jing.

**Lü** | Jia, Yi, Wu, Geng—moving with the seasons, never losing their proper rhythm. Sprouts bend to the law, all life emerges in accord, each following its kind.
*Variant:* Guimei’s Tongren.

**Xun** | Stumbling at the fork, losing advantage in the later market—no fawn is caught.

**Dui** | The merchant’s servant, self-important, refuses to yield to those below. Blood rises from the earth—punishment and retribution lose their reason.

**Huan** | The Yangtze, the Yellow River, the Huai, the sea—heaven’s great markets. Merchants receive fortune, the nation abounds in wealth.

**Jie** | Tempering emotions, curbing desires, taxation measured with restraint. Households are provided for, the people content—both noble and rich.

**Zhongfu** | The mare neighs and calls, seeking her mate. Clouds and rain gather in great assembly, flowing to form rivers and seas.

**Xiaoguo** | The path of sun and moon—wherever they travel, they must arrive, free from misfortune.

**Jiji** | Riding the wind aloft, soaring with the flying birds. A single flight of a thousand li—I see my beloved mother.
*Variant:* Mingyi’s Ding.

**Weiji** | Yin matches yang’s affairs, the outer wood inverts its stance. The nobleman proceeds—his office is lost.
*Variant:* Guimei’s fifty-fourth.

**Guimei** | Hard ice, the yellow bird, ever mourns its plaintive cry. No sweet grain is seen—only the glory of blossoms and punishment. Repeated alarms from magpies and crows—my heart is racked with care.

**Qian** | Punished wood grows in winter, the Minister of Justice delays sentencing. Authority lies below—the nation is in chaos and on the verge of collapse.

**Kun** | The panting ox, stricken by heat, cannot plow the fields. Weeds remain uncut—the year yields nothing.

**Zhun** | The fish seeks to swim against the current, but the many lack a common heart. Supreme virtue lies hidden.

**Meng** | Spring plowing brings rest, autumn harvest yields fortune and blessing. Offering the great boar in sacrifice, success is celebrated with joy.

**Xu** | Born with sagely virtue, matched to the Great Ultimate above. The august spirits establish the center—bestowing fortune upon me.
*Variant:* Jiaren’s Xu.

**Song** | Right hand on the zither’s head, left hand adjusting the sash. Endless strife and contention, mutual hostility—departing with no gain.

**Shi** | Roasting fish, grasping the dipper, leaning on the great rat. The tongue forgets taste, mockery arises as a curse—pressed down, it cannot escape.

**Bi** | Shen and You delight in submission, oxen and horses rest. The nobleman is at peace, the laborer finds relief.

**Xiaochu** | At Yao’s gate, the marquis is ennobled, his sagely virtue ever increasing. The people know no weariness, secure and without fear.

**Lǚ** | The solitary lord, the widowed wife—alone they lodge in sorrow. Eyes strain wide, ears ring hollow; none share in laughter or speech.

**Song** | *See* **Guimei**. Beyond the frontier, fine livestock are gained, and marriages are made. The wise and worthy gather, consulting on affairs. Yet the city is overthrown, the household left in turmoil.

**Pi** | Molten sand in scorching heat—few remain unspoiled. Three *li* from the river, my profitable trade is ruined. The old hand rears horses—what regret in leaving them?

**Tongren** | Under Jia, Yi, Wu, and Geng, one moves with the seasons. No fixed rhythm is lost; sprouts bend to the measure. All emerge in harmony, each delighting in its kind. *See* **Jian’s Lü**.

**Dayou** | Wandering by night, I meet my lord. Sorrows untangled, the heart is freed from care.

**Qian** | A dead friend, a severed bond—clever words become slander. White is soiled to black, and Yan Shu’s voice is stilled for a time.

**Yu** | Three years chasing gain, profit flees like a spirit. Turning east and west, like a bird dodging a pellet.

**Sui** | The dike breaks at its center, the river floods its banks. Crops are ruined, the people flee their homes. The lord sleeps alone, our town drowned in the deluge.

**Gu** | Yin and Yang are cut off, the betrothal long delayed. Niqiu’s new terrace—regret and sighs for what has passed. *See* **Jin’s Wuwang**.

**Lin** | Boyi and Shuqi, paragons of integrity. With virtue they ward off calamity, and sorrow finds no foothold. *See* **Tai’s Qian**, **Ge’s Pi**, **Bi’s Bo**.

**Guan** | Yang turns reckless and mad, drawing his sword to wound himself—bringing ruin upon his own body. *See* **Mingyi’s Jing**.

**Shike** | The scholar takes office, yet it cannot compare to tilling the fields—there, one gains long life and preserves the years. Carving stone yields no harvest; rushing rites brings no renown. The seamstress loses her needle, the loom stands idle.

**Bo** | The sacred turtle stranded on land, suddenly bereft of its place. Yi Zi returns to plow, but Jie’s chaos finds no aid.

**Fu** | The house stands by the plain’s edge, yet is swept away to become the sea. Wealth and property vanish; clothing and food are no more.

**Wuwang** | The parrot pecks at grain, only to be chased by a fox. It flees, unable to eat, panting in terror.

**Dachu** | My home lies at the sea’s edge, encircled by deep currents. How dare I shrink from the journey? Yet there is no wood to hasten my way.

**Yi** | The whetstone of another mountain becomes an enemy’s weapon. It comes to attack my city, wounding my flesh—the nation is thrown into turmoil. *See* **Mingyi’s Jing**.

**Daguo** | A tarnished mirror gives no light, its patterns unseen. The youngest daughter does not wed, but flees to her lord.

**Kan** | The great serpent and the giant fish slay one another. Lord and minister are cut off; Guo Gong loses his home.

**Li** | The line is severed, no heir remains. Blessing and fortune vanish. The spirit scatters, leaving the body behind.

**Xian** | By the virtue of the cultured lord, the people are nurtured and fortune is brought forth. No child is lost young; the nation prospers, its people treasured. The anxious gaze upon it, and even the hatred of thieves and bandits ceases.

**Heng** | In the land of harmonious joy, delight becomes my blessing. From the eastern peaks to the southern mountains, crossing brings favor and gratitude.

**Zhu** | The sorrow of the grieving man—his steps falter, his face changes. Bringing ruin upon himself, he must guard his own conduct.

Embracing joy in mutual embrace, the eldest son reaches venerable age, receiving blessings and divine favor.

**Great Strength** | The Grand Duke fled from Zhou, concealed in seclusion for seventy years. At last, he met the sagely Wen, becoming the kingdom’s pillar.

**Ming Yi’s Kun**

**Jin** | On the upper reaches of the Jiang and Han, governance is perverse and the people grieve. The yin supplants the yang; the female usurps the male lord.

**Ming Yi** | Tangled as disordered silk, raising a hand brings disaster. Chasing hares through the fields, one’s clothes are soaked and ruined.

**The Family** | Rotten wood borne by stench, aided by wolves. Husband lost, child gone—grief extends to parents.

**Divergence** | The sheep arrives unmet; the woman holds an empty basket. The hare limps, the deer is deformed; Green Mountain collapses, slander and flattery arise in chaos.

**Obstruction** | Drawing a sword to wound the hand, facing the enemy without joy. A loyal minister lacks support, beset by trouble and fault.

**Release** | Three offerings, five omens—together they proceed. Lost in an empty marsh, following the valley due north. Traversing six brambles, one is harmed and defeated.

**Decrease** | Contending for the oriole, the sheep is lost; the golden pouch vanishes. Gains are short-lived—the woes of Chen and Cai find peace only through Chu.

**Heng’s Central**

**Increase** | Three black steeds bear the crossbeam, journeying south to gather fragrant angelica. Autumn orchids, rich and sweet, fill the sacred coffer, benefiting my middle and youngest brothers.

**Gua** | In the first month of spring, on the day *ji-chou*, one calls out to Uncle Zhong. When bright virtue ends, tyranny and cruelty flourish.

**Pregnancy** | "The shoe does not fit the foot"—the southern mountain bears many leaves. A household with orchids and angelica knows no illness.

**Gathering** | Three legs, no head—it knows not where to go. The heart is mad, the eyes are wounded; let none make it see, for it beholds not the daylight.

**Ascending** | Supporting Yao and aiding Yu, the towering pines and Pengzu. Passing west of the Queen Mother, the road is smooth and easy—none dare oppose.

**The Army’s Li**

**Distress** | Fading, fading away—woe and misfortune entwine. Separated by rocky mountains, the household scatters.

**The Well** | The sacred tortoise on land, suddenly displaced. Yi’s son returns to plowing; Jie’s chaos lacks aid.

**Revolution** | Benevolent virtue spreads, grace extending to distant lands. Blessings reach foreign realms, while hidden calamities lurk. If one does not build a house early, in the cold there will be no shelter.

**The Cauldron** | Summer wheat, lush and abundant, its awns struck by frost. The cruel lord ruins the state, causing years to be cut short.

**Thunder** | Though fire blazes fiercely, it is behind me. Though bandits are many, they are to my right. My body is safe and fortunate, free from peril.

**Thunder’s Guimei, Abundance’s Need**

**Mountain** | Distant roads severed, the traveler lodges with much regret. The stubborn and reckless gather, breeding my fear and dread.

**Ming Yi’s Small Livestock**

**Gradual Progress** | Suspended over the southern sea, ten thousand *li* from home. The flying hare and swift steed—one day I see my mother, dispelling my sorrow and regret.

**Abundance** | Obstructed, then through—though pressed, not impoverished. At last, the wish is fulfilled; Ji and Jiang follow together.

**Travel** | The western merchant in Ba and Shu, the cold snow reaching the hub. Wishing to advance but unable, he returns to an empty chamber.

**Wind** | Building a new tomb, it collapses and is hard to ascend. Three colts push the cart, stumbling and wounding the jaw.

**Lake** | Stretching the neck to gaze at wine, it does not enter my mouth. Hollow-eyed, self-tormenting—the gain is nothing, yet the recluse is pleased.

**Exchange** | Mid-spring to early summer, where harmonious *qi* dwells. It brings me joy and fortune; the land knows no ruin or thieves.

**Moderation** | Casting a net to catch the turtledove, the hare escapes its harm. Male and female both caught, they are sold and betrayed.

**Li** should be *li* (suffering).

**Inner Truth** | Three travel together; one speaks of going north. The elder and second wish to go south, but the youngest cannot. The middle desires to split the path—strife and harm arise.

**Small Exceeding** | Promises unkept, deceit misleads. Forced to sleep in the open, returning at night to a warm chamber. The spirits are angered by injustice; ghosts strike the eyes.

**Desire** | Seeking fortune and profit, instead one harms oneself.

**Da Gu’s Observation**

**Completion** | Presenting words to convey sincerity, bringing peace without collapse. Increasing blessings and longevity, achieving fame and success.

**Ming Yi’s Jin**

**Incompletion** | Fire burns the lord’s bed, the household is destroyed. Yet peace and prosperity come—first sorrow, then heavy mourning.

**Feng (Abundance)**

**All Under Heaven** | The young merchants travel, crossing mountains and perilous paths. Trading with the Di tribes, they fear no danger—profits multiply

**Having enjoyed fine fortune, one attains it through righteousness.**

**Wu Wang (No Delusion)**
Three wildcats hunt the rat, blocking its path before and behind.
It dies within the city walls, unable to flee.

**Li’s You**

**Da Xu (Great Accumulation)**
Ghosts dance at the state altar—yearly joy, the people’s delight.
Ministers pay proper rites to their lord; sons show filial piety to their fathers.

**Yi (Nourishment)**
A loving mother awaits her son, her longing thoughts unceasing.
A traveler far from home in the wilds—my heart is heavy with sorrow.

**Da Guo (Great Exceeding)**
The Rain Master takes a bride, Huangyan’s youngest son.
The rites completed, the marriage sealed, they call to each other and ascend southward.
Rich moisture nourishes the earth below; the year’s harvest is abundant.
*(See also: Sun’s Yi, Dun’s Jin, Jing’s Kun, the original hexagram’s Bi.)*

**Kan (The Abysmal)**
Two dogs encircle the house, snarling and snapping over food.
A crooked arrow flies west, striking my violent state.
Gaozong campaigns against the Gui tribes—three years before they submit.
Early frost and late snow damage the grain and harm the wheat.
Labor is wasted, strength exhausted—hunger leaves nothing to eat.

**Li’s Gu**

**Xian (Influence)**
Where does the rot and stench arise? Green flies gather in swarms.
White turns to black, bringing ruin to the state.
The lord is driven out by his ministers—his favor extinguished.

**Zhen (The Arousing)**
Leading a sheep, it refuses to advance, turning against the heart’s intent.
Words are heard but not believed, misleading the elder.
*(One version reads: Speech is not abundant, misleading the elder.)*

**You (Wandering)**
Sweet endurance of harm, yet mutual enmity persists.
Lord Shang’s cruel punishments brought ruin upon himself.

**Da Zhuang (Great Strength)**
The ram butts without aim—blood is scant, no broth is made.
A woman holds an empty basket, unable to pluck the mulberry roots.

**Sui’s Gen**

**Jin**
Chirping and chattering, the impoverished ghosts reproach one another.
No joy or ease—nine knots tied in a single day.
*Shock’s Already Fated.*

**Ming Yi**
Two feet, four wings—flying into a blessed land.
My elder sister finds peace; mother and child are reunited.
*Adornment’s Fellowship.*

**Family**
On Wenshan, purple mushrooms; on Yongliang, vermilion grasses.
They grow in harmonious qi, treasured by kings.
The ancestral spirit joins the feast—fortune and blessings arrive.
*Opposition*

A soul cut off from the world, bereft of fortune and blessing.
Spirit scattered, body sundered.

**Obstruction**
The Purple Palace of the North Star—robed and capped, standing at the center.
Embracing vastness, establishing virtue, ever receiving great fortune.
*Release*

Uncle Sai and Uncle Shu are blind—none guard the stump.
I lose my robes and furs, taking your place in the yin realm.
*Vessel’s Radiance.*

**Decrease**
Two women share a chamber—hearts too troubled to eat.
Hair tangled like brambles, sorrow ever within.
*Stilling’s Splitting.*

**Increase**
Leaving bitterness for desolation, poison grows ever more cruel.
Fleeing and abandoned, one falls into a pit—daily woes arise.
*Decisiveness*
At first illness, in the end misfortune; in the end, death and mourning—no light seen.

**Pregnancy**
Three crows fly forth, arriving in timely fortune.
Those who journey together first reap the greatest gain.
*Fellowship’s Great Possession, Shock’s Parting.*

**Gathering**
Deer graze on mountain grasses, heedless of the village.
Though long delayed, no blame.
*Ascending*

A sheep’s gut, nine twists—pushing forward together, they halt.
Only the king’s grandson may ascend to heaven.
*Decrease’s Shock, Treading’s Army, Influence’s Splitting, Overseeing’s Grounding.*

**Distress**
Guan Zhong met Duke Huan, fulfilling his joyful wish.
Eyes glued shut, shaking off his cap—no sorrow.
Laughing and jesting without gravity, empty words and reckless deeds.
*Darkening’s Travel.*

**Well**
Jie and Jue dwell together—people distressed and sorrowful.
Traveling slowly, lingering in Qi and Lu.
*Return’s Exaltation.*

**Reform**
A soul alone, no home—gnawing its fingers, refusing to eat.
The thief Zhang boasts of his deeds, yet facing the enemy, loses his meat.
*Vessel*

Slanderous words disrupt the state, overturning right for wrong.
Bo Qi is estranged; Gongzi grieves for them both.
*Grounding’s Viewing.*

**Shock**
The Lord of Wei wanders in fetters, bewitched by the young concubine.
I lose my parents—long deluded, they do not return.
*Force’s Ascending, Travel’s Army.*

**Stilling**
The parrot cries in unison, longing to pair but finding no home.
Holding a jade pendant, seeking an audience—none can bring it to pass.
*Gradual’s Vessel.*

**Gradual**
Righteousness cannot overcome desire—entangled by longing.
Coveting profit, endangering oneself—horns broken, neck snapped.
*Earth’s Abundance, Return’s Earth, Passing’s Ascending.*

**Marrying Maiden**
Ministers exalted, the lord debased—power wanes daily.
Encroachment dims all light; the three families expel the duke.
*Ascending’s Grounding.*

**Travel**
Uncle Zhong excels in trade, making markets with joy.
Unfearing peril, he gains tenfold profit.
*Grounding*

Six snakes slither in flight, all plunging into the lush grass.
Startled on the long road, dreading the pecking beak.
*Well’s Joy, Center’s Faith’s Family.*

**Joy**
The waters ruin my village, flowing east to become the sea.
The clamor of turtles and clams makes dwelling uneasy.
*Travel’s Marrying Maiden.*

**Dispersing**
It does not fly far, lingering as a lowly servant within.
Its stipend meager, its wealth not yet abundant.
*Exchange’s Great Accumulation.*

**Moderation**
Yin transforms into yang; the woman becomes a man.
The Way of governance flows freely—lord and minister follow one another.
*Shock’s Radiance, Unfinished’s Parting, Dispersing’s Travel.*

**Center’s Faith**
Treading through peril and hardship, escaping calamity and woe.
Entering the gate of fortune and joy, meeting the great lord’s instruction.
*Shock’s Family, Joy’s Force.*

**Small Exceeding**
The net tightens, movement brings greater sorrow.
Distressed, one cannot rest.
*Already Fated*

Bearing an ox up the mountain—strength fails, the path is hard.
Fierce wind and rain, snow blocking my way.
Mid-journey, I turn back—those in sorrow find joy.
*Fellowship’s Without Trouble, Contention’s Splitting, Travel’s Opposition.*

**Unfinished**
Lush and fragrant grasses, longing for sweet rain to descend.
The scenic wind rises—imbibing the timely dew,
it nourishes my crops.
*Travel’s Fifty-Sixth*

**Travel**
The net spreads in four directions—birds have nowhere to soar.

**Expedition**

Exhausted from punitive campaigns, starving and parched, unable to eat.
*Revolution’s Peace, Joy’s Small Exceeding.*

**Qian ☰**
A mistletoe without roots, drifting like passing clouds.
Its foundation unsteady, it soon falls away,
becoming but a withered tree.
*Nurturance’s Decay.*

**Kun ☷**
A man without steadfast principle—an ox descends with trailing reins.
The male serpent flees in haste; yang fails to restrain yin,
and thus his household falls to ruin.

**Zhun ☳**
Where flocks of birds take flight, a great omen lurks within.
Nine bodies, no head—souls take fright, spirits flee,
and none dare dwell there.
*Gradual Progress’s Ignorance.*

**Meng ☶**
Sealing the Zhuo Ditch, flooding cities and towns.
Fire lodges in the mouth—
the people suffer many ailments.
*Waiting.*

**Xu ☰**
Beating wings, stirring pinions, soaring beyond the realm.
Wandering freely, drifting at ease,
they return to the warm chamber.
*Decrease’s Contemplation.*

**Song ☵**
Autumn’s painting left unfinished, winter’s sowing bears no life.
The Yin king defies principle,
forfeiting his favored name.
*Legion.*

**Shi ☷**
The Marquis of Wei wanders afar, bewitched by the Younger Concubine.
I lose my parents, lost in long delusion, never to return.
*Qian’s Ascent, Abundance’s Shock.*

**Bi ☷**
Crows gather with sparrows, drawn to evil company.
Magpies and crows exchange calls,
yet their hearts betray them.
*Small Nurturance.*

**Xiao Xu ☰**
A parrot without spurs clashes with sparrows in battle.
Wings broken, eyes blinded,
wounded by its foe.
*Treading.*

**Lü ☷**
Worms born within the wood gnaw above and below,
bringing ruin to my land.
*Peace.*

**Tai ☷**
Yanling journeys to Lu, observing music with the Grand Historian.
Chariots rumble, white-maned steeds—
he foresees Qin’s rise.

The state unites in its end, one ruler ascends.
*Kan’s Stripping, Great Accumulation’s Separation.*

**Pi ☷**
Ministers’ bond endures, never resting.
Timely clouds gather, blessing wherever they go.
*Fellowship.*

**Tong Ren ☰**
Lungs tilt, baskets break,
roofs leak, walls crumble—
Lady Ji finds no peace.
*Great Possession.*

**Eastward into the sea’s mouth,**
following the current northward.
Rising high then sinking low,
five towns lose their lord.
Six nights and seven days,
death comes at the water’s edge.
*Kui’s Obstruction.*

**Qian ☷**
Tigers swarm the town,
seeking meat to devour.
The great one defends—
the lord keeps his land.
*Contentment.*

**Yu ☷**
Fourfold chaos unsettles,
east and west bring calamity.
Retreat to the mountain’s foot,
never leave the realm—
thus preserved whole,
relying on life’s blessing.
*Great Possession’s Separation.*

**Sui ☷**
Shu Gan bears grievance,
Qi Zi flees his fief.
Rushing to resolve the crisis,
Yang She escapes—
his life spared.
*Obstruction’s Qian.*

**Gu ☷**
Craning for wine,
it never reaches my lips.
Sunken eyes torment themselves,
profit and gain vanish.
*Lawsuit’s Increase, Treading’s Gathering.*

**Lin ☷**
Virtue of humane governance,
growing daily in reverence.
The capital’s walls stand firm,
daily receiving its fortune.
*Xun’s Initial Difficulty.*

**Guan ☷**
Pulling the head, striking the tail,
bent near to death.
A degenerate age lacks kindness—
nowhere to return.
*Ascending’s Great Accumulation.*

**Shi He ☷**
Teaching sheep to chase hares,
making fish hunt mice.
Entrusting the wrong man,
wasting days without success.
*Waiting’s Biting Through.*

**Bi ☷**
Born with horns and tail,
spreading calamity to rule the house.
Driving out sheep, pursuing foxes,
the Zhangs supplant the Duke—
grief and disaster compound.
*Stripping.*

**Falling from safety into peril,**
plunging into wells and pools,
shattering my jade.
Then chewing orchid roots, swallowing yellow,
sipping jade’s essence.
Communing with spirits, flowing as one,
forever free of sorrow and misfortune.
*Completion’s Obstruction.*

**Wu Wang ☰**
Heavy wings struggle to fly,
unable to cross the pass,
never leaving the courtyard walls.
*Thunder’s Cauldron.*

**Da Xu ☰**
Nests topple, trees snap,
damaging my sacred vessels.
Elder stumbles, younger falls—
the sheep lost, then pursued.
*Corners of the Mouth.*

**Six travel together,**
each forgetting their sack.
The yellow crane loses its pearl—
nothing left to illuminate.
*Adornment’s Biting Through.*

**Da Guo ☰**
Scattering branches, shifting forks.
Parting from mother,
cut off, never to know one another.
*Great Possession’s Kun.*

**Kan ☷**
Welcoming fortune, opening the door,
joy follows behind.
Duke Cao’s kindness and harmony
make him lord of Song.
*Separation.*

**Li ☷**
Both foolish and mad,
two eyes gone blind.
Squatting in darkness, mute—
deemed useless.
*Influence.*

**Xian ☷**
Golden beams, jade pillars,
a decade of steadfast strength.
Unrotted, whole—
the sage dwells in peace.
*Constancy.*

**Heng ☷**
Wrapping rations, shouldering grain,
meeting a hunter on the path.
Wanting to fly but unable,
ensnared by the net.
*Pursuit.*

**Driving away Peng Sheng’s demon,**
the violent dragon wreaks havoc.
Stealing Yao’s robes,
marauders brandish weapons.
The blue bird lights the night—
after three dawns, Qi falls.
*Cauldron’s Delay, Comparison’s Youth.*

**Da Zhuang ☷**
The coarse-clad man and old woman
cannot bear children,
living as widower and widow.
*Advancement.*

**Jin ☷**
The quail steals tallow,
nesting on a slender branch.
Shaken, unstable,
blown by the wind.
Heart chilled, trembling—
ever fearing danger.
*Darkening Light.*

**The plain carriage, wooden horse,**
unfit to bear weight.
The prince sets out on campaign—
doubt and worry bring misfortune.
*Household.*

**Trapped on all sides,**
yet safe and unharmed.
Favorable to dwell here,
protecting one’s jade maiden.
*Separation.*

**Carrying an ox up the mountain,**
strength fails, the path is hard.
Fierce wind and rain,
blocking my way—
mid-journey, I turn back.
*Lawsuit’s Stripping.*

**The golden city, jade walls,**
all unite in strength.
Governance is just, the people dear—
bandits dare not plunder.
*Release.*

**Pure and deep, yet blocked,**
slandered by rumors.
Evidence clarifies the truth,
struck at the root’s warmth.
The sweet pear’s judgment—
clearly, grace is received.
*Army’s Decay.*

**Sun ☷**
Gao Yao hears the case,
Qi Bo rejoices.
Westward to Hua’s road,
eastward home without blame.
*Increase.*

**Bowing the head, stealing glances,**
fearing to be seen.
Acting brings misfortune—
wine sours, fish spoil,
none dare to taste.
*Cauldron’s Release.*

**Ten pheasants, a hundred chicks,**
always with their mother.
Holding a hawk, wrestling a tiger—
who would find it amusing?
*Pregnancy.*

**High mounds and mountains,**
steep cliffs crumble.
An omen for the state—
the supreme ruler perishes.
*Gathering.*

**Six magpies retreat in flight,**
an ill omen for Xiang.
Armies join in battle,
the left thigh is wounded.
Thus he collapses and dies—
his hegemony unfulfilled.
*Obstruction’s Decay.*

**Ascending ☰**
Foreign lands, strange customs,
hearts never in accord.
Metal and wood as enemies,
the Qiang and Di seize control.
*Household’s Unfinished.*

**Kun ☷**
Crows caw in the courtyard,
warning of disaster.
Double gates, watchmen’s clappers—
guarding against violent intruders.
*Well.*

**The kind mother and her child**
receive gifts and gain scholars.
Subduing the Yi, removing threats—
the royal house is secure,
obscurity meets its time.
*Removing Doubt, Becoming Leisurely.*

**Revolution ☷**
Borderlands breed wicked men,
blocking the path of virtue.
Scorching drought brings ruin,
the year’s harvest greatly harmed.
*Kun’s Great Possession.*

**Cauldron ☷**
Walking in great virtue,
awaiting the sash’s tying.
The cultured lord hunts,
Lü Shang gains fortune.

**Proclaimed Grand Preceptor, enfeoffed to establish the State of Qi.**

**Zhen ☳**
The campaigning general halts evil,
drumming at Han to eliminate bandits.
Qing Zhong flees to Ju,
Zi Ban gains fortune.

**Gen ☶**
The worthy man and virtuous woman,
joined in harmonious union.
Many descendants, long-lived children,
fearing joy’s enduring span.

**Jian ☴**
Four stallions wind and weave,
longing for their mother.
Royal affairs lack rest,
no peace to dwell in.
*Exchange for Fu.*

**Guimei ☳**
Water ruins my village,
flowing east to the sea.
Turtles and fish clamor,
no place to settle.
*Feng to Dui.*

**Feng ☱**
Silken bolts bundled tight,
mourning gifts for my Meng Kong.
Summoned to escort the lord,
names and titles change.

**Xun ☴**
The firm practices great virtue,
nurturing the Six Directions.
Warmth ripens the harvest,
bringing me fortune and power.

**Dui ☱**
The great states of Qin and Jin,
clashing in mutual strife.
Capturing Hui, seizing Zhi Yu,
Zheng bears the blame.

**Huan ☵**
Darkness and gloom,
the lord lacks order.
On the jiazi day, chaos arises,
Duke Jian meets his end.

**Jie ☱**
Three legs without a head,
not knowing where to go.
The heart mad, the essence harmed,
none can bring light—
the sun’s radiance unseen.
*Xiaoxu to Fu.*

**Zhongfu ☱**
Long nights, short days,
yin preys upon yang.
All things wither and dry,
hidden in the northern wilds.
*Yang to Mingyi, Qian to Jian.*

**Xiaoguo ☶**
Roaming by night,
encountering the lord.
Dispelling vexation, resolving doubt,
bringing me no sorrow.
*Guimei to Dayou.*

**Jiji ☲**
Pursuing deer on South Mountain,
knowing I enter the gate.
Yin and yang in harmony,
the state free from disaster.
The eldest son flees,
awaiting his benevolent lord.

**Weiji ☳**
Begging to ride the left ear,
stingy, refusing me.
Driving away my parents.

**Xun ☴**
The warm mountain’s pines,
ever lush, never falling.
The luan and phoenix find shelter,
gaining their joy.
*Ding to Tai, Xu to Kun, Pi to Heng.*

**Qian ☰**
Gathering dodder in Mu’s village,
seeking me in Sang’s midst.
Losing trust, failing to meet,
grief binds my waist.
*Wuwang to Heng, Shi to Shihe.*

**Kun ☷**
A bird flies in,
perching on the palace tree.
Its cry sounds alarm,
the lord departs.
*Tun to Fu.*

**Tun ☷**
The virtue of benevolent governance,
daily growing more abundant.
The capital’s walls stand firm,
daily receiving its blessings.

**Meng ☷**
The other mountain’s flaws,
enmity with Lü.
Besieging our city,
wounding our flesh,
the state thrown into turmoil.
*Mingyi, Xun, Meng.*

**Xu ☴**
Demanding cowries to ransom the fox,
refusing my words.
Bound to the tiger’s whiskers,
dragged but not coming.
*Zhen to Xian, Cui to Jian, Pi to Ge, Sui to Shi.*

**Song ☵**
One reed, two tongues,
flattering words and sycophantic speech.
Three traitors make a tiger,
even Zeng’s mother casts her shuttle.
*Shi to Qian.*

**Shi ☷**
Thin conduct, wagging tail,
chasing clouds to clear water.
Mud becomes land,
low fields fit for millet.

**Bi ☷**
The ninefold gates of heaven,
probing within, no passage.
Ascending at dawn, arriving at dusk—
the divine lord unseen.

**Xiaoxu ☶**
Dim and unclear,
ears deaf, no hearing.
Sinking into the marsh’s depths,
drowning, meeting misfortune.
*Dui to Jing.*

**Lü ☶**
Mist, dew, early frost,
the sun darkened.
Yin and yang’s perverse affliction,
the year’s harvest greatly harmed.

**Tai ☷**
Three steps to the earthen terrace,
virtue and righteousness shine in the hall.
Courteous exchanges, mutual deference,
feasting and succession.
The Earl of Ji attends the king,
bestowing upon me black and yellow silk.

**Pi ☷**
Quarreling over quails, losing sheep,
profit not enduring.
The troubles of Chen and Cai,
relying on Chu for peace.

**Tongren ☷**
Heaven drought, water scarce,
withered and dry, no moisture—
nothing to reap.

**Dayou ☷**
Tao Zhu and Bai Gui,
skilled merchants amassing wealth.
The lord’s sons and nobles,
rich, never poor.

**Qian ☷**
The turtle wearies of rivers and seas,
traveling land without cease.
Self-inflicted withering,
losing its market,
regret without blame.

**Yu ☷**
The yellow bird gathers mulberry,
having sown, no weeds.
Thinking of my father and brothers,
longing to restore the state.

**Sui ☷**
Field mice and wild fledglings,
ever wishing to flee.
Bound in cages and pens,
no freedom to move.
*Guai to Qian, Xu to Sui.*

**Gu ☷**
The state without a lord,
the Xia clan rebels.
The Wuhao bow secretly loosed,
Duke Ling meets his end.
*Jiji to Shihe, Lin to Jin.*

**Lin ☷**
A giant serpent, a great sturgeon,
battling at the state’s outskirts.
Above and below blocked,
the lord flees in flight.
*Bo to Gen.*

**Guan ☷**
Slanderous words disrupt the state,
overturning right and wrong.
Boqi exiled, Gongzi grieving.
*Feng to Ding.*

**Shi ☷**
Gloom and obscurity,
harmed by yin.
Mists gather,
together stealing the sun’s light.

**Bi ☸**
Gazing at the city, embracing a child,
seeing the village unharmed.
The duke’s grandson ascends the hall,
the great lord rejoices.

**Bo ☷**
Three worms become gu,
carving and flattering, no allies.
"Victorious Mother" and "Thief Spring"—
the noble man does not dwell there.
*Yu to Guan, Guan to Kun.*

**Fu ☷**
Chariots race, men hasten,
armor rolled, seeking battle.
Qi and Lu raid and fight,
defeated at Taiqiu.

**Fu to Xiaoxu, Kun to Dui.**
**Wuwang**
Seeking to visit Ziche,
fine words deceive and flatter.
Duke Huan’s welcome arrives—
yet what was promised is not seen.

**Daxu**
Quarreling over pheasants, losing sheep,
the golden pouch is gone.
Gains are not lasting—
the troubles of Chen and Cai
rely on Chu for peace.
*Guimei to Sun.*

**Yi**
At year’s end, flowers fall,
yang enters yin’s chamber.
The myriad things hide in concealment—
profit cannot be obtained.

**Daguo**
The morning wind’s patterned wings,
a great flock seeks warmth.
Passing through my walled city,
Yi gains nothing.
*Dazhuang to Zhen, Xiaoxu to Ge, Daguo to Yu.*

**Kan**
Holding a magpie, embracing its young,
seeing a snake—what blame?
The household remains intact,
none lose their place.

**Li**
Rumbling great thunder,
mists thicken into rain.
A woman grows mad and wild,
startling the neighboring villages.

**Xian**
Footless, heels severed,
dwelling brings no peace—
misfortune and calamity arise.
*Ge to Jian.*

**Da**

A broken basket, a tattered mat—
cast aside on the road,
no longer treasured.

**You**

Three parrots peck at grain,
ten chicks follow to feed.
A starving kite strikes suddenly—
two fledglings are lost.
*Zhongfu to Yi.*

**Dazhuang**

Seven hundred chariots ride forth,
illuminating virtue and power.
At Jiantu and Kuiqiu,
Qi and Jin receive blessings.
*Dui to Bo.*

**Jin**

A hundred legs move as one,
mutual support makes strength.
Three sages assist the enterprise—
the royal house shines in glory.
*Tun to Lü, Jin to Kun, Zhu to Fu, Jing to Lü.*

**Mingyi**

Canonical texts and legal writs,
stored in the Orchid Terrace.
Though chaos and ruin arise,
they alone escape disaster.
*Kun to Daxu, Dayou to Heng, Zhongfu to Heng.*

**Jiaren**

Western tribes resist, unyielding,
relying on might and force.
Turning from the Way to rush the foe,
the army is crushed and overthrown.
*Yi to Tongren, Xu to Tun.*

**Kui**

Spring’s yang revives the grasses,
summer lengthens the branches.
The myriad things flourish and multiply,
filling and increasing their store.
*Jing to Xun.*

**Jian**

Withered and white, the stumps stand bare—
no millet or sorghum will grow.
Nothing to offer in sacrifice,
the spirits lack their rites.

**Xie**

Tearing robes to cross the river,
the torrent runs swift and deep.
Fortune favors the boatman—
crossing safely, no harm befalls.
*Kun to Cui, Jian to Shi.*

**Sun**

Go forth to trade in the market,
what you seek will double.
Returning with joy, a child in arms,
profit becomes your friend.
*Weiji to Yi, Daguo to Dan.*

**Yi**

The elder campaigns against Dongyi,
the younger strikes Liaoxi.
Great victory is won—
enfeoffed at Hejian.
Though first startled and alarmed,
afterward, no injury comes.
Receiving blessings and fortune,
filial piety makes one king.

**Gou**

Following the wind, riding the dragon,
meeting with fortune.
Fields yield triple harvests,
merchants and travelers succeed.
In the well-ordered city,
Chang’an knows no harm.

**Cui**

Fish stir the muddied waters,
bandits besiege our town.
The city stands imperiled, unsafe—
terror and madness arise.
Though blocked, the way reopens;
treading peril, no misfortune.
Preserve your bright merit,
establish the lineage by the Dao.

**Kun**

The earth’s deep virtue, Kun’s generosity,
nurtures the ten thousand things.
Peace, prosperity, and uprightness
bring great fortune to rest.
*Tai to Xie, Bi to Lü, Huan to Xie, Jian to Fu.*

**Jing**

Mountain torrents rage in fury,
smashing beams and snapping pillars.
Travelers are hindered,
lingering in sorrow and bitterness.
*Xian to Yu.*

**Ge**

Sending Yan to build a house,
the body finds no shelter.

**Household**

With no one to rely on at home,
I weave my own clothes.

**Ding**

Struck by arrows and sling stones,
Duke Xiang suffers from dysentery.
Wuzi at the nest gate,
wounded and sick, finds no cure.

**Zhen**

Sun and moon move in their course,
one cold, one hot.
Glory and favor blaze bright—
yet cannot be preserved.
Falling, crashing, tumbling down,
reduced to common rank.
*Zhongfu to Jin.*

**Gen**

The palace gate wails in sorrow,
ministers besiege their lord,
bound east and west.

**Jian**

Wearing a basin, gazing at the sky—
no stars are seen.
Fixating on the small, losing the great,
fortune flees beyond the wall.
*Fu to Meng, Xiaoguo to Gu.*

**Guimei**

What Heaven makes clear,
misfortune does not strike the household.
Turning against each other, they chase—
yet in the end, harmony and beauty.

**Feng**

Heaven darkens with ceaseless rain,
roads turn to mud and mire.
Merchants halt their trade,
the market holds nothing.
*Ge to Kui, Sheng to Sui, Fu to Daguo.*

**Lü**

The virtuous gate brings fortune and joy,
its blessings ever-growing.
Daily progress yields gain—
fitting for household and state.

**Dui**

On the southern slope of the mountain,
flowers and leaves rustle bright.
The noble and joyous lord,
brings radiance to the state.
*Ge to Dayou.*

**Huan**

Painting the dragon’s head and neck,
the pattern remains unfinished.
Sweet words and fair speech,
deceptive phrases without name.
*Sheng to Meng, Meng to Shihe, Jiaren to Bi.*

**Jie**

Infant and child,
without knowledge.
That boy sprouts horns—
disrupting my governance.
*Zhongfu.*

**Xiaoguo**

Yin works great treachery,
urging the lord to silence.
The swan goose’s sharp tongue
unleashes calamity and chaos.
Jing Ji bears sorrow,
Zhang Bo suffers disaster.

**Xiaoguo**

Virtue flows and spreads,
benefiting the four directions.
The Rain Master washes the roads,
the Wind Earl drives away misfortune.
Patrolling and sealing the sacred peaks,
to announce success.
*Cui to Bi, Yi to Fu.*

**Jiji**

Yu prepares to be lord,
entering Kunlun’s halls.
Gradually advancing into sunlight,
ascending to the warm springs—
his merit and power shine bright.

**Weiji**

The Five Peaks and Four Rivers,
holding moisture as virtue.
Acting without losing principle,
the people rely on grace and fortune.
*Heng to Jing, Yi to Mingyi, Li to Da.*

Variants and Emendations:

#34 *Xuankē* (絢轲) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *gōugōu* (枸枸).
#35 *Disaster* (灾) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *míng* (螟); *míng* is preferred.
#36 Originally *roasted* (炙) — emended to *disaster* (灾) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#37 Originally *overcome* (克) — emended to *fill* (充) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#38 Originally *lún* (仑) — unchanged in *Baizi Quanshu*.
#39 *Open* (开) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *same* (同).
#40 *Observe* (观) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *joy* (欢).

#286 Originally *split* (拆) — emended to *watchman’s rattle* (柝) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#287 Originally *rank* (侪) — emended to *prepare* (备) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#288 Originally *follow* (从) — emended to *cause* (使) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#289 Originally omitted *one* (一) after the note *side make* (边造) — supplied following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#290 Originally *belt* (带) — emended to *await* (待) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#291 Originally *weak* (弱) — emended to *mutual* (相) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#292 *Longevity* (寿) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *multitude* (众).
#293 Originally *person* (人) — emended to *long* (久) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#294 Originally *tear* (扯) — emended to *male* (牡) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#295 *Note note* (笺笺) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *ginger water chestnut* (姜菱).
#296 *Empty* (空) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *proclaim* (宣).

#297 Originally *dwell* (处) — emended to *transform* (变) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#298 Originally *child* (子) — emended to *character* (字) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#299 *Covering gaze* (覆赡) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *treading gaze* (履瞻).
#300 *Baizi Quanshu* adds a note under *virtue* (德): *treading gaze* (履瞻) for *covering gaze* (覆瞻).
#301 Originally *combine six* (并六) — emended to *Jin the Great* (晋大) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#302 Originally *go* (往) — emended to *mad* (狂) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#303 Originally *lack* (缺) — emended to *center* (央) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#304 *Know I enter the gate* (知我入门) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *profit enters my gate* (利入我门).
#305 *Flee* (逃) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *wander* (游).
#306 *Flee, one version reads welcome* (逃一作迎) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *wander, one version reads welcome* (游一作迎).
#307 Originally *make* (作) — emended to *ah left* (啊左) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#308 Originally *dragon* (龙) — emended to *shield* (庇) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#309 Originally *minister* (卿) — emended to *village* (乡) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#310 Originally *at the hook* (在钧) — emended to *think of restraint* (思约) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#311 *Fear evil* (畏恶) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *fearsome* (可畏).
#312 Originally *lack* (缺) — emended to *center* (央) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#313 *Repeatedly* (参参) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *reverently* (恭恭).
#314 *Sun* (日) — *Baizi Quanshu* also reads *sun* (日).
#315 *Disturb* (扰) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *grieve* (忧).
#316 Originally *household* (家) — emended to *obscured* (蒙) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
Note: *Bright Obscurity, Wind, Obscured* (明夷、巽、蒙) refers to *Bright Obscurity’s Wind* and *Bright Obscurity’s Obscured*.
#317 Originally *slow* (徐) — emended to *remove* (除) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#318 *Land* (陆) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *road* (涂).
#319 Originally *marsh* (泽) — emended to *deep* (深) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#320 *Ascend* (登) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *sit* (坐).
#321 *None* (莫) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *dusk* (暮).
#322 *Ignorant* (昧) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *hear* (闻).
#323 *Vast* (廓) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *corridor* (廊).
#324 Originally *blame* (责) — emended to *wealth* (赀) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#325 Originally *should* (当) — emended to *constant* (常) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#326 Originally *lack* (缺) — emended to *center* (央) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#327 Originally *leisure* (闲) — emended to *close* (闭) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#328 *Retreat* (遁) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *master* (主).
#329 Originally *bright* (明) — emended to *distress* (困) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#330 *Great* (大) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *dog* (犬).
#331 Originally *bright* (明) — emended to *earth* (坤) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#332 *Pheasant* (雉) — *Baizi Quanshu* reads *chicken* (鸡).
#333 Originally *cauldron* (鼎) — emended to *thunder* (震) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#334 Originally omitted *one* (一) under *nourishment* (颐) — supplied following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#335 Originally *special* (特) — emended to *rely* (恃) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
In the *Divergence* (睽) hexagram’s forest of verses, *practice* (肄) originally read *indulge* (肆) — emended following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#336 Originally *conquer* (伐) — emended to *lack* (乏) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#337 Originally *swallow* (燕) — emended to *barbarian* (夷) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#338 Originally *see* (见) — emended to *overcome* (克) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#339 Originally *lord* (君) — emended to *dwell* (居) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#340 Originally *lack* (缺) — emended to *center* (央) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#341 Originally *strength* (力) — emended to *merit* (功) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#342 Originally *respect* (敬) — emended to *startle* (惊) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#343 Originally *well* (井) — emended to *ascend* (升) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#344 Originally *Zhou* (周) — emended to *tread* (履) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#345 Originally *sprout* (苗) — emended to *remain* (留) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#346 Originally *finish* (了) — emended to *child* (子) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#347 Originally *gate* (门) — emended to *follow* (随) following *Baizi Quanshu*.

#348 Originally *lack* (缺) — emended to *now* (夫) following *Baizi Quanshu*.
#349 Originally *north* (北) — emended to *compare* (比).

*Yilin*, Scroll 5, Part 2: Hexagram Fifty-Eight (兑 *Dui*)

**Dui (兑)**
The piebald horses return with the army,
To rest their toil and weariness.
The conscripted men rejoice,
Entering their doors to see their wives.

*Guan* changing to *Jiji*, *Bi* changing to *Gu*, *Bo* changing to *Fu*.

**Qian (乾)**
Treading perilous difficulties,
They escape from danger and calamity.
Entering the gate of fortune and blessing,
They behold the great lord’s instruction.

*Zhen* changing to *Jiaren*, *Feng* changing to *Zhongfu*.

**Kun (坤)**
The disciple binds the qilin,
As spring and autumn compose the *Yin*.
The primal sage nears his end,
And Confucius grieves in his heart.

*Song* changing to *Tongren*, *Yu* changing to *Dayou*, *Ge* changing to *Zhen*.

**Zhun (屯)**
Marriage by the river’s edge,
The appointed time arrives, yet no boat comes.
The heart wavers in lost hope,
And the beloved is not seen.

*Zhun* changing to *Xiaoxu*.

**Meng (蒙)**
The heavenly grandson, the emperor’s child,
Dwells with the sun and moon.
Radiant glory in the world,
With blessings and fortune abundant.

*Xie* changing to *Lin*.

**Xu (需)**
Three years contending for a wife,
They chase and race in pursuit.
All day without food,
Essence and qi wearied and spent.
*Qian* changing to *Daxu*, *Kan* changing to *Jiaren*.

**Song (讼)**
Yu summons the lords,
At Kuaiji’s southern mountain.
Jade from ten thousand states,
The world at peace and tranquility.
*Shen* changing to *Lin*, *Ding* changing to *Gen* changing to *Lü*.

**Shi (师)**
Early frost and late snow,
Harvesting grain and wheat.
Labor lost and strength abandoned,
Hunger with nothing to eat.
*Bi* changing to *Yun*, *Feng* changing to *Li*, *Xu* changing to *Xian*.

**Bi (比)**
Songrong wields the halberd,
Dubo shoulders the crossbow.
Descending to observe the lower states,
They punish and expel the lawless.
In the waning days of Yin’s commerce,
Losing fortune, they flee in retreat.

**Xiaoxu (小畜)**
Born with sagely virtue,
Matching above with the Great Ultimate.
The august spirit establishes the center,
Bestowing upon me with fortune.
*Jiaren* changing to *Xu*, *Guimei* changing to *Xu*.

**Lǚ (履)**
Low fields and dry millet,
Ten thousand sprouts rise in teeth.
Great rains gather in torrents,
Waves sicken and rot.
*Tai* changing—

**Tai (泰)**
The master fears in Kuang,
Beset by hardship in Chen and Cai.
Yet bright virtue is not imperiled,
And in the end, harm is averted.
*Huan* changing to *Kan*, *Daguo* changing to *Jin*.

**Pi (否)**
Two red-headed ones,
Roaming the Five Peaks.
Lascivious words bring no protection,
They flee into your grove.
Bowing low, they heed the command,
Daring not stir or sway.

**Tongren (同人)**
One ought to know oneself,
And not encounter misfortune.
The declining will rise again,
And in the end, fortune will come.

**Dayou (大有)**
Rotten roots and withered trees,
Blossoms and leaves fallen away.
Suddenly meeting a host of flames,
Humbled, they topple with the wind.
*Zhun* changing to *Kan*, *Shike* changing to *Pi*, *Gen* changing to *Xu*, *Guai* changing to *Dan*.

**Ge (葛)**
Creeping vines spread and entwine,
Sparse yet fulfilling the wish.
The household’s way is sincere and deep,
Father and elder brothers rejoice.

**Shi (束)**
Seeking jade on the road,
Returning with worthless stone.
Named "Without Integrity,"
Called "Ugly and Vile,"
Despised by all.

**Zhan (瞻)**
Drawing the white bowstring,
The crossbow weak and timid.

**Ren (任)**
Carrying a blade at one’s side,
Like a dragonfly spying a magpie—
Eyes cast down, bowels seething with rage,
Daring not resist or strike.

**Gu (蠱)**
Wounds and sores, manifold sickness;
The Duke of Song, perilous and frail.
Wu’s son at the gate of his nest,
Without fate, he loses his place.

**Lin (臨)**
The eastern mountains and the western peaks,
Gathering to feast as one.
Following Wu’s escort,
To forge grace and fortune.

**Guan (觀)**
Dancing where it does not belong,
Losing rhythm, filled with regret,
Not suiting my intent.

**Shike (噬嗑)**
Southward along the Ru River,
Felling trees, lopping branches.
Missing the time, no encounter—
Rage like the hunger of Zhou.

**Bi (賁)**
Gongsun driving a black steed,
Journeying east to Qi.
Yanling offers his estate,
Bequeathing Ji a robe of many hues.
*Gen* changing to *Weiji*.

**Bo (剝)**
A chariot of eight hundred,
Illuminating civil virtue.
At Jiantu and Kuiqiu,
Qi and Lu receive fortune.
*Xun* changing to *Dazhuang*.

**Fu (復)**
The male dwells by weak waters,
The female by the sea’s edge.
Parting to feed,
Heart filled with sorrow.

**Wu Wang (無妄)**
Weaving nets to catch fish,
Receiving fortune, sitting in peace—
In the end, no calamity.

**Da Xu (大畜)**
Autumn south, spring north,
Resting in season.
Abiding in harmony, treading the center,
No fear of misfortune.

**Yi (頤)**
Opening doors and gates,
Patrolling to release grievances.
From the Xia Terrace and Youli,
Tang and Wen rejoice.

**Da Guo (大過)**
Left tally and right contract,
Joining in accord.
Heaven and Earth’s fruitful constancy—
A womb bears six sons.
Grown and accomplished,
Their words like a mother’s.
*Zhongfu* changing to *Kun*.

**Kan (坎)**
Hungry and hasty in building,
Silk threads tangled in disorder,
The end unattainable.

**Li (離)**
Eastern walls, lingering light,
Flickering, not darkening.
The mistress, jealous and grasping,
Disrupts my affairs.
*Ge* changing to *Qian*, *Dazhuang* changing to *Heng*, *Qian* changing to *Zhun*.

**Xian (咸)**
White cogon grass, salted wine,
The spirit-medium bows in prayer.
The gods relish food and drink,
Granting the lord long life.

**Heng (恒)**
Fan Li and Tao Zhu,
Shrewd in trade, amassing wealth.
East to Yingqiu,
Exchanging names with Zipi.
Bearing pearls and laden with gold,
Returning with abundant profit.

**Zhu (逐)**
Three segments, five omens,
Following one another.
Lost in the empty marsh,
Passing through the tiger’s den.
North along the valley’s course,
Traversing the six-hued steeds.
Wounded by bandits,
Dying in the jaws and belly.

**Da Zhuang (大壮)**
A male pheasant stretches its neck,
Desiring to fly into the pass.
The Rain Master sprinkles the road,
Drenching my robe and furs.
The cart, heavy, cannot advance;
The attendants bow their heads.

**Jin (晉)**
In middle age, veiled blessings;
This year, receiving fortune.
There must be gain,
Honor and emolument bestowed.

**Ming Yi (明夷)**
Emolument like the Duke of Zhou,
Establishing the state east of Luo—
Father and son both enfeoffed.
*Ge* changing to *Mingyi*.

**Jia Ren (家人)**
A sturdy bed, thick mat,
No long abiding.
Forsaking my fine tower,
Beset in the eastern land.
The anxiety of casting aside the shuttle—
Yet no disaster comes.
*Jiaren* changing to *Kui*, *Gen* changing to *Jie*.

**Kui (睽)**
Storing abundance in surplus,
Not dwelling in filth,
Profit in what is gained.

**Jian (蹇)**
The heart’s desire fulfilled,
Now meeting its time.
I gain fortune and blessing,
Not parted from war and arms.
*Jiji* changing to *Fu*.

**Xie (解)**
Eyes cannot close,
Anxiety scratching at the feet.
Restless fear and dread,
Departing from one’s state and clan.
*Cui* changing to *Kui*.

**Sun (損)**
A man of fortune and virtue,
Joyful and pleased each day.
Yi Wu aids Huan,
Three returns to serve—
His reward flows to his descendants.

**Yi (益)**
Xia Ji whispers in the ear,
Heart listening with delight,
Profit in taking counsel.
*Guai* changing to *Xian*.

**Guai (夬)**
Uncle welcomes his brothers,
Meeting in the lane under the sun.
The lord’s son and Ji,
Sitting together, striking the zither.
*Xian* changing to *Zhen*.

**Shen (娠)**
Moving the nest from home,
Southward encountering a white crow.
East and west receiving fortune,
Harmonizing with joy.

**Cui (萃)**
Shun ascends to Great Yu,
In the wilds of Shiyi.
Marching to the royal court,
To govern the waters and lands.
*Qian* changing to *Zhongfu*, *Shi* changing to *Xiaoxu*.

**Sheng (升)**
The Yangtze, the Yellow River, the Huai, the sea—
Heaven’s marketplaces.
Merchants receive fortune,
The state grows rich.

**Kun (困)**
Fretful and vexed,
Fire scorching the mountain’s roots.
It does not moisten my neighbor,
Alone I do not receive grace.
*Bi* changing to *Jian*.

**Jing (井)**
Dim and obscure,
Ears deaf, not keen.
Sinking into the deep abyss,
Drowning—misfortune and grief.
*Xun* changing to *Xiaoxu*.

**Ge (革)**
Crows cawing in clamor,
Heaven’s fire about to descend.
It burns my halls and chambers,
Disaster reaching the queen.
Same as *Zhongfu*.

**Ding (鼎)**
A hundred chicks with ten pheasants,
Ever with their mother.
Holding a chicken to grapple a tiger—
Who dares challenge them?

**Zhen (震)**
Building the city of Luoyi,
Crafted by the Duke of Zhou.
Thirty generations established,
Eight hundred years endured.
Fortune and blessing entwined,
Firm and unyielding.
*Jing* changing to *Sheng*.

**Gen (艮)**
Three walk together,
Parting to take their meal.
One body with five hearts,
Tossed in confusion.

**Jian (漸)**
Three tigers grappling a wolf,
Strength unequal.
Like a hawk seizing a pheasant,
One strike—destruction.

**Guimei (归妹)**
Raising tigers, keeping wolves,
Yet harming oneself.
As the years grow long,
The ailing lord prays—
Though perilous, not ill-fated.

**Feng (丰)**
Missing the timely moment,
Desires unfulfilled.

**Lǚ (旅)**
A bundle of pheasants and hares,
The wilds their arena.
Spotting the hawk, they flee—
Death at the valley’s mouth.

**Xun (巽)**
Autumn serpents toward their dens,
Not losing their rhythm.
Lady Jiang,
From Qi returns home.

**Huan (涣)**
A crow caws at the nest’s edge,
One call—three tremors.
Shaken east and west,
A restless, imperiled soul.

**Jie (节)**
Life cut short, unfulfilled,
Death brings many hauntings.
Wife and children weep in darkness,
Early they lose their pillar.
*Chongfu* changing to *Jiji*.

**Zhongfu (中孚)**
A thatched hut woven with mats,
Exalting my cultured virtue.
The three luminaries on banners,
The household receives its blessing.

**Xiaoguo (小过)**
Nets cast on four sides,
Not a bird takes flight.
Expeditions exhausted,
Hunger and hardship—no sustenance.

**Jiji (既济)**
Heaven completes, earth settles,
Piled stones form a mountain.
